001package squidpony.squidmath;
002
003import squidpony.ArrayTools;
004import squidpony.StringKit;
005import squidpony.annotation.Beta;
006import squidpony.squidgrid.zone.MutableZone;
007import squidpony.squidgrid.zone.Zone;
008
009import java.io.Serializable;
010import java.util.*;
011
012/**
013 * Region encoding of on/off information about areas using bitsets; uncompressed (fatty), but fast (greased lightning).
014 * This can handle any size of 2D data, and is not strictly limited to 256x256 as CoordPacker is. It stores several long
015 * arrays and uses each bit in one of those numbers to represent a single point, though sometimes this does waste bits
016 * if the height of the area this encodes is not a multiple of 64 (if you store a 80x64 map, this uses 80 longs; if you
017 * store an 80x65 map, this uses 160 longs, 80 for the first 64 rows and 80 more to store the next row). It's much
018 * faster than CoordPacker at certain operations (anything that expands or retracts an area, including
019 * {@link #expand()}), {@link #retract()}), {@link #fringe()}), {@link #surface()}, and {@link #flood(GreasedRegion)},
020 * and slightly faster on others, like {@link #and(GreasedRegion)} (called intersectPacked() in CoordPacker) and
021 * {@link #or(GreasedRegion)} (called unionPacked() in CoordPacker).
022 * <br>
023 * Each GreasedRegion is mutable, and instance methods typically modify that instance and return it for chaining. There
024 * are exceptions, usually where multiple GreasedRegion values are returned and the instance is not modified.
025 * <br>
026 * Typical usage involves constructing a GreasedRegion from some input data, like a char[][] for a map or a double[][]
027 * from DijkstraMap, and modifying it spatially with expand(), retract(), flood(), etc. It's common to mix in data from
028 * other GreasedRegions with and() (which gets the intersection of two GreasedRegions and stores it in one), or() (which
029 * is like and() but for the union), xor() (like and() but for exclusive or, finding only cells that are on in exactly
030 * one of the two GreasedRegions), and andNot() (which can be considered the "subtract another region from me" method).
031 * There are 8-way (Chebyshev distance) variants on all of the spatial methods, and methods without "8way" in the name
032 * are either 4-way (Manhattan distance) or not affected by distance measurement. Once you have a GreasedRegion, you may
033 * want to:
034 * <ul>
035 *     <li>get a single random point from it (use {@link #singleRandom(IRNG)}),</li>
036 *     <li>get several random points from it with random sampling (use {@link #randomPortion(IRNG, int)}),</li>
037 *     <li>mutate the current GreasedRegion to keep random points from it with random sampling (use {@link #randomRegion(IRNG, int)}),</li>
038 *     <li>get random points that are likely to be separated (use {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int, long)} with
039 *     a random long for the last parameter, or {@link #quasiRandomSeparated(double)} if you don't want a random seed),</li>
040 *     <li>do what any of the above "separated" methods can do, but mutate the current GreasedRegion (use
041 *     {@link #mixedRandomRegion(double, int, long)} or {@link #quasiRandomRegion(double, int)}),</li>
042 *     <li>get all points from it (use {@link #asCoords()} to get a Coord array, or produce a 2D array of the contents
043 *     with {@link #decode()} or {@link #toChars(char, char)}),</li>
044 *     <li>use it to modify other 2D data, such as with {@link #mask(char[][], char)},
045 *     {@link #inverseMask(char[][], char)}, {@link #writeDoubles(double[][], double)}, or
046 *     {@link #writeIntsInto(int[][], int)}, along with variations on those.</li>
047 * </ul>
048 * <br>
049 * You may also want to produce some 2D data from one or more GreasedRegions, as with {@link #sum(GreasedRegion...)} or
050 * {@link #toChars()}. The most effective techniques regarding GreasedRegion involve multiple methods, like getting a
051 * few random points from an existing GreasedRegion representing floor tiles in a dungeon with
052 * {@link #randomRegion(IRNG, int)}, then finding a random expansion of those initial points with
053 * {@link #spill(GreasedRegion, int, IRNG)}, giving the original GreasedRegion of floor tiles as the first argument.
054 * This could be used to position puddles of water or toxic waste in a dungeon level, while still keeping the starting
055 * points and finished points within the boundaries of valid (floor) cells. If you wanted to place something like mold
056 * that can be on floors or on cells immediately adjacent to floors (like walls), you could call {@link #expand()} on
057 * the floor tiles before calling spill, allowing the spill to spread onto non-floor cells that are next to floors.
058 * <br>
059 * For efficiency, you can place one GreasedRegion into another (typically a temporary value that is no longer needed
060 * and can be recycled) using {@link #remake(GreasedRegion)}, or give the information that would normally be used to
061 * construct a fresh GreasedRegion to an existing one of the same dimensions with {@link #refill(boolean[][])} or any
062 * of the overloads of refill(). These re-methods don't do as much work as a constructor does if the width and height
063 * of their argument are identical to their current width and height, and don't create more garbage for the GC.
064 * <br>
065 * Created by Tommy Ettinger on 6/24/2016.
066 */
067@Beta
068public class GreasedRegion extends Zone.Skeleton implements Collection<Coord>, Serializable, MutableZone {
069    private static final long serialVersionUID = 0;
070    private static final SobolQRNG sobol = new SobolQRNG(2);
071
072    public long[] data;
073    public int height;
074    public int width;
075    private int ySections;
076    private long yEndMask;
077    private boolean tallied;
078    private int ct;
079    private int[] counts;
080
081    private void tally()
082    {
083        ct = 0;
084        for (int i = 0, tmp; i < counts.length; i++) {
085            tmp = Long.bitCount(data[i]);
086            counts[i] = tmp == 0 ? 0 : (ct += tmp);
087        }
088        tallied = true;
089    }
090
091    /**
092     * Constructs an empty 64x64 GreasedRegion.
093     * GreasedRegions are mutable, so you can add to this with insert() or insertSeveral(), among others.
094     */
095    public GreasedRegion()
096    {
097        width = 64;
098        height = 64;
099        ySections = 1;
100        yEndMask = -1L;
101        data = new long[64];
102        counts = new int[64];
103        ct = 0;
104        tallied = true;
105    }
106
107    /**
108     * Constructs a GreasedRegion with the given rectangular boolean array, with width of bits.length and height of
109     * bits[0].length, any value of true considered "on", and any value of false considered "off."
110     * @param bits a rectangular 2D boolean array where true is on and false is off
111     */
112    public GreasedRegion(final boolean[][] bits)
113    {
114        width = bits.length;
115        height = bits[0].length;
116        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
117        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
118        data = new long[width * ySections];
119        for (int x = 0, xs = 0; x < width; x++, xs += ySections) {
120            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
121                if(bits[x][y]) data[xs + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
122            }
123        }
124        counts = new int[width * ySections];
125        tallied = false;
126    }
127    /**
128     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular boolean array, reusing the current data storage (without
129     * extra allocations) if this.width == map.length and this.height == map[0].length. The current values stored in
130     * this are always cleared, then any value of true in map is considered "on", and any value of false in map is
131     * considered "off."
132     * @param map a rectangular 2D boolean array where true is on and false is off
133     * @return this for chaining
134     */
135    public GreasedRegion refill(final boolean[][] map) {
136        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length && height == map[0].length) {
137            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
138            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
139                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
140                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= (map[x][y] ? 1L : 0L) << (y & 63);
141                }
142            }
143            tallied = false;
144            return this;
145        } else {
146            width = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length;
147            height = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length;
148            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
149            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
150            data = new long[width * ySections];
151            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
152                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
153                    if(map[x][y]) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
154                }
155            }
156            counts = new int[width * ySections];
157            tallied = false;
158            return this;
159        }
160    }
161
162    /**
163     * Constructs a GreasedRegion with the given rectangular char array, with width of map.length and height of
164     * map[0].length, any value that equals yes is considered "on", and any other value considered "off."
165     * @param map a rectangular 2D char array where yes is on and everything else is off
166     * @param yes which char to encode as "on"
167     */
168    public GreasedRegion(final char[][] map, final char yes)
169    {
170        width = map.length;
171        height = map[0].length;
172        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
173        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
174        data = new long[width * ySections];
175        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
176            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
177                if(map[x][y] == yes) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
178            }
179        }
180        counts = new int[width * ySections];
181        tallied = false;
182    }
183    /**
184     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular char array, reusing the current data storage (without
185     * extra allocations) if this.width == map.length and this.height == map[0].length. The current values stored in
186     * this are always cleared, then any value that equals yes is considered "on", and any other value considered "off."
187     * @param map a rectangular 2D char array where yes is on and everything else is off
188     * @param yes which char to encode as "on"
189     * @return this for chaining
190     */
191    public GreasedRegion refill(final char[][] map, final char yes) {
192        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length && height == map[0].length) {
193            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
194            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
195                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
196                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= ((map[x][y] == yes) ? 1L : 0L) << (y & 63);
197                }
198            }
199            tallied = false;
200            return this;
201        } else {
202            width = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length;
203            height = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length;
204            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
205            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
206            data = new long[width * ySections];
207            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
208                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
209                    if(map[x][y] == yes) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
210                }
211            }
212            counts = new int[width * ySections];
213            tallied = false;
214            return this;
215        }
216    }

218    /**
219     * Weird constructor that takes a String array, _as it would be printed_, so each String is a row and indexing would
220     * be done with y, x instead of the normal x, y.
221     * @param map String array (as printed, not the normal storage) where each String is a row
222     * @param yes the char to consider "on" in the GreasedRegion
223     */
224    public GreasedRegion(final String[] map, final char yes)
225    {
226        height = map.length;
227        width = map[0].length();
228        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
229        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
230        data = new long[width * ySections];
231        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
232            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
233                if(map[y].charAt(x) == yes) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
234            }
235        }
236        counts = new int[width * ySections];
237        tallied = false;
238    }
239
240    /**
241     * Weird refill method that takes a String array, _as it would be printed_, so each String is a row and indexing
242     * would be done with y, x instead of the normal x, y.
243     * @param map String array (as printed, not the normal storage) where each String is a row
244     * @param yes the char to consider "on" in the GreasedRegion
245     * @return this for chaining
246     */
247    public GreasedRegion refill(final String[] map, final char yes) {
248        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && height == map.length && width == map[0].length()) {
249            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
250            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
251                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
252                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= ((map[y].charAt(x) == yes) ? 1L : 0L) << (y & 63);
253                }
254            }
255            tallied = false;
256            return this;
257        } else {
258            height = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length;
259            width = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length();
260            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
261            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
262            data = new long[width * ySections];
263            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
264                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
265                    if(map[y].charAt(y) == yes) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
266                }
267            }
268            counts = new int[width * ySections];
269            tallied = false;
270            return this;
271        }
272    }
273    /**
274     * Constructs a GreasedRegion with the given rectangular int array, with width of map.length and height of
275     * map[0].length, any value that equals yes is considered "on", and any other value considered "off."
276     * @param map a rectangular 2D int array where an int == yes is on and everything else is off
277     * @param yes which int to encode as "on"
278     */
279    public GreasedRegion(final int[][] map, final int yes)
280    {
281        width = map.length;
282        height = map[0].length;
283        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
284        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
285        data = new long[width * ySections];
286        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
287            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
288                if(map[x][y] == yes) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
289            }
290        }
291        counts = new int[width * ySections];
292        tallied = false;
293    }

295     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular int array, reusing the current data storage (without

299     * @param yes which int to encode as "on"
300     * @return this for chaining
301     */
302    public GreasedRegion refill(final int[][] map, final int yes) {
303        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length && height == map[0].length) {
304            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
305            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {

308                }

328
329    /**
330     * Constructs this GreasedRegion using an int[][], treating cells as on if they are greater than or equal to lower
331     * and less than upper, or off otherwise.
332     * @param map an int[][] that should have some ints between lower and upper
333     * @param lower lower bound, inclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are at least equal to lower
334     * @param upper upper bound, exclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are less than upper
335     */
336    public GreasedRegion(final int[][] map, final int lower, final int upper)
337    {
338        width = map.length;
339        height = map[0].length;
340        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
341        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
342        data = new long[width * ySections];
343        int[] column;
344        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
345            column = map[x];
346            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
347                if(column[y] >= lower && column[y] < upper) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
348            }
349        }
350        counts = new int[width * ySections];
351        tallied = false;
352    }
353
354    /**
355     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular int array, reusing the current data storage (without
356     * extra allocations) if this.width == map.length and this.height == map[0].length. The current values stored in
357     * this are always cleared, then cells are treated as on if they are greater than or equal to lower and less than
358     * upper, or off otherwise.
359     * @param map a rectangular 2D int array that should have some values between lower and upper
360     * @param lower lower bound, inclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are at least equal to lower
361     * @param upper upper bound, exclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are less than upper
362     * @return this for chaining
363     */
364    public GreasedRegion refill(final int[][] map, final int lower, final int upper) {
365        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length && height == map[0].length) {
366            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
367            int[] column;
368            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
369                column = map[x];
370                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
371                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= ((column[y] >= lower && column[y] < upper) ? 1L : 0L) << (y & 63);
372                }
373            }
374            tallied = false;
375            return this;
376        } else {
377            width = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length;
378            height = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length;
379            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
380            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
381            data = new long[width * ySections];
382            int[] column;
383            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
384                column = map[x];
385                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
386                    if(column[y] >= lower && column[y] < upper) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
387                }
388            }
389            counts = new int[width * ySections];
390            tallied = false;
391            return this;
392        }
393    }

401     */

420    /**
421     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular short array, reusing the current data storage (without
422     * extra allocations) if this.width == map.length and this.height == map[0].length. The current values stored in
423     * this are always cleared, then cells are treated as on if they are greater than or equal to lower and less than
424     * upper, or off otherwise.
425     * @param map a rectangular 2D short array that should have some values between lower and upper
426     * @param lower lower bound, inclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are at least equal to lower
427     * @param upper upper bound, exclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are less than upper
428     * @return this for chaining
429     */
430    public GreasedRegion refill(final short[][] map, final int lower, final int upper) {
431        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length && height == map[0].length) {
432            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
433            short[] column;
434            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
435                column = map[x];
436                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
437                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= ((column[y] >= lower && column[y] < upper) ? 1L : 0L) << (y & 63);
438                }
439            }
440            tallied = false;
441            return this;
442        } else {
443            width = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length;
444            height = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length;
445            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
446            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
447            data = new long[width * ySections];
448            short[] column;
449            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
450                column = map[x];
451                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
452                    if(column[y] >= lower && column[y] < upper) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
453                }
454            }
455            counts = new int[width * ySections];
456            tallied = false;
457            return this;
458        }
459    }
460    /**
461     * Constructs this GreasedRegion using a double[][] (typically one generated by
462     * {@link squidpony.squidai.DijkstraMap}) that only stores two relevant states:  an "on" state for values less than
463     * or equal to upperBound (inclusive), and an "off" state for anything else.
464     * @param map a double[][] that probably relates in some way to DijkstraMap.
465     * @param upperBound upper inclusive; any double greater than this will be off, any others will be on
466     */
467    public GreasedRegion(final double[][] map, final double upperBound)
468    {
469        width = map.length;
470        height = map[0].length;
471        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
472        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
473        data = new long[width * ySections];
474        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
475            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
476                if(map[x][y] <= upperBound)
477                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
478            }
479        }
480        counts = new int[width * ySections];
481        tallied = false;
482    }
483    /**
484     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular double array, reusing the current data storage (without
485     * extra allocations) if this.width == map.length and this.height == map[0].length. The current values stored in
486     * this are always cleared, then cells are treated as on if they are less than or equal to upperBound, or off
487     * otherwise.
488     * @param map a rectangular 2D double array that should usually have some values less than or equal to upperBound
489     * @param upperBound upper bound, inclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are less than or equal to this
490     * @return this for chaining
491     */
492    public GreasedRegion refill(final double[][] map, final double upperBound) {
493        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length && height == map[0].length) {
494            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
495            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
496                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
497                    if(map[x][y] <= upperBound) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
498                }
499            }
500            tallied = false;
501            return this;
502        } else {
503            width = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length;
504            height = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length;
505            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
506            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
507            data = new long[width * ySections];
508            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
509                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
510                    if(map[x][y] <= upperBound) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
511                }
512            }
513            counts = new int[width * ySections];
514            tallied = false;
515            return this;
516        }
517    }
518
519    /**
520     * Constructs this GreasedRegion using a double[][] (typically one generated by
521     * {@link squidpony.squidai.DijkstraMap}) that only stores two relevant states:  an "on" state for values between
522     * lowerBound (inclusive) and upperBound (exclusive), and an "off" state for anything else.
523     * @param map a double[][] that probably relates in some way to DijkstraMap.
524     * @param lowerBound lower inclusive; any double lower than this will be off, any equal to or greater than this,
525     *                   but less than upper, will be on
526     * @param upperBound upper exclusive; any double greater than or equal to this this will be off, any doubles both
527     *                   less than this and equal to or greater than lower will be on
528     */
529    public GreasedRegion(final double[][] map, final double lowerBound, final double upperBound)
530    {
531        width = map.length;
532        height = map[0].length;
533        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
534        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
535        data = new long[width * ySections];
536        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
537            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
538                if(map[x][y] >= lowerBound && map[x][y] < upperBound)
539                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
540            }
541        }
542        counts = new int[width * ySections];
543        tallied = false;
544    }
545    /**
546     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular double array, reusing the current data storage (without
547     * extra allocations) if this.width == map.length and this.height == map[0].length. The current values stored in
548     * this are always cleared, then cells are treated as on if they are greater than or equal to lower and less than
549     * upper, or off otherwise.
550     * @param map a rectangular 2D double array that should have some values between lower and upper
551     * @param lower lower bound, inclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are at least equal to lower
552     * @param upper upper bound, exclusive; all on cells will have values in map that are less than upper
553     * @return this for chaining
554     */
555    public GreasedRegion refill(final double[][] map, final double lower, final double upper) {
556        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length && height == map[0].length) {
557            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
558            double[] column;
559            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
560                column = map[x];
561                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
562                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= ((column[y] >= lower && column[y] < upper) ? 1L : 0L) << (y & 63);
563                }
564            }
565            tallied = false;
566            return this;
567        } else {
568            width = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length;
569            height = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length;
570            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
571            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
572            data = new long[width * ySections];
573            double[] column;
574            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
575                column = map[x];
576                for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
577                    if(column[y] >= lower && column[y] < upper) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
578                }
579            }
580            counts = new int[width * ySections];
581            tallied = false;
582            return this;
583        }
584    }
585
586    /**
587     * Constructs this GreasedRegion using a double[][] (this was made for use inside
588     * {@link squidpony.squidgrid.BevelFOV}) that only stores two relevant states:  an "on" state for values between
589     * lowerBound (inclusive) and upperBound (exclusive), and an "off" state for anything else. This variant scales the
590     * input so each "on" position in map produces a 2x2 on area if scale is 2, a 3x3 area if scale is 3, and so on.
591     * @param map a double[][] that may relate in some way to BevelFOV
592     * @param lowerBound lower inclusive; any double lower than this will be off, any equal to or greater than this,
593     *                   but less than upper, will be on
594     * @param upperBound upper exclusive; any double greater than or equal to this this will be off, any doubles both
595     *                   less than this and equal to or greater than lower will be on
596     * @param scale      the size of the square of cells in this that each "on" value in map will correspond to
597     */
598    public GreasedRegion(final double[][] map, final double lowerBound, final double upperBound, int scale)
599    {
600        scale = Math.min(63, Math.max(1, scale));
601        int baseWidth = map.length, baseHeight = map[0].length;
602        width =  baseWidth * scale;
603        height = baseHeight * scale;
604        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
605        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
606        data = new long[width * ySections];
607        long shape = (1L << scale) - 1L, leftover;
608        for (int bx = 0, x = 0; bx < baseWidth; bx++, x += scale) {
609            for (int by = 0, y = 0; by < baseHeight; by++, y += scale) {
610                if(map[bx][by] >= lowerBound && map[bx][by] < upperBound) {
611                    for (int i = 0; i < scale; i++) {
612                        data[(x + i) * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= shape << (y & 63);
613                        if((leftover = (y + scale - 1 & 63) + 1) < (y & 63) + 1 && (y + leftover >> 6) < ySections)
614                        {
615                            data[(x + i) * ySections + (y >> 6) + 1] |= (1L << leftover) - 1L;
616                        }
617                    }
618                }
619            }
620        }
621        counts = new int[width * ySections];
622        tallied = false;
623    }
624    /**
625     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given rectangular double array, reusing the current data storage (without
626     * extra allocations) if {@code this.width == map.length * scale && this.height == map[0].length * scale}. The
627     * current values stored in this are always cleared, then cells are treated as on if they are greater than or equal
628     * to lower and less than upper, or off otherwise, before considering scaling. This variant scales the input so each
629     * "on" position in map produces a 2x2 on area if scale is 2, a 3x3 area if scale is 3, and so on.
630     * @param map a double[][] that may relate in some way to BevelFOV
631     * @param lowerBound lower inclusive; any double lower than this will be off, any equal to or greater than this,
632     *                   but less than upper, will be on
633     * @param upperBound upper exclusive; any double greater than or equal to this this will be off, any doubles both
634     *                   less than this and equal to or greater than lower will be on
635     * @param scale      the size of the square of cells in this that each "on" value in map will correspond to
636     * @return this for chaining
637     */
638    public GreasedRegion refill(final double[][] map, final double lowerBound, final double upperBound, int scale) {
639        scale = Math.min(63, Math.max(1, scale));
640        if (map != null && map.length > 0 && width == map.length * scale && height == map[0].length * scale) {
641            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
642            double[] column;
643            int baseWidth = map.length, baseHeight = map[0].length;
644            long shape = (1L << scale) - 1L, leftover;
645            for (int bx = 0, x = 0; bx < baseWidth; bx++, x += scale) {
646                column = map[bx];
647                for (int by = 0, y = 0; by < baseHeight; by++, y += scale) {
648                    if(column[by] >= lowerBound && column[by] < upperBound) {
649                        for (int i = 0; i < scale; i++) {
650                            data[(x + i) * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= shape << (y & 63);
651                            if((leftover = (y + scale - 1 & 63) + 1) < (y & 63) + 1 && (y + leftover >> 6) < ySections)
652                            {
653                                data[(x + i) * ySections + (y >> 6) + 1] |= (1L << leftover) - 1L;
654                            }
655                        }
656                    }
657                }
658            }
659            tallied = false;
660            return this;
661        } else {
662            int baseWidth = (map == null) ? 0 : map.length,
663                    baseHeight = (map == null || map.length <= 0) ? 0 : map[0].length;
664            width =  baseWidth * scale;
665            height = baseHeight * scale;
666            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
667            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
668            data = new long[width * ySections];
669            long shape = (1L << scale) - 1L, leftover;
670            for (int bx = 0, x = 0; bx < baseWidth; bx++, x += scale) {
671                for (int by = 0, y = 0; by < baseHeight; by++, y += scale) {
672                    if(map[bx][by] >= lowerBound && map[bx][by] < upperBound) {
673                        for (int i = 0; i < scale; i++) {
674                            data[(x + i) * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= shape << (y & 63);
675                            if((leftover = (y + scale - 1 & 63)) < y && y < height - leftover)
676                            {
677                                data[(x + i) * ySections + (y >> 6) + 1] |= (1L << leftover) - 1L;
678                            }
679                        }
680                    }
681                }
682            }
683            counts = new int[width * ySections];
684            tallied = false;
685            return this;
686        }
687    }
688
689    /**
690     * Constructs a GreasedRegion with the given 1D boolean array, with the given width and height, where an [x][y]
691     * position is obtained from bits given an index n with x = n / height, y = n % height, any value of true
692     * considered "on", and any value of false considered "off."
693     * @param bits a 1D boolean array where true is on and false is off
694     * @param width the width of the desired GreasedRegion; width * height should equal bits.length
695     * @param height the height of the desired GreasedRegion; width * height should equal bits.length
696     */
697    public GreasedRegion(final boolean[] bits, final int width, final int height)
698    {
699        this.width = width;
700        this.height = height;
701        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
702        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
703        data = new long[width * ySections];
704        for (int a = 0, x = 0, y = 0; a < bits.length; a++, x = a / height, y = a % height) {
705            if(bits[a]) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
706        }
707        counts = new int[width * ySections];
708        tallied = false;
709    }
710    /**
711     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion with the given 1D boolean array, reusing the current data storage (without
712     * extra allocations) if this.width == width and this.height == height, where an [x][y]
713     * position is obtained from bits given an index n with x = n / height, y = n % height, any value of true
714     * considered "on", and any value of false considered "off."
715     * @param bits a 1D boolean array where true is on and false is off
716     * @param width the width of the desired GreasedRegion; width * height should equal bits.length
717     * @param height the height of the desired GreasedRegion; width * height should equal bits.length
718     * @return this for chaining
719     */
720    public GreasedRegion refill(final boolean[] bits, final int width, final int height) {
721        if (bits != null && this.width == width && this.height == height) {
722            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
723            for (int a = 0, x = 0, y = 0; a < bits.length; a++, x = a / height, y = a % height) {
724                data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= (bits[a] ? 1L : 0L) << (y & 63);
725            }
726            tallied = false;
727            return this;
728        } else {
729            this.width = (bits == null || width < 0) ? 0 : width;
730            this.height = (bits == null || bits.length <= 0 || height < 0) ? 0 : height;
731            ySections = (this.height + 63) >> 6;
732            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (this.height & 63));
733            data = new long[this.width * ySections];
734            if(bits != null) {
735                for (int a = 0, x = 0, y = 0; a < bits.length; a++, x = a / this.height, y = a % this.height) {
736                    if (bits[a]) data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
737                }
738            }
739            counts = new int[width * ySections];
740            tallied = false;
741            return this;
742        }
743    }
744
745    /**
746     * Constructor for an empty GreasedRegion of the given width and height.
747     * GreasedRegions are mutable, so you can add to this with insert() or insertSeveral(), among others.
748     * @param width the maximum width for the GreasedRegion
749     * @param height the maximum height for the GreasedRegion
750     */
751    public GreasedRegion(final int width, final int height)
752    {
753        this.width = width;
754        this.height = height;
755        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
756        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
757        data = new long[width * ySections];
758        counts = new int[width  * ySections];
759        ct = 0;
760        tallied = true;
761    }
762
763    /**
764     * If this GreasedRegion has the same width and height passed as parameters, this acts the same as {@link #empty()},
765     * makes no allocations, and returns this GreasedRegion with its contents all "off"; otherwise, this does allocate
766     * a differently-sized amount of internal data to match the new width and height, sets the fields to all match the
767     * new width and height, and returns this GreasedRegion with its new width and height, with all contents "off". This
768     * is meant for cases where a GreasedRegion may be reused effectively, but its size may not always be the same.
769     * @param width the width to potentially resize this GreasedRegion to
770     * @param height the height to potentially resize this GreasedRegion to
771     * @return this GreasedRegion, always with all contents "off", and with the height and width set.
772     */
773    public GreasedRegion resizeAndEmpty(final int width, final int height) {
774        if (width == this.width && height == this.height) {
775            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
776            Arrays.fill(counts, 0);
777            ct = 0;
778            tallied = true;
779        } else {
780            this.width = (width <= 0) ? 0 : width;
781            this.height = (height <= 0) ? 0 : height;
782            ySections = (this.height + 63) >> 6;
783            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (this.height & 63));
784            data = new long[this.width * ySections];
785            counts = new int[this.width * ySections];
786            ct = 0;
787            tallied = true;
788        }
789        return this;
790
791    }
792
793    /**
794     * Constructor for a GreasedRegion that contains a single "on" cell, and has the given width and height.
795     * Note that to avoid confusion with the constructor that takes multiple Coord values, this takes the single "on"
796     * Coord first, while the multiple-Coord constructor takes its vararg or array of Coords last.
797     * @param single the one (x,y) point to store as "on" in this GreasedRegion
798     * @param width the maximum width for the GreasedRegion
799     * @param height the maximum height for the GreasedRegion
800     */
801    public GreasedRegion(final Coord single, final int width, final int height)
802    {
803        this.width = width;
804        this.height = height;
805        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
806        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
807        data = new long[width * ySections];
808        counts = new int[width * ySections];
809        if(single.x < width && single.y < height && single.x >= 0 && single.y >= 0)
810        {
811            data[ct = single.x * ySections + (single.y >> 6)] |= 1L << (single.y & 63);
812            counts[ct] = 1;
813            ct = 1;
814            tallied = true;
815        }
816        else
817        {
818            ct = 0;
819            tallied = true;
820        }
821    }
822
823    /**
824     * Constructor for a GreasedRegion that can have several "on" cells specified, and has the given width and height.
825     * Note that to avoid confusion with the constructor that takes one Coord value, this takes the vararg or array of
826     * Coords last, while the single-Coord constructor takes its one Coord first.
827     * @param width the maximum width for the GreasedRegion
828     * @param height the maximum height for the GreasedRegion
829     * @param points an array or vararg of Coord to store as "on" in this GreasedRegion
830     */
831    public GreasedRegion(final int width, final  int height, final Coord... points)
832    {
833        this.width = width;
834        this.height = height;
835        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
836        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
837        data = new long[width * ySections];
838        if(points != null)
839        {
840            for (int i = 0, x, y; i < points.length; i++) {
841                x = points[i].x;
842                y = points[i].y;
843                if(x < width && y < height && x >= 0 && y >= 0)
844                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
845            }
846        }
847        counts = new int[width * ySections];
848        tallied = false;
849    }
850
851    /**
852     * Constructor for a GreasedRegion that can have several "on" cells specified, and has the given width and height.
853     * Note that to avoid confusion with the constructor that takes one Coord value, this takes the Iterable of
854     * Coords last, while the single-Coord constructor takes its one Coord first.
855     * @param width the maximum width for the GreasedRegion
856     * @param height the maximum height for the GreasedRegion
857     * @param points an array or vararg of Coord to store as "on" in this GreasedRegion
858     */
859    public GreasedRegion(final int width, final int height, final Iterable<Coord> points)
860    {
861        this.width = width;
862        this.height = height;
863        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
864        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
865        data = new long[width * ySections];
866        if(points != null) {
867            int x, y;
868            for (Coord c : points) {
869                x = c.x;
870                y = c.y;
871                if (x < width && y < height && x >= 0 && y >= 0)
872                    data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
873            }
874        }
875        counts = new int[width * ySections];
876        tallied = false;
877
878    }
879
880    /**
881     * Constructor for a random GreasedRegion of the given width and height, typically assigning approximately half of
882     * the cells in this to "on" and the rest to off. A RandomnessSource can be slightly more efficient than an RNG when
883     * you're making a lot of calls on it.
884     * @param random a RandomnessSource that should have a good nextLong() method; LinnormRNG is excellent but Lathe32RNG is faster on GWT (only there) 
885     * @param width the maximum width for the GreasedRegion
886     * @param height the maximum height for the GreasedRegion
887     */
888    public GreasedRegion(final RandomnessSource random, final int width, final int height)
889    {
890        this.width = width;
891        this.height = height;
892        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
893        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
894        data = new long[width * ySections];
895        for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
896            data[i] = random.nextLong();
897        }
898        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
899            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
900                data[a] &= yEndMask;
901            }
902        }
903        counts = new int[width * ySections];
904        tallied = false;
905    }
906    /**
907     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion by filling it with random values from random, reusing the current data storage
908     * (without extra allocations) if this.width == width and this.height == height, and typically assigning
909     * approximately half of the cells in this to "on" and the rest to off. A RandomnessSource can be slightly more
910     * efficient than an RNG when you're making a lot of calls on it.
911     * @param random a RandomnessSource that should have a good nextLong() method; LinnormRNG is excellent but Lathe32RNG is faster on GWT (only there) 
912     * @param width the width of the desired GreasedRegion
913     * @param height the height of the desired GreasedRegion
914     * @return this for chaining
915     */
916    public GreasedRegion refill(final RandomnessSource random, final int width, final int height) {
917        if (random != null){
918            if(this.width == width && this.height == height) {
919                for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
920                    data[i] = random.nextLong();
921                }
922            } else {
923                this.width = (width <= 0) ? 0 : width;
924                this.height = (height <= 0) ? 0 : height;
925                ySections = (this.height + 63) >> 6;
926                yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (this.height & 63));
927                data = new long[this.width * ySections];
928                for (int i = 0; i < this.width * ySections; i++) {
929                    data[i] = random.nextLong();
930                }
931                counts = new int[this.width * ySections];
932            }
933            if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
934                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
935                    data[a] &= yEndMask;
936                }
937            }
938            tallied = false;
939        }
940        return this;
941    }
942
943    /**
944     * Constructor for a random GreasedRegion of the given width and height, typically assigning approximately half of
945     * the cells in this to "on" and the rest to off. A RandomnessSource can be slightly more efficient than an RNG when
946     * you're making a lot of calls on it, so you may prefer {@link #GreasedRegion(RandomnessSource, int, int)}.
947     * @param random an IRNG, such as an RNG, that this will use to generate its contents
948     * @param width the maximum width for the GreasedRegion
949     * @param height the maximum height for the GreasedRegion
950     */
951    public GreasedRegion(final IRNG random, final int width, final int height)
952    {
953        this.width = width;
954        this.height = height;
955        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
956        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
957        data = new long[width * ySections];
958        for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
959            data[i] = random.nextLong();
960        }
961        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
962            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
963                data[a] &= yEndMask;
964            }
965        }
966        counts = new int[width * ySections];
967        tallied = false;
968    }
969    /**
970     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion by filling it with random values from random, reusing the current data storage
971     * (without extra allocations) if this.width == width and this.height == height, and typically assigning
972     * approximately half of the cells in this to "on" and the rest to off.
973     * @param random an IRNG that should have a good nextLong() method; an RNG constructed with the default RandomnessSource will be fine
974     * @param width the width of the desired GreasedRegion
975     * @param height the height of the desired GreasedRegion
976     * @return this for chaining
977     */
978    public GreasedRegion refill(final IRNG random, final int width, final int height) {
979        if (random != null){
980            if(this.width == width && this.height == height) {
981                for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
982                    data[i] = random.nextLong();
983                }
984            } else {
985                this.width = (width <= 0) ? 0 : width;
986                this.height = (height <= 0) ? 0 : height;
987                ySections = (this.height + 63) >> 6;
988                yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (this.height & 63));
989                data = new long[this.width * ySections];
990                for (int i = 0; i < this.width * ySections; i++) {
991                    data[i] = random.nextLong();
992                }
993                counts = new int[width * ySections];
994            }
995            if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
996                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
997                    data[a] &= yEndMask;
998                }
999            }
1000            tallied = false;
1001        }
1002        return this;
1003    }
1004
1005    /**
1006     * Constructor for a random GreasedRegion of the given width and height, trying to set the given fraction of cells
1007     * to on. Depending on the value of fraction, this makes between 0 and 6 calls to the nextLong() method of random's
1008     * internal RandomnessSource, per 64 cells of this GreasedRegion (if height is not a multiple of 64, round up to get
1009     * the number of calls this makes). As such, this sacrifices the precision of the fraction to obtain significantly
1010     * better speed than generating one random number per cell, although the precision is probably good enough (fraction
1011     * is effectively rounded down to the nearest multiple of 0.015625, and clamped between 0.0 and 1.0). The parameter
1012     * {@code random} can be an object like a {@link LinnormRNG}, an {@link RNG} backed by a well-distributed
1013     * RandomnessSource like its default, LinnormRNG, a {@link GWTRNG} (especially if you target GWT, where it will
1014     * perform much better than most alternatives), or any of various other RandomnessSource implementations that
1015     * distribute bits well for {@link RandomnessSource#nextLong()}, but should not be intentionally-biased RNGs like
1016     * {@link DharmaRNG} or {@link EditRNG}, nor double-based QRNGs like {@link VanDerCorputQRNG} or {@link SobolQRNG}.
1017     * @param random a RandomnessSource that should produce high-quality long values, like the defaults for {@link RNG}
1018     * @param fraction between 0.0 and 1.0 (clamped), only considering a precision of 1/64.0 (0.015625) between steps
1019     * @param width the maximum width for the GreasedRegion
1020     * @param height the maximum height for the GreasedRegion
1021     */
1022    public GreasedRegion(final RandomnessSource random, final double fraction, final int width, final int height)
1023    {
1024        this.width = width;
1025        this.height = height;
1026        int bitCount = (int) (fraction * 64);
1027        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
1028        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
1029        data = new long[width * ySections];
1030        for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
1031            data[i] = approximateBits(random, bitCount);
1032        }
1033        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
1034            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1035                data[a] &= yEndMask;
1036            }
1037        }
1038        counts = new int[width * ySections];
1039        tallied = false;
1040    }
1041    /**
1042     * Reassigns this GreasedRegion randomly, reusing the current data storage (without extra allocations) if this.width
1043     * == width and this.height == height, while trying to set the given fraction of cells to on. Depending on the value
1044     * of fraction, this makes between 0 and 6 calls to the nextLong() method of random's internal RandomnessSource, per
1045     * 64 cells of this GreasedRegion (if height is not a multiple of 64, round up to get the number of calls this
1046     * makes). As such, this sacrifices the precision of the fraction to obtain significantly better speed than
1047     * generating one random number per cell, although the precision is probably good enough (fraction is effectively
1048     * rounded down to the nearest multiple of 0.015625, and clamped between 0.0 and 1.0). The parameter {@code random}
1049     * can be an object like a {@link LinnormRNG}, an {@link RNG} backed by a well-distributed RandomnessSource like its
1050     * default, LinnormRNG, a {@link GWTRNG} (especially if you target GWT, where it will perform much better than most
1051     * alternatives), or any of various other RandomnessSource implementations that distribute bits well for
1052     * {@link RandomnessSource#nextLong()}, but should not be intentionally-biased RNGs like {@link DharmaRNG} or
1053     * {@link EditRNG}, nor double-based QRNGs like {@link VanDerCorputQRNG} or {@link SobolQRNG}.
1054     * @param random a RandomnessSource that should produce high-quality long values, like the defaults for {@link RNG}
1055     * @param fraction between 0.0 and 1.0 (clamped), only considering a precision of 1/64.0 (0.015625) between steps
1056     * @param width the maximum width for the GreasedRegion
1057     * @param height the maximum height for the GreasedRegion
1058     * @return this for chaining
1059     */
1060    public GreasedRegion refill(final RandomnessSource random, final double fraction, final int width, final int height) {
1061        if (random != null){
1062            int bitCount = (int) (fraction * 64);
1063            if(this.width == width && this.height == height) {
1064                for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
1065                    data[i] = approximateBits(random, bitCount);
1066                }
1067            } else {
1068                this.width = (width <= 0) ? 0 : width;
1069                this.height = (height <= 0) ? 0 : height;
1070                ySections = (this.height + 63) >> 6;
1071                yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (this.height & 63));
1072                data = new long[this.width * ySections];
1073                for (int i = 0; i < this.width * ySections; i++) {
1074                    data[i] = approximateBits(random, bitCount);
1075                }
1076                counts = new int[width * ySections];
1077            }
1078            if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
1079                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1080                    data[a] &= yEndMask;
1081                }
1082            }
1083
1084        }
1085        return this;
1086    }
1087
1088    /**
1089     * Copy constructor that takes another GreasedRegion and copies all of its data into this new one.
1090     * If you find yourself frequently using this constructor and assigning it to the same variable, consider using the
1091     * {@link #remake(GreasedRegion)} method on the variable instead, which will, if it has the same width and height
1092     * as the other GreasedRegion, avoid creating garbage and quickly fill the variable with the other's contents.
1093     * @see #copy() for a convenience method that just uses this constructor
1094     * @param other another GreasedRegion that will be copied into this new GreasedRegion
1095     */
1096    public GreasedRegion(final GreasedRegion other)
1097    {
1098        width = other.width;
1099        height = other.height;
1100        ySections = other.ySections;
1101        yEndMask = other.yEndMask;
1102        data = new long[width * ySections];
1103        counts = new int[width * ySections];
1104        System.arraycopy(other.data, 0, data, 0, width * ySections);
1105        System.arraycopy(other.data, 0, data, 0, width * ySections);
1106        ct  = other.ct;
1107        tallied = other.tallied;
1108    }
1109
1110    /**
1111     * Primarily for internal use, this constructor copies data2 exactly into the internal long array the new
1112     * GreasedRegion will use, and does not perform any validation steps to ensure that cells that would be "on" but are
1113     * outside the actual height of the GreasedRegion are actually removed (this only matters if height is not a
1114     * multiple of 64).
1115     * @param data2 a long array that is typically from another GreasedRegion, and would be hard to make otherwise
1116     * @param width the width of the GreasedRegion to construct
1117     * @param height the height of the GreasedRegion to construct
1118     */
1119    public GreasedRegion(final long[] data2, final int width, final int height)
1120    {
1121        this.width = width;
1122        this.height = height;
1123        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
1124        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
1125        data = new long[width * ySections];
1126        System.arraycopy(data2, 0, data, 0, width * ySections);
1127        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
1128            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1129                data[a] &= yEndMask;
1130            }
1131        }
1132        counts = new int[width * ySections];
1133    }
1134
1135    /**
1136     * Primarily for internal use, this constructor copies data2 into the internal long array the new GreasedRegion will
1137     * use, but treats data2 as having the dimensions [dataWidth][dataHeight], and uses the potentially-different
1138     * dimensions [width][height] for the constructed GreasedRegion. This will truncate data2 on width, height, or both
1139     * if width or height is smaller than dataWidth or dataHeight. It will fill extra space with all "off" if width or
1140     * height is larger than dataWidth or dataHeight. It will interpret data2 as the same 2D shape regardless of the
1141     * width or height it is being assigned to, and data2 will not be reshaped by truncation.
1142     * @param data2 a long array that is typically from another GreasedRegion, and would be hard to make otherwise
1143     * @param dataWidth the width to interpret data2 as having
1144     * @param dataHeight the height to interpret data2 as having
1145     * @param width the width of the GreasedRegion to construct
1146     * @param height the height of the GreasedRegion to construct
1147     */
1148    public GreasedRegion(final long[] data2, final int dataWidth, final int dataHeight, final int width, final int height)
1149    {
1150        this.width = width;
1151        this.height = height;
1152        ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
1153        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
1154        data = new long[width * ySections];
1155
1156        final int ySections2 = (dataHeight + 63) >> 6;
1157        if(ySections2 == 0)
1158            return;
1159        if(ySections == 1) {
1160            System.arraycopy(data2, 0, data, 0, dataWidth);
1161        }
1162        else
1163        {
1164            if(dataHeight >= height) {
1165                for (int i = 0, j = 0; i < width && i < dataWidth; i += ySections2, j += ySections) {
1166                    System.arraycopy(data2, i, data, j, ySections);
1167                }
1168            }
1169            else
1170            {
1171                for (int i = 0, j = 0; i < width && i < dataWidth; i += ySections2, j += ySections) {
1172                    System.arraycopy(data2, i, data, j, ySections2);
1173                }
1174            }
1175        }
1176        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
1177            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1178                data[a] &= yEndMask;
1179            }
1180        }
1181        counts = new int[width * ySections];
1182    }
1183    /**
1184     * Primarily for internal use, this method copies data2 into the internal long array the new GreasedRegion will
1185     * use, but treats data2 as having the dimensions [dataWidth][dataHeight], and uses the potentially-different
1186     * dimensions [width][height] for this GreasedRegion, potentially re-allocating the internal data this uses if width
1187     * and/or height are different from what they were. This will truncate data2 on width, height, or both if width or
1188     * height is smaller than dataWidth or dataHeight. It will fill extra space with all "off" if width or height is
1189     * larger than dataWidth or dataHeight. It will interpret data2 as the same 2D shape regardless of the width or
1190     * height it is being assigned to, and data2 will not be reshaped by truncation.
1191     * @param data2 a long array that is typically from another GreasedRegion, and would be hard to make otherwise
1192     * @param dataWidth the width to interpret data2 as having
1193     * @param dataHeight the height to interpret data2 as having
1194     * @param width the width to set this GreasedRegion to have
1195     * @param height the height to set this GreasedRegion to have
1196     */
1197    public GreasedRegion refill(final long[] data2, final int dataWidth, final int dataHeight, final int width, final int height)
1198    {
1199        if(width != this.width || height != this.height) {
1200            this.width = width;
1201            this.height = height;
1202            ySections = (height + 63) >> 6;
1203            yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (height & 63));
1204            data = new long[width * ySections];
1205            counts = new int[width * ySections];
1206        }
1207        else {
1208            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
1209        }
1210        final int ySections2 = (dataHeight + 63) >> 6;
1211        if(ySections2 == 0)
1212            return this;
1213        if(ySections == 1) {
1214            System.arraycopy(data2, 0, data, 0, dataWidth);
1215        }
1216        else
1217        {
1218            if(dataHeight >= height) {
1219                for (int i = 0, j = 0; i < width && i < dataWidth; i += ySections2, j += ySections) {
1220                    System.arraycopy(data2, i, data, j, ySections);
1221                }
1222            }
1223            else
1224            {
1225                for (int i = 0, j = 0; i < width && i < dataWidth; i += ySections2, j += ySections) {
1226                    System.arraycopy(data2, i, data, j, ySections2);
1227                }
1228            }
1229        }
1230        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
1231            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1232                data[a] &= yEndMask;
1233            }
1234        }
1235        tallied = false;
1236        return this;
1237    }
1238
1239    /**
1240     * A useful method for efficiency, remake() reassigns this GreasedRegion to have its contents replaced by other. If
1241     * other and this GreasedRegion have identical width and height, this is very efficient and performs no additional
1242     * allocations, simply replacing the cell data in this with the cell data from other. If width and height are not
1243     * both equal between this and other, this does allocate a new data array, but still reassigns this GreasedRegion
1244     * in-place and acts similarly to when width and height are both equal (it just uses some more memory).
1245     * <br>
1246     * Using remake() or the similar refill() methods in chains of operations on multiple GreasedRegions can be key to
1247     * maintaining good performance and memory usage. You often can recycle a no-longer-used GreasedRegion by assigning
1248     * a GreasedRegion you want to keep to it with remake(), then mutating either the remade value or the one that was
1249     * just filled into this but keeping one version around for later usage.
1250     * @param other another GreasedRegion to replace the data in this GreasedRegion with
1251     * @return this for chaining
1252     */
1253    public GreasedRegion remake(GreasedRegion other) {
1254        if (width == other.width && height == other.height) {
1255            System.arraycopy(other.data, 0, data, 0, width * ySections);
1256            System.arraycopy(other.counts, 0, counts, 0, width * ySections);
1257            ct = other.ct;
1258            tallied = other.tallied;
1259            return this;
1260        } else {
1261            width = other.width;
1262            height = other.height;
1263            ySections = other.ySections;
1264            yEndMask = other.yEndMask;
1265            data = new long[width * ySections];
1266            System.arraycopy(other.data, 0, data, 0, width * ySections);
1267            System.arraycopy(other.counts, 0, counts, 0, width * ySections);
1268            ct = other.ct;
1269            tallied = other.tallied;
1270            return this;
1271        }
1272    }
1273
1274    /**
1275     * Changes the width and/or height of this GreasedRegion, enlarging or shrinking starting at the edges where
1276     * {@code x == width - 1} and {@code y == height - 1}. There isn't an especially efficient way to expand from the
1277     * other edges, but this method is able to copy data in bulk, so at least this method should be very fast. You can
1278     * use {@code insert(int, int, GreasedRegion)} if you want to place one GreasedRegion inside another one,
1279     * potentially with a different size. The space created by any enlargement starts all off; shrinking doesn't change
1280     * the existing data where it isn't removed by the shrink.
1281     * @param widthChange the amount to change width by; can be positive, negative, or zero
1282     * @param heightChange the amount to change height by; can be positive, negative, or zero
1283     * @return this for chaining
1284     */
1285    public GreasedRegion alterBounds(int widthChange, int heightChange)
1286    {
1287        int newWidth = width + widthChange;
1288        int newHeight = height + heightChange;
1289        if(newWidth <= 0 || newHeight <= 0)
1290        {
1291            width = 0;
1292            height = 0;
1293            ySections= 0;
1294            yEndMask = -1;
1295            data = new long[0];
1296            counts = new int[0];
1297            ct = 0;
1298            tallied = true;
1299            return this;
1300        }
1301        int newYSections = (newHeight + 63) >> 6;
1302        yEndMask = -1L >>> (64 - (newHeight & 63));
1303        long[] newData = new long[newWidth * newYSections];         
1304        counts = new int[newWidth * newYSections];
1305        
1306        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < newWidth; x++) {
1307            for (int ys = 0; ys < ySections && ys < newYSections; ys++) {
1308                newData[x * newYSections + ys] = data[x * ySections + ys];
1309            }
1310        }
1311        ySections = newYSections;
1312        width = newWidth;
1313        height = newHeight;
1314        data = newData;
1315        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
1316            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1317                data[a] &= yEndMask;
1318            }
1319        }
1320        tallied = false;
1321        return this;
1322    }
1323
1324    /**
1325     * Sets the cell at x,y to on if value is true or off if value is false. Does nothing if x,y is out of bounds.
1326     * @param value the value to set in the cell
1327     * @param x the x-position of the cell
1328     * @param y the y-position of the cell
1329     * @return this for chaining
1330     */
1331    public GreasedRegion set(boolean value, int x, int y)
1332    {
1333        if(x < width && y < height && x >= 0 && y >= 0) {
1334            if(value)
1335                data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
1336            else
1337                data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] &= ~(1L << (y & 63));
1338            tallied = false;
1339        }
1340        return this;
1341    }
1342
1343    /**
1344     * Sets the cell at point to on if value is true or off if value is false. Does nothing if point is out of bounds,
1345     * or if point is null.
1346     * @param value the value to set in the cell
1347     * @param point the x,y Coord of the cell to set
1348     * @return this for chaining
1349     */
1350    public GreasedRegion set(boolean value, Coord point)
1351    {
1352        if(point == null) return this;
1353        return set(value, point.x, point.y);
1354    }
1355
1356    /**
1357     * Sets the cell at x,y to "on". Does nothing if x,y is out of bounds.
1358     * More efficient, slightly, than {@link #set(boolean, int, int)} if you just need to set a cell to "on".
1359     * @param x the x-position of the cell
1360     * @param y the y-position of the cell
1361     * @return this for chaining
1362     */
1363    public GreasedRegion insert(int x, int y)
1364    {
1365        if(x < width && y < height && x >= 0 && y >= 0)
1366        {
1367            data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
1368            tallied = false;
1369        }
1370        return this;
1371    }
1372
1373    /**
1374     * Sets the given cell, "tightly" encoded for a specific width/height as by {@link #asTightEncoded()}, to "on".
1375     * Does nothing if the cell is out of bounds.
1376     * @param tight a cell tightly encoded for this GreasedRegion's width and height
1377     * @return this for chaining
1378     */
1379    public GreasedRegion insert(int tight)
1380    {
1381        if(tight < width * height && tight >= 0)
1382        {
1383            data[(tight % width) * ySections + ((tight / width) >>> 6)] |= 1L << ((tight / width) & 63);
1384            tallied = false;
1385        }
1386        return this;
1387    }
1388    /**
1389     * Sets the cell at point to "on". Does nothing if point is out of bounds, or if point is null.
1390     * More efficient, slightly, than {@link #set(boolean, Coord)} if you just need to set a cell to "on".
1391     * @param point the x,y Coord of the cell
1392     * @return this for chaining
1393     */
1394    public GreasedRegion insert(Coord point)
1395    {
1396
1397        if(point == null) return this;
1398        return insert(point.x, point.y);
1399    }
1400
1401    /**
1402     * Takes another GreasedRegion, called other, with potentially different size and inserts its "on" cells into thi
1403     * GreasedRegion at the given x,y offset, allowing negative x and/or y to put only part of other in this.
1404     * <br>
1405     * This is a rather complex method internally, but should be about as efficient as a general insert-region method
1406     * can be.
1407     * @param x the x offset to start inserting other at; may be negative
1408     * @param y the y offset to start inserting other at; may be negative
1409     * @param other the other GreasedRegion to insert
1410     * @return this for chaining
1411     */
1412    public GreasedRegion insert(int x, int y, GreasedRegion other)
1413    {
1414        if(other == null || other.ySections <= 0 || other.width <= 0)
1415            return this;
1416
1417        int start = Math.max(0, x), len = Math.min(width, Math.min(other.width, other.width + x) - start),
1418        oys = other.ySections, jump = (y == 0) ? 0 : (y < 0) ? -(1-y >>> 6) : (y-1 >>> 6), lily = (y < 0) ? -(-y & 63) : (y & 63),
1419        originalJump = Math.max(0, -jump), alterJump = Math.max(0, jump);
1420        long[] data2 = new long[other.width * ySections];
1421
1422        long prev, tmp;
1423        if(oys == ySections) {
1424            if (x < 0) {
1425                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1426                    for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
1427                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1428                    }
1429                }
1430            } else if (x > 0) {
1431                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1432                    for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
1433                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * ySections + oi];
1434                    }
1435                }
1436            } else {
1437                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1438                    for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
1439                        data2[j * ySections + i] = other.data[j * ySections + oi];
1440                    }
1441                }
1442            }
1443        }
1444        else if(oys < ySections)
1445        {
1446            if (x < 0) {
1447                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1448                    for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
1449                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1450                    }
1451                }
1452            } else if (x > 0) {
1453                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {// oi < oys - Math.max(0, jump)
1454                    for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
1455                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1456                    }
1457                }
1458            } else {
1459                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1460                    for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
1461                        data2[j * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1462                    }
1463                }
1464            }
1465        }
1466        else
1467        {
1468            if (x < 0) {
1469                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1470                    for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
1471                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1472                    }
1473                }
1474            } else if (x > 0) {
1475                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1476                    for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
1477                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1478                    }
1479                }
1480            } else {
1481                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1482                    for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
1483                        data2[j * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1484                    }
1485                }
1486            }
1487        }
1488
1489        if(lily < 0) {
1490            for (int i = start; i < len; i++) {
1491                prev = 0L;
1492                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
1493                    tmp = prev;
1494                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L << -lily)) << (64 + lily);
1495                    data2[i * ySections + j] >>>= -lily;
1496                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
1497                }
1498            }
1499        }
1500        else if(lily > 0) {
1501            for (int i = start; i < start + len; i++) {
1502                prev = 0L;
1503                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
1504                    tmp = prev;
1505                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L >>> lily)) >>> (64 - lily);
1506                    data2[i * ySections + j] <<= lily;
1507                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
1508                }
1509            }
1510        }
1511        len = Math.min(width, start + len);
1512        for (int i = start; i < len; i++) {
1513            for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
1514                data[i * ySections + j] |= data2[i * ySections + j];
1515            }
1516        }
1517
1518        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
1519            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1520                data[a] &= yEndMask;
1521            }
1522        }
1523        tallied = false;
1524        return this;
1525    }
1526
1527    public GreasedRegion insertSeveral(Coord... points)
1528    {
1529        for (int i = 0, x, y; i < points.length; i++) {
1530            x = points[i].x;
1531            y = points[i].y;
1532            if(x < width && y < height && x >= 0 && y >= 0)
1533            {
1534                data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
1535                tallied = false;
1536            }
1537        }
1538        return this;
1539    }
1540
1541    public GreasedRegion insertSeveral(final int[] points)
1542    {
1543        for (int i = 0, tight; i < points.length; i++) {
1544            tight = points[i];
1545            if(tight < width * height && tight >= 0)
1546            {
1547                data[(tight % width) * ySections + ((tight / width) >>> 6)] |= 1L << ((tight / width) & 63);
1548                tallied = false;
1549            }
1550        }
1551        return this;
1552    }
