1554    public GreasedRegion insertSeveral(Iterable<Coord> points)
1555    {
1556        int x, y;
1557        for (Coord pt : points) {
1558            x = pt.x;
1559            y = pt.y;
1560            if(x < width && y < height && x >= 0 && y >= 0)
1561            {
1562                data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] |= 1L << (y & 63);
1563                tallied = false;
1564            }
1565        }
1566        return this;
1567    }
1568
1569    public GreasedRegion insertRectangle(int startX, int startY, int rectangleWidth, int rectangleHeight)
1570    {
1571        if(rectangleWidth < 1 || rectangleHeight < 1 || ySections <= 0)
1572            return this;
1573        if(startX < 0)
1574            startX = 0;
1575        else if(startX >= width)
1576            startX = width - 1;
1577        if(startY < 0)
1578            startY = 0;
1579        else if(startY >= height)
1580            startY = height - 1;
1581        int endX = Math.min(width, startX + rectangleWidth) - 1,
1582                endY = Math.min(height, startY + rectangleHeight) - 1,
1583                startSection = startY >> 6, endSection = endY >> 6;
1584        if(startSection < endSection)
1585        {
1586            long startMask = -1L << (startY & 63),
1587                    endMask = -1L >>> (~endY & 63);
1588            for (int a = startX * ySections + startSection; a <= endX * ySections + startSection; a += ySections) {
1589                data[a] |= startMask;
1590            }
1591            if(endSection - startSection > 1)
1592            {
1593                for (int b = 1; b < endSection - startSection; b++) {
1594                    for (int a = startX * ySections + startSection + b; a < endX * ySections + ySections; a += ySections) {
1595                        data[a] = -1;
1596                    }
1597                }
1598            }
1599            for (int a = startX * ySections + endSection; a <= endX * ySections + endSection; a += ySections) {
1600                data[a] |= endMask;
1601            }
1602        }
1603        else
1604        {
1605            long mask = (-1L << (startY & 63)) & (-1L >>> (~endY & 63));
1606            for (int a = startX * ySections + startSection; a <= endX * ySections + startSection; a += ySections) {
1607                data[a] |= mask;
1608            }
1609        }
1610
1611        if(yEndMask != -1L) {
1612            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1613                data[a] &= yEndMask;
1614            }
1615        }
1616        tallied = false;
1617        return this;
1618    }
1619
1620    public GreasedRegion insertCircle(Coord center, int radius)
1621    {
1622        float high, changedX;
1623        int rndX, rndY;
1624        for (int dx = -radius; dx <= radius; ++dx) {
1625            changedX = dx - 0.25f * Math.signum(dx);
1626            rndX = Math.round(changedX);
1627            high = (float) Math.sqrt(radius * radius - changedX * changedX);             
1628            insert(center.x + rndX, center.y);
1629            for (float dy = high; dy >= 0.75f; --dy) {
1630                rndY = Math.round(dy - 0.25f);                 
1631                insert(center.x + rndX, center.y + rndY);
1632                insert(center.x + rndX, center.y - rndY);
1633            }
1634        }
1635        return this;
1636    }
1637
1638    public GreasedRegion remove(int x, int y)
1639    {
1640        if(x < width && y < height && x >= 0 && y >= 0)
1641        {
1642            data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] &= ~(1L << (y & 63));
1643            tallied = false;
1644        }
1645        return this;
1646    }
1647    public GreasedRegion remove(Coord point)
1648    {
1649        return remove(point.x, point.y);
1650    }
1651    /**
1652     * Takes another GreasedRegion, called other, with potentially different size and removes its "on" cells from this
1653     * GreasedRegion at the given x,y offset, allowing negative x and/or y to remove only part of other in this.
1654     * <br>
1655     * This is a rather complex method internally, but should be about as efficient as a general remove-region method
1656     * can be. The code is identical to {@link #insert(int, int, GreasedRegion)} except that where insert only adds
1657     * cells, this only removes cells. Essentially, insert() is to {@link #or(GreasedRegion)} as remove() is to
1658     * {@link #andNot(GreasedRegion)}.
1659     * @param x the x offset to start removing other from; may be negative
1660     * @param y the y offset to start removing other from; may be negative
1661     * @param other the other GreasedRegion to remove
1662     * @return this for chaining
1663     */
1664    public GreasedRegion remove(int x, int y, GreasedRegion other)
1665    {
1666        if(other == null || other.ySections <= 0 || other.width <= 0)
1667            return this;
1668
1669        int start = Math.max(0, x), len = Math.min(width, Math.min(other.width, other.width + x) - start),
1670                oys = other.ySections, jump = (y == 0) ? 0 : (y < 0) ? -(1-y >>> 6) : (y-1 >>> 6), lily = (y < 0) ? -(-y & 63) : (y & 63),
1671                originalJump = Math.max(0, -jump), alterJump = Math.max(0, jump);
1672        long[] data2 = new long[other.width * ySections];
1673
1674        long prev, tmp;
1675        if(oys == ySections) {
1676            if (x < 0) {
1677                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1678                    for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
1679                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1680                    }
1681                }
1682            } else if (x > 0) {
1683                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1684                    for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
1685                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * ySections + oi];
1686                    }
1687                }
1688            } else {
1689                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1690                    for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
1691                        data2[j * ySections + i] = other.data[j * ySections + oi];
1692                    }
1693                }
1694            }
1695        }
1696        else if(oys < ySections)
1697        {
1698            if (x < 0) {
1699                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1700                    for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
1701                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1702                    }
1703                }
1704            } else if (x > 0) {
1705                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {// oi < oys - Math.max(0, jump)
1706                    for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
1707                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1708                    }
1709                }
1710            } else {
1711                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1712                    for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
1713                        data2[j * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1714                    }
1715                }
1716            }
1717        }
1718        else
1719        {
1720            if (x < 0) {
1721                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1722                    for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
1723                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1724                    }
1725                }
1726            } else if (x > 0) {
1727                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1728                    for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
1729                        data2[jj * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1730                    }
1731                }
1732            } else {
1733                for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < oys; i++, oi++) {
1734                    for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
1735                        data2[j * ySections + i] = other.data[j * oys + oi];
1736                    }
1737                }
1738            }
1739        }
1740
1741        if(lily < 0) {
1742            for (int i = start; i < len; i++) {
1743                prev = 0L;
1744                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
1745                    tmp = prev;
1746                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L << -lily)) << (64 + lily);
1747                    data2[i * ySections + j] >>>= -lily;
1748                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
1749                }
1750            }
1751        }
1752        else if(lily > 0) {
1753            for (int i = start; i < start + len; i++) {
1754                prev = 0L;
1755                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
1756                    tmp = prev;
1757                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L >>> lily)) >>> (64 - lily);
1758                    data2[i * ySections + j] <<= lily;
1759                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
1760                }
1761            }
1762        }
1763        len = Math.min(width, start + len);
1764        for (int i = start; i < len; i++) {
1765            for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
1766                data[i * ySections + j] &= ~data2[i * ySections + j];
1767            }
1768        }
1769
1770        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
1771            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1772                data[a] &= yEndMask;
1773            }
1774        }
1775        tallied = false;
1776
1777        return this;
1778    }

1783            y = points[i].y;
1784            if(x < width && y < height && x >= 0 && y >= 0)
1785            {
1786                data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] &= ~(1L << (y & 63));
1787                tallied = false;
1788            }
1789        }
1790        return this;
1791    }

1797            x = pt.x;
1798            y = pt.y;
1799            if(x < width && y < height && x >= 0 && y >= 0)
1800            {

1802                tallied = false;
1803            }

1807
1808    public GreasedRegion removeRectangle(int startX, int startY, int rectangleWidth, int rectangleHeight)
1809    {
1810        if(startX < 0)
1811        {
1812            rectangleWidth += startX;
1813            startX = 0;
1814        }
1815        else if(startX >= width)
1816        {
1817            rectangleWidth = 1;
1818            startX = width - 1;
1819        }
1820        if(startY < 0)
1821        {
1822            rectangleHeight += startY;
1823            startY = 0;
1824        }
1825        else if(startY >= height)
1826        {
1827            rectangleHeight = 1;
1828            startY = height - 1;
1829        }
1830        if(rectangleWidth < 1 || rectangleHeight < 1 || ySections <= 0)
1831            return this;
1832        int endX = Math.min(width, startX + rectangleWidth) - 1,
1833                endY = Math.min(height, startY + rectangleHeight) - 1,
1834                startSection = startY >> 6, endSection = endY >> 6;
1835        if(startSection < endSection)
1836        {
1837            long startMask = ~(-1L << (startY & 63)),
1838                    endMask = ~(-1L >>> (~endY & 63));
1839            for (int a = startX * ySections + startSection; a <= endX * ySections; a += ySections) {
1840                data[a] &= startMask;
1841            }
1842            if(endSection - startSection > 1)
1843            {
1844                for (int b = 1; b < endSection - startSection; b++) {
1845                    for (int a = startX * ySections + startSection + b; a < endX * ySections + ySections; a += ySections) {
1846                        data[a] = 0;
1847                    }
1848                }
1849            }
1850            for (int a = startX * ySections + endSection; a <= endX * ySections + ySections; a += ySections) {
1851                data[a] &= endMask;
1852            }
1853        }
1854        else
1855        {
1856            long mask = ~((-1L << (startY & 63)) & (-1L >>> (~endY & 63)));
1857            for (int a = startX * ySections + startSection; a <= endX * ySections + startSection; a += ySections) {
1858                data[a] &= mask;
1859            }
1860        }
1861        tallied = false;
1862        return this;
1863    }
1864
1865    public GreasedRegion removeCircle(Coord center, int radius)
1866    {
1867        float high, changedX;
1868        int rndX, rndY;
1869        for (int dx = -radius; dx <= radius; ++dx) {
1870            changedX = dx - 0.25f * Math.signum(dx);
1871            rndX = Math.round(changedX);
1872            high = (float) Math.sqrt(radius * radius - changedX * changedX);
1873            remove(center.x + rndX, center.y);
1874            for (float dy = high; dy >= 0.75f; --dy) {
1875                rndY = Math.round(dy - 0.25f);
1876                remove(center.x + rndX, center.y + rndY);
1877                remove(center.x + rndX, center.y - rndY);
1878            }
1879        }
1880        return this;
1881    }
1882
1883    /**
1884     * Equivalent to {@link #clear()}, setting all cells to "off," but also returns this for chaining.
1885     * @return this for chaining
1886     */
1887    public GreasedRegion empty()
1888    {
1889        Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
1890        Arrays.fill(counts, 0);
1891        ct = 0;
1892        tallied = true;
1893        return this;
1894    }
1895
1896    /**
1897     * Sets all cells in this to "on."
1898     * @return this for chaining
1899     */
1900    public GreasedRegion allOn()
1901    {
1902        if(ySections > 0)
1903        {
1904            if(yEndMask == -1) {
1905                Arrays.fill(data, -1);
1906                Arrays.fill(counts, 64);
1907                ct = ySections * width << 6;
1908                tallied = true;
1909            }
1910            else
1911            {
1912                ct = Long.bitCount(yEndMask);
1913                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1914                    data[a] = yEndMask;
1915                    counts[a] = ct;
1916                    for (int i = 0; i < ySections - 1; i++) {
1917                        data[a-i-1] = -1;
1918                        counts[a-i-1] = 64;
1919                    }
1920                }
1921                ct *= width;
1922                ct += (ySections - 1) * width << 6;
1923                tallied = true;
1924            }
1925        }
1926        return this;
1927    }
1928
1929    /**
1930     * Sets all cells in this to "on" if contents is true, or "off" if contents is false.
1931     * @param contents true to set all cells to on, false to set all cells to off
1932     * @return this for chaining
1933     */
1934    public GreasedRegion fill(boolean contents)
1935    {
1936        if(contents)
1937        {
1938            if(ySections > 0)
1939            {
1940                if(yEndMask == -1) {
1941                    Arrays.fill(data, -1);
1942                    Arrays.fill(counts, 64);
1943                    ct = ySections * width << 6;
1944                    tallied = true;
1945                }
1946                else
1947                {
1948                    ct = Long.bitCount(yEndMask);
1949                    for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
1950                        data[a] = yEndMask;
1951                        counts[a] = ct;
1952                        for (int i = 0; i < ySections - 1; i++) {
1953                            data[a-i-1] = -1;
1954                            counts[a-i-1] = 64;
1955                        }
1956                    }
1957                    ct *= width;
1958                    ct += (ySections - 1) * width << 6;
1959                    tallied = true;
1960                }
1961            }
1962            //else... what, if ySections is 0 there's nothing to do
1963        }
1964        else
1965        {
1966            Arrays.fill(data, 0L);
1967            Arrays.fill(counts, 0);
1968            ct = 0;
1969            tallied = true;
1970        }
1971        return this;
1972    }
1973    /**
1974     * Turns all cells that are adjacent to the boundaries of the GreasedRegion to "off".
1975     * @return this for chaining
1976     */
1977    public GreasedRegion removeEdges()
1978    {
1979        if(ySections > 0) {
1980            for (int i = 0; i < ySections; i++) {
1981                data[i] = 0L;
1982                data[width * ySections - 1 - i] = 0L;
1983            }
1984            if (ySections == 1) {
1985                for (int i = 0; i < width; i++) {
1986                    data[i] &= yEndMask >>> 1 & -2L;
1987                }
1988            } else {
1989                for (int i = ySections; i < data.length - ySections; i += ySections) {
1990                    data[i] &= -2L;
1991                }
1992                for (int a = ySections * 2 - 1; a < data.length - ySections; a += ySections) {
1993                    data[a] &= yEndMask >>> 1;
1994                }
1995            }
1996            tallied = false;
1997        }
1998        return this;
1999    }

2001    /**
2002     * Simple method that returns a newly-allocated copy of this GreasedRegion; modifications to one won't change the
2003     * other, and this method returns the copy while leaving the original unchanged.
2004     * @return a copy of this GreasedRegion; the copy can be changed without altering the original
2005     */
2006    public GreasedRegion copy()
2007    {
2008        return new GreasedRegion(this);
2009    }

2011    /**
2012     * Returns this GreasedRegion's data as a 2D boolean array, [width][height] in size, with on treated as true and off
2013     * treated as false.
2014     * @return a 2D boolean array that represents this GreasedRegion's data
2015     */
2016    public boolean[][] decode()
2017    {
2018        boolean[][] bools = new boolean[width][height];
2019        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
2020            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
2021                bools[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0;
2022            }
2023        }
2024        return bools;
2025    }
2026
2027    /**
2028     * Fills this GreasedRegion's data into the given 2D char array, modifying it and returning it, with "on" cells
2029     * filled with the char parameter {@code on} and "off" cells with the parameter {@code off}.
2030     * @param chars a 2D char array that will be modified; must not be null, nor can it contain null elements
2031     * @param on the char to use for "on" cells
2032     * @param off the char to use for "off" cells
2033     * @return a 2D char array that represents this GreasedRegion's data
2034     */
2035    public char[][] intoChars(char[][] chars, char on, char off)
2036    {
2037        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < chars.length; x++) {
2038            for (int y = 0; y < height && y < chars[x].length; y++) {
2039                chars[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? on : off;
2040            }
2041        }
2042        return chars;
2043    }
2044
2045    /**
2046     * Fills this GreasedRegion's data into the given 2D char array, modifying it and returning it, with "on" cells
2047     * filled with the char parameter {@code on} and "off" cells left as-is.
2048     * @param chars a 2D char array that will be modified; must not be null, nor can it contain null elements
2049     * @param on the char to use for "on" cells
2050     * @return a 2D char array that represents the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion's data written over chars
2051     */
2052    public char[][] intoChars(char[][] chars, char on)
2053    {
2054        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < chars.length; x++) {
2055            for (int y = 0; y < height && y < chars[x].length; y++) {
2056                if((data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0)
2057                    chars[x][y] = on;
2058            }
2059        }
2060        return chars;
2061    }

2063    /**
2064     * Returns this GreasedRegion's data as a 2D char array,  [width][height] in size, with "on" cells filled with the
2065     * char parameter on and "off" cells with the parameter off.
2066     * @param on the char to use for "on" cells
2067     * @param off the char to use for "off" cells
2068     * @return a 2D char array that represents this GreasedRegion's data
2069     */
2070    public char[][] toChars(char on, char off)
2071    {
2072        char[][] chars = new char[width][height];
2073        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
2074            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
2075                chars[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? on : off;
2076            }
2077        }
2078        return chars;
2079    }
2080    /**
2081     * Returns this GreasedRegion's data as a 2D char array,  [width][height] in size, with "on" cells filled with '.'
2082     * and "off" cells with '#'.
2083     * @return a 2D char array that represents this GreasedRegion's data
2084     */
2085
2086    public char[][] toChars()
2087    {
2088        return toChars('.', '#');
2089    }
2090
2091    /**
2092     * Returns this GreasedRegion's data as a StringBuilder, with each row made of the parameter on for "on" cells and
2093     * the parameter off for "off" cells, separated by newlines, with no trailing newline at the end.
2094     * @param on the char to use for "on" cells
2095     * @param off the char to use for "off" cells
2096     * @return a StringBuilder that stores each row of this GreasedRegion as chars, with rows separated by newlines.
2097     */
2098    public StringBuilder show(char on, char off)
2099    {
2100        StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder((width+1) * height);
2101        for (int y = 0; y < height;) {
2102            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
2103                sb.append((data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? on : off);
2104            }
2105            if(++y < height)
2106                sb.append('\n');
2107        }
2108        return sb;
2109    }
2110
2111    /**
2112     * Returns a legible String representation of this that can be printed over multiple lines, with all "on" cells
2113     * represented by '.' and all "off" cells by '#', in roguelike floors-on walls-off convention, separating each row
2114     * by newlines (without a final trailing newline, so you could append text right after this).
2115     * @return a String representation of this GreasedRegion using '.' for on, '#' for off, and newlines between rows
2116     */
2117    @Override
2118    public String toString()
2119    {
2120        return show('.', '#').toString();
2121    }

2123    /**
2124     * Returns a copy of map where if a cell is "on" in this GreasedRegion, this keeps the value in map intact,
2125     * and where a cell is "off", it instead writes the char filler.
2126     * @param map a 2D char array that will not be modified
2127     * @param filler the char to use where this GreasedRegion stores an "off" cell
2128     * @return a masked copy of map
2129     */
2130    public char[][] mask(char[][] map, char filler)
2131    {
2132        if(map == null || map.length == 0)
2133            return new char[0][0];
2134        int width2 = Math.min(width, map.length), height2 = Math.min(height, map[0].length);
2135        char[][] chars = new char[width2][height2];
2136        for (int x = 0; x < width2; x++) {
2137            for (int y = 0; y < height2; y++) {
2138                chars[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? map[x][y] : filler;
2139            }
2140        }
2141        return chars;
2142    }

2145     * Returns a copy of map where if a cell is "on" in this GreasedRegion, this keeps the value in map intact,
2146     * and where a cell is "off", it instead writes the short filler. Meant for use with MultiSpill, but may be
2147     * used anywhere you have a 2D short array. {@link #mask(char[][], char)} is more likely to be useful.

2149     * @param filler the short to use where this GreasedRegion stores an "off" cell

2151     */
2152    public short[][] mask(short[][] map, short filler)

2155            return new short[0][0];
2156        int width2 = Math.min(width, map.length), height2 = Math.min(height, map[0].length);
2157        short[][] shorts = new short[width2][height2];
2158        for (int x = 0; x < width2; x++) {
2159            for (int y = 0; y < height2; y++) {
2160                shorts[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? map[x][y] : filler;
2161            }
2162        }
2163        return shorts;
2164    }

2167     * Returns a copy of map where if a cell is "off" in this GreasedRegion, this keeps the value in map intact,
2168     * and where a cell is "on", it instead writes the char toWrite.
2169     * @param map a 2D char array that will not be modified
2170     * @param toWrite the char to use where this GreasedRegion stores an "on" cell
2171     * @return a masked copy of map
2172     */
2173    public char[][] inverseMask(char[][] map, char toWrite)
2174    {
2175        if(map == null || map.length == 0)
2176            return new char[0][0];
2177        int width2 = Math.min(width, map.length), height2 = Math.min(height, map[0].length);
2178        char[][] chars = new char[width2][height2];
2179        for (int x = 0; x < width2; x++) {
2180            for (int y = 0; y < height2; y++) {
2181                chars[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? toWrite : map[x][y];
2182            }

2187    /**
2188     * "Inverse mask for ints;" returns a copy of map where if a cell is "off" in this GreasedRegion, this keeps

2190     * @param map a 2D int array that will not be modified
2191     * @param toWrite the int to use where this GreasedRegion stores an "on" cell
2192     * @return an altered copy of map
2193     */
2194    public int[][] writeInts(int[][] map, int toWrite)
2195    {

2197            return new int[0][0];
2198        int width2 = Math.min(width, map.length), height2 = Math.min(height, map[0].length);
2199        int[][] ints = new int[width2][height2];
2200        for (int x = 0; x < width2; x++) {
2201            for (int y = 0; y < height2; y++) {
2202                ints[x][y] = (data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? toWrite : map[x][y];
2203            }
2204        }
2205        return ints;

2208    /**
2209     * "Inverse mask for ints;" returns a copy of map where if a cell is "off" in this GreasedRegion, this keeps
2210     * the value in map intact, and where a cell is "on", it instead writes the int toWrite. Modifies map in-place,
2211     * unlike {@link #writeInts(int[][], int)}.
2212     * @param map a 2D int array that <b>will</b> be modified
2213     * @param toWrite the int to use where this GreasedRegion stores an "on" cell
2214     * @return map, with the changes applied; not a copy
2215     */
2216    public int[][] writeIntsInto(int[][] map, int toWrite)
2217    {
2218        if(map == null || map.length == 0)
2219            return map;
2220        int width2 = Math.min(width, map.length), height2 = Math.min(height, map[0].length);
2221        for (int x = 0; x < width2; x++) {
2222            for (int y = 0; y < height2; y++) {
2223                if((data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0)
2224                    map[x][y] = toWrite;
2225            }
2226        }
2227        return map;
2228    }

2272    /**
2273     * Union of two GreasedRegions, assigning the result into this GreasedRegion. Any cell that is "on" in either
2274     * GreasedRegion will be made "on" in this GreasedRegion.
2275     * @param other another GreasedRegion that will not be modified
2276     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2277     */
2278    public GreasedRegion or(GreasedRegion other)
2279    {
2280        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
2281            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
2282                data[x * ySections + y] |= other.data[x * ySections + y];
2283            }
2284        }
2285
2286        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2287            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
2288                data[a] &= yEndMask;
2289            }
2290        }
2291        tallied = false;
2292
2293        return this;
2294    }

2296    /**
2297     * Intersection of two GreasedRegions, assigning the result into this GreasedRegion. Any cell that is "on" in both
2298     * GreasedRegions will be kept "on" in this GreasedRegion, but all other cells will be made "off."
2299     * @param other another GreasedRegion that will not be modified
2300     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2301     */
2302    public GreasedRegion and(GreasedRegion other)
2303    {
2304        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
2305            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
2306                data[x * ySections + y] &= other.data[x * ySections + y];
2307            }
2308        }
2309        tallied = false;
2310        return this;
2311    }
2312    /**
2313     * Difference of two GreasedRegions, assigning the result into this GreasedRegion. Any cell that is "on" in this
2314     * GreasedRegion and "off" in other will be kept "on" in this GreasedRegion, but all other cells will be made "off."
2315     * @param other another GreasedRegion that will not be modified
2316     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2317     * @see #notAnd(GreasedRegion) notAnd is a very similar method that acts sort-of in reverse of this method
2318     */
2319    public GreasedRegion andNot(GreasedRegion other)
2320    {
2321        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
2322            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
2323                data[x * ySections + y] &= ~other.data[x * ySections + y];
2324            }
2325        }
2326        tallied = false;
2327        return this;
2328    }

2330    /**
2331     * Like andNot, but subtracts this GreasedRegion from other and stores the result in this GreasedRegion, without
2332     * mutating other.
2333     * @param other another GreasedRegion that will not be modified
2334     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2335     * @see #andNot(GreasedRegion) andNot is a very similar method that acts sort-of in reverse of this method
2336     */
2337    public GreasedRegion notAnd(GreasedRegion other)
2338    {
2339        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
2340            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
2341                data[x * ySections + y] = other.data[x * ySections + y] & ~data[x * ySections + y];
2342            }
2343        }
2344        tallied = false;
2345        return this;
2346    }

2348    /**
2349     * Symmetric difference (more commonly known as exclusive or, hence the name) of two GreasedRegions, assigning the
2350     * result into this GreasedRegion. Any cell that is "on" in this and "off" in other, or "off" in this and "on" in
2351     * other, will be made "on" in this; all other cells will be made "off." Useful to find cells that are "on" in
2352     * exactly one of two GreasedRegions (not "on" in both, or "off" in both).
2353     * @param other another GreasedRegion that will not be modified
2354     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2355     */
2356    public GreasedRegion xor(GreasedRegion other)
2357    {
2358        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
2359            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
2360                data[x * ySections + y] ^= other.data[x * ySections + y];
2361            }
2362        }
2363
2364        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2365            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
2366                data[a] &= yEndMask;
2367            }
2368        }
2369        tallied = false;
2370        return this;
2371    }
2372
2373    /**
2374     * Negates this GreasedRegion, turning "on" to "off" and "off" to "on."
2375     * @return this, after modification, for chaining
2376     */
2377    public GreasedRegion not()
2378    {
2379        for (int a = 0; a < data.length; a++)
2380        {
2381            data[a] = ~data[a];
2382        }
2383
2384        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2385            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
2386                data[a] &= yEndMask;
2387            }
2388        }
2389        tallied = false;
2390        return this;
2391    }

2393    /**
2394     * Moves the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion to the given x and y offset, removing cells that move out of bounds.
2395     * @param x the x offset to translate by; can be negative
2396     * @param y the y offset to translate by; can be negative
2397     * @return this for chaining
2398     */
2399    public GreasedRegion translate(int x, int y)
2400    {
2401        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0 || (x == 0 && y == 0))
2402            return this;
2403        int start = Math.max(0, x), len = Math.min(width, width + x) - start,
2404                jump = (y == 0) ? 0 : (y < 0) ? -(1-y >>> 6) : (y-1 >>> 6), lily = (y < 0) ? -(-y & 63) : (y & 63),
2405                originalJump = Math.max(0, -jump), alterJump = Math.max(0, jump);
2406        long[] data2 = new long[width * ySections];
2407
2408        long prev, tmp;
2409        if (x < 0) {
2410            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2411                for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
2412                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2413                }
2414            }
2415        } else if (x > 0) {
2416            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2417                for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
2418                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2419                }
2420            }
2421        } else {
2422            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2423                for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
2424                    data2[j * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2425                }
2426            }
2427        }
2428
2429        if(lily < 0) {
2430            for (int i = start; i < len; i++) {
2431                prev = 0L;
2432                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
2433                    tmp = prev;
2434                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L << -lily)) << (64 + lily);
2435                    data2[i * ySections + j] >>>= -lily;
2436                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2437                }
2438            }
2439        }
2440        else if(lily > 0) {
2441            for (int i = start; i < start + len; i++) {
2442                prev = 0L;
2443                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
2444                    tmp = prev;
2445                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L >>> lily)) >>> (64 - lily);
2446                    data2[i * ySections + j] <<= lily;
2447                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2448                }
2449            }
2450        }
2451
2452
2453        if(yEndMask != -1) {
2454            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data2.length; a += ySections) {
2455                data2[a] &= yEndMask;
2456            }
2457        }
2458
2459        data = data2;
2460        tallied = false;
2461        return this;
2462    }
2463
2464    /**
2465     * Adds to this GreasedRegion with a moved set of its own "on" cells, moved to the given x and y offset.
2466     * Ignores cells that would be added out of bounds. Keeps all cells that are currently "on" unchanged.
2467     * @param x the x offset to translate by; can be negative
2468     * @param y the y offset to translate by; can be negative
2469     * @return this for chaining
2470     */
2471    public GreasedRegion insertTranslation(int x, int y)
2472    {
2473        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0 || (x == 0 && y == 0))
2474            return this;
2475        int start = Math.max(0, x), len = Math.min(width, width + x) - start,
2476                jump = (y == 0) ? 0 : (y < 0) ? -(1-y >>> 6) : (y-1 >>> 6), lily = (y < 0) ? -(-y & 63) : (y & 63),
2477                originalJump = Math.max(0, -jump), alterJump = Math.max(0, jump);
2478        long[] data2 = new long[width * ySections];
2479        long prev, tmp;
2480        if (x < 0) {
2481            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2482                for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
2483                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2484                }
2485            }
2486        } else if (x > 0) {
2487            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2488                for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
2489                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2490                }
2491            }
2492        } else {
2493            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i < ySections && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2494                for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
2495                    data2[j * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2496                }
2497            }
2498        }
2499
2500        if(lily < 0) {
2501            for (int i = start; i < len; i++) {
2502                prev = 0L;
2503                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
2504                    tmp = prev;
2505                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L << -lily)) << (64 + lily);
2506                    data2[i * ySections + j] >>>= -lily;
2507                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2508                }
2509            }
2510        }
2511        else if(lily > 0) {
2512            for (int i = start; i < start + len; i++) {
2513                prev = 0L;
2514                for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
2515                    tmp = prev;
2516                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L >>> lily)) >>> (64 - lily);
2517                    data2[i * ySections + j] <<= lily;
2518                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2519                }
2520            }
2521        }
2522
2523        for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
2524            data2[i] |= data[i];
2525        }
2526
2527
2528        if(yEndMask != -1) {
2529            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data2.length; a += ySections) {
2530                data2[a] &= yEndMask;
2531            }
2532        }
2533
2534        data = data2;
2535        tallied = false;
2536        return this;
2537    }

2539    /**
2540     * Effectively doubles the x and y values of each cell this contains (not scaling each cell to be larger, so each
2541     * "on" cell will be surrounded by "off" cells), and re-maps the positions so the given x and y in the doubled space
2542     * become 0,0 in the resulting GreasedRegion (which is this, assigning to itself).
2543     * @param x in the doubled coordinate space, the x position that should become 0 x in the result; can be negative
2544     * @param y in the doubled coordinate space, the y position that should become 0 y in the result; can be negative
2545     * @return this for chaining
2546     */
2547    public GreasedRegion zoom(int x, int y)
2548    {
2549        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0)
2550            return this;
2551        x = -x;
2552        y = -y;
2553        int
2554                width2 = width + 1 >>> 1, ySections2 = ySections + 1 >>> 1,
2555                start = Math.max(0, x), len = Math.min(width, width + x) - start,
2556                //tall = (Math.min(height, height + y) - Math.max(0, y)) + 63 >> 6,
2557                jump = (y == 0) ? 0 : (y < 0) ? -(1-y >>> 6) : (y-1 >>> 6), lily = (y < 0) ? -(-y & 63) : (y & 63),
2558                originalJump = Math.max(0, -jump), alterJump = Math.max(0, jump),
2559                oddX = (x & 1), oddY = (y & 1);
2560        long[] data2 = new long[width * ySections];
2561
2562        long prev, tmp, yEndMask2 = -1L >>> (64 - ((height + 1 >>> 1) & 63));
2563        if (x < 0) {
2564            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i <= ySections2 && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2565                for (int j = Math.max(0, -x), jj = 0; jj < len; j++, jj++) {
2566                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2567                }
2568            }
2569        } else if (x > 0) {
2570            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i <= ySections2 && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2571                for (int j = 0, jj = start; j < len; j++, jj++) {
2572                    data2[jj * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2573                }
2574            }
2575        } else {
2576            for (int i = alterJump, oi = originalJump; i <= ySections2 && oi < ySections; i++, oi++) {
2577                for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
2578                    data2[j * ySections + i] = data[j * ySections + oi];
2579                }
2580            }
2581        }
2582
2583        if(lily < 0) {
2584            for (int i = start; i < len; i++) {
2585                prev = 0L;
2586                for (int j = ySections2; j >= 0; j--) {
2587                    tmp = prev;
2588                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L << -lily)) << (64 + lily);
2589                    data2[i * ySections + j] >>>= -lily;
2590                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2591                }
2592            }
2593        }
2594        else if(lily > 0) {
2595            for (int i = start; i < start + len; i++) {
2596                prev = 0L;
2597                for (int j = 0; j < ySections2; j++) {
2598                    tmp = prev;
2599                    prev = (data2[i * ySections + j] & ~(-1L >>> lily)) >>> (64 - lily);
2600                    data2[i * ySections + j] <<= lily;
2601                    data2[i * ySections + j] |= tmp;
2602                }
2603            }
2604        }
2605
2606
2607        if(ySections2 > 0 && yEndMask2 != -1) {
2608            for (int a = ySections2 - 1; a < data2.length; a += ySections) {
2609                data2[a] &= yEndMask2;
2610                if(ySections2 < ySections)
2611                    data2[a+1] = 0L;
2612            }
2613        }
2614        for (int i = 0; i < width2; i++) {
2615            for (int j = 0; j < ySections2; j++) {
2616                prev = data2[i * ySections + j];
2617                tmp = prev >>> 32;
2618                prev &= 0xFFFFFFFFL;
2619                prev = (prev | (prev << 16)) & 0x0000FFFF0000FFFFL;
2620                prev = (prev | (prev << 8)) & 0x00FF00FF00FF00FFL;
2621                prev = (prev | (prev << 4)) & 0x0F0F0F0F0F0F0F0FL;
2622                prev = (prev | (prev << 2)) & 0x3333333333333333L;
2623                prev = (prev | (prev << 1)) & 0x5555555555555555L;
2624                prev <<= oddY;
2625                if(oddX == 1) {
2626                    if (i * 2 + 1 < width)
2627                        data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + ySections] = prev;
2628                    if (i * 2 < width)
2629                        data[(i * ySections + j) * 2] = 0L;
2630                }
2631                else
2632                {
2633                    if (i * 2 < width)
2634                        data[(i * ySections + j) * 2] = prev;
2635                    if (i * 2 + 1 < width)
2636                        data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + ySections] = 0L;
2637                }
2638                if(j * 2 + 1 < ySections) {
2639                    tmp = (tmp | (tmp << 16)) & 0x0000FFFF0000FFFFL;
2640                    tmp = (tmp | (tmp << 8)) & 0x00FF00FF00FF00FFL;
2641                    tmp = (tmp | (tmp << 4)) & 0x0F0F0F0F0F0F0F0FL;
2642                    tmp = (tmp | (tmp << 2)) & 0x3333333333333333L;
2643                    tmp = (tmp | (tmp << 1)) & 0x5555555555555555L;
2644                    tmp <<= oddY;
2645                    if(oddX == 1) {
2646                        if (i * 2 + 1 < width)
2647                            data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + ySections + 1] = tmp;
2648                        if (i * 2 < width)
2649                            data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + 1] = 0L;
2650                    }
2651                    else
2652                    {
2653                        if (i * 2 < width)
2654                            data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + 1] = tmp;
2655                        if (i * 2 + 1 < width)
2656                            data[(i * ySections + j) * 2 + ySections + 1] = 0L;
2657                    }
2658                }
2659            }
2660        }
2661
2662        if(yEndMask != -1) {
2663            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < data.length; a += ySections) {
2664                data[a] &= yEndMask;
2665            }
2666        }
2667        tallied = false;
2668        return this;
2669    }
2670
2671    /**
2672     * Takes the pairs of "on" cells in this GreasedRegion that are separated by exactly one cell in an orthogonal line,
2673     * and changes the gap cells to "on" as well.
2674     * <br>
2675     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
2676     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
2677     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
2678     * @return this for chaining
2679     */
2680    public GreasedRegion connect()
2681    {
2682        if(width < 2 || ySections == 0)
2683            return this;
2684
2685        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
2686        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
2687        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
2688            next[a] |= ((data[a] << 1) & (data[a] >>> 1)) | data[a+ySections];
2689            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= ((data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) & (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1)) | data[(width-2) *ySections+a];
2690
2691            for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2692                next[i] |= ((data[i] << 1) & (data[i] >>> 1)) | (data[i - ySections] & data[i + ySections]);
2693            }
2694
2695            if(a > 0) {
2696                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2697                    next[i] |= (data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i] >>> 1);
2698                }
2699            }
2700            else
2701            {
2702                for (int i = ySections; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2703                    next[i] |= (data[i] >>> 1 & 1L);
2704                }
2705            }
2706
2707            if(a < ySections - 1) {
2708                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2709                    next[i] |= (data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i] << 1);
2710                }
2711            }
2712            else
2713            {
2714                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2715                    next[i] |= (data[i] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L);
2716                }
2717
2718            }
2719        }
2720
2721        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2722            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
2723                next[a] &= yEndMask;
2724            }
2725        }
2726        data = next;
2727        tallied = false;
2728        return this;
2729    }
2730
2731    /**
2732     * Takes the pairs of "on" cells in this GreasedRegion that are separated by exactly one cell in an orthogonal or
2733     * diagonal line, and changes the gap cells to "on" as well.
2734     * <br>
2735     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
2736     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
2737     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
2738     * @return this for chaining
2739     */
2740    public GreasedRegion connect8way()
2741    {
2742        if(width < 2 || ySections == 0)
2743            return this;
2744
2745        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
2746        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
2747        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
2748            next[a] |= ((data[a] << 1) & (data[a] >>> 1)) | data[a+ySections] | (data[a+ySections] << 1) | (data[a+ySections] >>> 1);
2749            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= ((data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) & (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1))
2750                    | data[(width-2) *ySections+a] | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] >>> 1);
2751
2752            for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2753                next[i] |= ((data[i] << 1) & (data[i] >>> 1)) | (data[i - ySections] & data[i + ySections])
2754                        | ((data[i - ySections] << 1) & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1))
2755                        | ((data[i + ySections] << 1) & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1));
2756            }
2757
2758            if(a > 0) {
2759                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2760                    next[i] |= ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i] >>> 1)) |
2761                            ((data[i - ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1)) |
2762                            ((data[i + ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1));
2763                }
2764            }
2765            else
2766            {
2767                for (int i = ySections; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2768                    next[i] |= (data[i] >>> 1 & 1L) | (data[i - ySections] >>> 1 & 1L) | (data[i + ySections] >>> 1 & 1L);
2769                }
2770            }
2771
2772            if(a < ySections - 1) {
2773                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2774                    next[i] |= ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i] << 1)) |
2775                            ((data[i - ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i + ySections] << 1)) |
2776                            ((data[i + ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i - ySections] << 1)) ;
2777                }
2778            }
2779            else
2780            {
2781                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2782                    next[i] |= (data[i] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L)
2783                            | (data[i - ySections] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L) | (data[i + ySections] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L);
2784                }
2785
2786            }
2787        }
2788
2789        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2790            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
2791                next[a] &= yEndMask;
2792            }
2793        }
2794        data = next;
2795        tallied = false;
2796        return this;
2797    }
2798    /**
2799     * Takes the pairs of "on" cells in this GreasedRegion that are separated by exactly one cell in an orthogonal or
2800     * diagonal line, and changes the gap cells to "on" as well. As a special case, this requires diagonals to either
2801     * have no "on" cells adjacent along the perpendicular diagonal, or both cells on that perpendicular diagonal need
2802     * to be "on." This is useful to counteract some less-desirable behavior of {@link #connect8way()}, where a right
2803     * angle would always get the inner corners filled because it was considered a diagonal.
2804     * <br>
2805     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
2806     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
2807     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
2808     * @return this for chaining
2809     */
2810    public GreasedRegion connectLines()
2811    {
2812        if(width < 2 || ySections == 0)
2813            return this;
2814
2815        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
2816        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
2817        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
2818            next[a] |= ((data[a] << 1) & (data[a] >>> 1)) | data[a+ySections] | (data[a+ySections] << 1) | (data[a+ySections] >>> 1);
2819            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= ((data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) & (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1))
2820                    | data[(width-2) *ySections+a] | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] >>> 1);
2821
2822            for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2823                next[i] |= ((data[i] << 1) & (data[i] >>> 1)) | (data[i - ySections] & data[i + ySections])
2824                        | (((data[i - ySections] << 1) & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1))
2825                           ^ ((data[i + ySections] << 1) & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)));
2826            }
2827
2828            if(a > 0) {
2829                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2830                    next[i] |= ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i] >>> 1))
2831                            | (((data[i - ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1))
2832                               ^ ((data[i + ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63 & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)));
2833                }
2834            }
2835            else
2836            {
2837                for (int i = ySections; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2838                    next[i] |= (data[i] >>> 1 & 1L) | (data[i - ySections] >>> 1 & 1L) | (data[i + ySections] >>> 1 & 1L);
2839                }
2840            }
2841
2842            if(a < ySections - 1) {
2843                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2844                    next[i] |= ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i] << 1))
2845                            | (((data[i - ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i + ySections] << 1))
2846                               ^ ((data[i + ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63 & (data[i - ySections] << 1)));
2847                }
2848            }
2849            else
2850            {
2851                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
2852                    next[i] |= (data[i] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L)
2853                            | (data[i - ySections] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L) | (data[i + ySections] << 1 & 0x8000000000000000L);
2854                }
2855
2856            }
2857        }
2858
2859        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
2860            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
2861                next[a] &= yEndMask;
2862            }
2863        }
2864        data = next;
2865        tallied = false;
2866        return this;
2867    }
2868
2869    /**
2870     * Like {@link #retract()}, this reduces the width of thick areas of this GreasedRegion, but thin() will not remove
2871     * areas that would be identical in a subsequent call to retract(), such as if the area would be eliminated. This
2872     * is useful primarily for adjusting areas so they do not exceed a width of 2 cells, though their length (the longer
2873     * of the two dimensions) will be unaffected by this. Especially wide, irregularly-shaped areas may have unintended
2874     * appearances if you call this repeatedly or use {@link #thinFully()}; consider using this sparingly, or primarily
2875     * when an area has just gotten thicker than desired.
2876     * <br>
2877     * This currently uses 4-way adjacency, but had previously used 8-way; if you want the behavior this previously had,
2878     * you can use {@link #thin8way()}, but it may be a good idea to try this method as well (some of the old behavior
2879     * had problems where it yielded significantly larger minimum widths in some areas).
2880     * @return this for chaining
2881     */
2882    public GreasedRegion thin()
2883    {
2884        if(width <= 2 || ySections <= 0)
2885            return this;
2886        GreasedRegion c1 = new GreasedRegion(this).retract(),
2887                c2 = new GreasedRegion(c1).expand().xor(this).expand().and(this);
2888        remake(c1).or(c2);
2889        /*
2890        System.out.println("\n\nc1:\n" + c1.toString() + "\n");
2891        System.out.println("\n\nc2:\n" + c2.toString() + "\n");
2892        System.out.println("\n\nthis:\n" + toString() + "\n");
2893        */
2894        return this;
2895    }
2896
2897    /**
2898     * Calls {@link #thin()} repeatedly, until the result is unchanged from the last call. Consider using the idiom
2899     * {@code expand8way().retract().thinFully()} to help change a possibly-strange appearance when the GreasedRegion
2900     * this is called on touches the edges of the grid. In general, this method is likely to go too far when it tries to
2901     * thin a round or irregular area, and this often results in many diagonal lines spanning the formerly-thick area.
2902     * <br>
2903     * This currently uses 4-way adjacency, but had previously used 8-way; if you want the behavior this previously had,
2904     * you can use {@link #thinFully8way()}, but it may be a good idea to try this method as well (some of the old
2905     * behavior had problems where it yielded significantly larger minimum widths in some areas).
2906     * @return this for chaining
2907     */
2908    public GreasedRegion thinFully()
2909    {
2910        while (size() != thin().size());
2911        return this;
2912    }

2915    /**
2916     * Like {@link #retract8way()}, this reduces the width of thick areas of this GreasedRegion, but thin8way() will not
2917     * remove areas that would be identical in a subsequent call to retract8way(), such as if the area would be
2918     * eliminated. This is useful primarily for adjusting areas so they do not exceed a width of 2 cells, though their
2919     * length (the longer of the two dimensions) will be unaffected by this. Especially wide, irregularly-shaped areas
2920     * may have unintended appearances if you call this repeatedly or use {@link #thinFully8way()}; consider using this
2921     * sparingly, or primarily when an area has just gotten thicker than desired.
2922     * <br>
2923     * This method was called {@link #thin()}, but now that name refers to a variant that uses 4-way adjacency.
2924     * @return this for chaining
2925     */
2926    public GreasedRegion thin8way()
2927    {
2928        if(width <= 2 || ySections <= 0)
2929            return this;
2930        GreasedRegion c1 = new GreasedRegion(this).retract8way(),
2931                c2 = new GreasedRegion(c1).expand8way().xor(this).expand8way().and(this);
2932        remake(c1).or(c2);
2933        return this;
2934    }

2936    /**
2937     * Calls {@link #thin8way()} repeatedly, until the result is unchanged from the last call. Consider using the idiom
2938     * {@code expand8way().retract().thinFully8way()} to help change a strange appearance when the GreasedRegion this is
2939     * called on touches the edges of the grid. In general, this method is likely to go too far when it tries to thin a
2940     * round or irregular area, and this often results in many diagonal lines spanning the formerly-thick area.
2941     * <br>
2942     * This method was called {@link #thinFully()}, but now that name refers to a variant that uses 4-way adjacency.
2943     * @return this for chaining
2944     */
2945    public GreasedRegion thinFully8way()
2946    {
2947        while (size() != thin8way().size());
2948        return this;
2949    }

2951
2952    /**
2953     * Removes "on" cells that are orthogonally adjacent to other "on" cells, keeping at least one cell in a group "on."
2954     * Uses a "checkerboard" pattern to determine which cells to turn  off, with all cells that would be black on a
2955     * checkerboard turned off and all others kept as-is.
2956     * @return this for chaining
2957     */
2958    public GreasedRegion disperse()
2959    {
2960        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0)
2961            return this;
2962        long mask = 0x5555555555555555L;
2963        for (int i = 0; i < width; i++) {
2964            for (int j = 0; j < ySections; j++) {
2965                data[j] &= mask;
2966            }
2967            mask = ~mask;
2968        }
2969        tallied = false;
2970        return this;
2971    }
2972    /**
2973     * Removes "on" cells that are 8-way adjacent to other "on" cells, keeping at least one cell in a group "on."
2974     * Uses a "grid-like" pattern to determine which cells to turn off, with all cells with even x and even y kept as-is
2975     * but all other cells (with either or both odd x or odd y) turned off.
2976     * @return this for chaining
2977     */
2978    public GreasedRegion disperse8way()
2979    {
2980        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0)
2981            return this;
2982        int len = data.length;
2983        long mask = 0x5555555555555555L;
2984        for (int j = 0; j < len - 1; j += 2) {
2985            data[j] &= mask;
2986            data[j+1] = 0;
2987        }
2988        tallied = false;
2989        return this;
2990    }
2991    /**
2992     * Removes "on" cells that are nearby other "on" cells, with a random factor to which bits are actually turned off
2993     * that still ensures exactly half of the bits are kept as-is (the one exception is when height is an odd number,
2994     * which makes the bottom row slightly random).
2995     * @param random the RNG used for a random factor
2996     * @return this for chaining
2997     */
2998    public GreasedRegion disperseRandom(RandomnessSource random)
2999    {
3000        if(width < 1 || ySections <= 0)
3001            return this;
3002        int len = data.length;
3003        for (int j = 0; j < len; j++) {
3004            data[j] &= randomInterleave(random);
3005        }
3006        tallied = false;
3007        return this;
3008    }
3009    /**
3010     * Generates a random 64-bit long with a number of '1' bits (Hamming weight) equal on average to bitCount.
3011     * For example, calling this with a parameter of 32 will be equivalent to calling nextLong() on the given
3012     * RandomnessSource, which could be an {@link RNG} or any RandomnessSource with good 64-bit generation quality.
3013     * Calling this with a parameter of 16 will have on average 16 of the 64 bits in the returned long set to '1',
3014     * distributed pseudo-randomly, while a parameter of 47 will have on average 47 bits set. This can be useful for
3015     * certain code that uses bits to represent data but needs a different ratio of set bits to unset bits than 1:1.
3016     * <br>
3017     * The parameter {@code random} can be an object like a {@link LinnormRNG}, an {@link RNG} backed by a
3018     * well-distributed RandomnessSource like its default, LinnormRNG, a {@link GWTRNG} (especially if you target GWT,
3019     * where it will perform much better than most alternatives), or any of various other RandomnessSource
3020     * implementations that distribute bits well for {@link RandomnessSource#nextLong()}, but should not be
3021     * intentionally-biased RNGs like {@link DharmaRNG} or {@link EditRNG}, nor double-based QRNGs like
3022     * {@link VanDerCorputQRNG} or {@link SobolQRNG}.
3023     * @param random used to determine random factors; likely to be an {@link RNG}, {@link LinnormRNG}, or {@link GWTRNG}
3024     * @param bitCount an int, only considered if between 0 and 64, that is the average number of bits to set
3025     * @return a 64-bit long that, on average, should have bitCount bits set to 1, potentially anywhere in the long
3026     */
3027    public static long approximateBits(RandomnessSource random, int bitCount) {
3028        if (bitCount <= 0)
3029            return 0L;
3030        if (bitCount >= 64)
3031            return -1L;
3032        if (bitCount == 32)
3033            return random.nextLong();
3034        boolean high = bitCount > 32;
3035        int altered = (high ? 64 - bitCount : bitCount), lsb = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(altered);
3036        long data = random.nextLong();
3037        for (int i = lsb << 1; i <= 16; i <<= 1) {
3038            if ((altered & i) == 0)
3039                data &= random.nextLong();
3040            else
3041                data |= random.nextLong();
3042        }
3043        return high ? ~(random.nextLong() & data) : (random.nextLong() & data);
3044    }
3045
3046    /**
3047     * Gets a somewhat-random long with exactly 32 bits set; in each pair of bits starting at bit 0 and bit 1, then bit
3048     * 2 and bit 3, up to bit 62 and bit 3, one bit will be 1 and one bit will be 0 in each pair.
3049     * <br>
3050     * Not exactly general-use; meant for generating data for GreasedRegion.
3051     * @return a random long with 32 "1" bits, distributed so exactly one bit is "1" for each pair of bits
3052     */
3053    public static long randomInterleave(RandomnessSource random) {
3054        long bits = random.nextLong() & 0xFFFFFFFFL, ib = ~bits & 0xFFFFFFFFL;
3055        bits |= (bits << 16);
3056        ib |= (ib << 16);
3057        bits &= 0x0000FFFF0000FFFFL;
3058        ib &= 0x0000FFFF0000FFFFL;
3059        bits |= (bits << 8);
3060        ib |= (ib << 8);
3061        bits &= 0x00FF00FF00FF00FFL;
3062        ib &= 0x00FF00FF00FF00FFL;
3063        bits |= (bits << 4);
3064        ib |= (ib << 4);
3065        bits &= 0x0F0F0F0F0F0F0F0FL;
3066        ib &= 0x0F0F0F0F0F0F0F0FL;
3067        bits |= (bits << 2);
3068        ib |= (ib << 2);
3069        bits &= 0x3333333333333333L;
3070        ib &= 0x3333333333333333L;
3071        bits |= (bits << 1);
3072        ib |= (ib << 1);
3073        bits &= 0x5555555555555555L;
3074        ib &= 0x5555555555555555L;
3075        return (bits | (ib << 1));
3076    }

3078    /**
3079     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and expands them by one cell in the 4 orthogonal directions, making
3080     * each "on" cell take up a plus-shaped area that may overlap with other "on" cells (which is just a normal "on"
3081     * cell then).
3082     * <br>
3083     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3084     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3085     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
3086     * @return this for chaining
3087     */
3088    public GreasedRegion expand()
3089    {
3090        if(width < 2 || ySections == 0)
3091            return this;
3092
3093        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3094        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
3095        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
3096            next[a] |= (data[a] << 1) | (data[a] >>> 1) | data[a+ySections];
3097            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1) | data[(width-2) *ySections+a];
3098
3099            for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3100                next[i] |= (data[i] << 1) | (data[i] >>> 1) | data[i - ySections] | data[i + ySections];
3101            }
3102
3103            if(a > 0) {
3104                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3105                    next[i] |= (data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63;
3106                }
3107            }
3108
3109            if(a < ySections - 1) {
3110                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3111                    next[i] |= (data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63;
3112                }
3113            }
3114        }
3115
3116        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
3117            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3118                next[a] &= yEndMask;
3119            }
3120        }
3121        data = next;
3122        tallied = false;
3123        return this;
3124    }
3125    /**
3126     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and expands them by amount cells in the 4 orthogonal directions,
3127     * making each "on" cell take up a plus-shaped area that may overlap with other "on" cells (which is just a normal
3128     * "on" cell then).
3129     * <br>
3130     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3131     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3132     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
3133     * @return this for chaining
3134     */
3135    @Override
3136    public GreasedRegion expand(int amount)
3137    {
3138        for (int i = 0; i < amount; i++) {
3139            expand();
3140        }
3141        return this;
3142    }
3143    /**
3144     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and produces amount GreasedRegions, each one expanded by 1 cell in
3145     * the 4 orthogonal directions relative to the previous GreasedRegion, making each "on" cell take up a plus-shaped
3146     * area that may overlap with other "on" cells (which is just a normal "on" cell then). This returns an array of
3147     * GreasedRegions with progressively greater expansions, and does not modify this GreasedRegion.
3148     * <br>
3149     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3150     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3151     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
3152     * @return an array of new GreasedRegions, length == amount, where each one is expanded by 1 relative to the last
3153     */
3154    public GreasedRegion[] expandSeries(int amount)
3155    {
3156        if(amount <= 0) return new GreasedRegion[0];
3157        GreasedRegion[] regions = new GreasedRegion[amount];
3158        GreasedRegion temp = new GreasedRegion(this);
3159        for (int i = 0; i < amount; i++) {
3160            regions[i] = new GreasedRegion(temp.expand());
3161        }
3162        return regions;
3163    }

3174    /**
3175     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and expands them by one cell in the 4 orthogonal directions, producing
3176     * a diamoond shape, then removes the original area before expansion, producing only the cells that were "off" in
3177     * this and within 1 cell (orthogonal-only) of an "on" cell. This method is similar to {@link #surface()}, but
3178     * surface finds cells inside the current GreasedRegion, while fringe finds cells outside it.
3179     * <br>
3180     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3181     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3182     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time. The surface and fringe methods do allocate one
3183     * temporary GreasedRegion to store the original before modification, but the others generally don't.
3184     * @return this for chaining
3185     */
3186    public GreasedRegion fringe()
3187    {
3188        GreasedRegion cpy = new GreasedRegion(this);
3189        expand();
3190        return andNot(cpy);
3191    }
3192    /**
3193     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and expands them by amount cells in the 4 orthogonal directions
3194     * (iteratively, producing a diamond shape), then removes the original area before expansion, producing only the
3195     * cells that were "off" in this and within amount cells (orthogonal-only) of an "on" cell. This method is similar
3196     * to {@link #surface()}, but surface finds cells inside the current GreasedRegion, while fringe finds cells outside
3197     * it.
3198     * <br>
3199     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3200     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3201     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time. The surface and fringe methods do allocate one
3202     * temporary GreasedRegion to store the original before modification, but the others generally don't.
3203     * @return this for chaining
3204     */
3205
3206    public GreasedRegion fringe(int amount)
3207    {
3208        GreasedRegion cpy = new GreasedRegion(this);
3209        expand(amount);
3210        return andNot(cpy);
3211    }

3213    /**
3214     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and produces amount GreasedRegions, each one expanded by 1 cell in
3215     * the 4 orthogonal directions relative to the previous GreasedRegion, making each "on" cell take up a diamond-
3216     * shaped area. After producing the expansions, this removes the previous GreasedRegion from the next GreasedRegion
3217     * in the array, making each "fringe" in the series have 1 "thickness," which can be useful for finding which layer
3218     * of expansion a cell lies in. This returns an array of GreasedRegions with progressively greater expansions
3219     * without the cells of this GreasedRegion, and does not modify this GreasedRegion.
3220     * <br>
3221     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3222     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3223     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
3224     * @return an array of new GreasedRegions, length == amount, where each one is a 1-depth fringe pushed further out from this
3225     */
3226    public GreasedRegion[] fringeSeries(int amount)
3227    {
3228        if(amount <= 0) return new GreasedRegion[0];
3229        GreasedRegion[] regions = new GreasedRegion[amount];
3230        GreasedRegion temp = new GreasedRegion(this);
3231        regions[0] = new GreasedRegion(temp);
3232        for (int i = 1; i < amount; i++) {
3233            regions[i] = new GreasedRegion(temp.expand());
3234        }
3235        for (int i = 0; i < amount - 1; i++) {
3236            regions[i].xor(regions[i + 1]);
3237        }
3238        regions[amount - 1].fringe();
3239        return regions;
3240    }
3241    public ArrayList<GreasedRegion> fringeSeriesToLimit()
3242    {
3243        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> regions = expandSeriesToLimit();
3244        for (int i = regions.size() - 1; i > 0; i--) {
3245            regions.get(i).xor(regions.get(i-1));
3246        }
3247        regions.get(0).xor(this);
3248        return regions;
3249    }
3250
3251    /**
3252     * Takes the "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and retracts them by one cell in the 4 orthogonal directions,
3253     * making each "on" cell that was orthogonally adjacent to an "off" cell into an "off" cell.
3254     * <br>
3255     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3256     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3257     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
3258     * @return this for chaining
3259     */
3260    public GreasedRegion retract()
3261    {
3262        if(width <= 2 || ySections <= 0)
3263            return this;
3264
3265        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3266        System.arraycopy(data, ySections, next, ySections, (width - 2) * ySections);
3267        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
3268            if(a > 0 && a < ySections - 1) {
3269                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3270                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3271                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63))
3272                            & data[i - ySections]
3273                            & data[i + ySections];
3274                }
3275            }
3276            else if(a > 0) {
3277                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3278                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3279                            & (data[i] >>> 1)
3280                            & data[i - ySections]
3281                            & data[i + ySections];
3282                }
3283            }
3284            else if(a < ySections - 1) {
3285                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3286                    next[i] &= (data[i] << 1)
3287                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63))
3288                            & data[i - ySections]
3289                            & data[i + ySections];
3290                }
3291            }
3292            else // only the case when ySections == 1
3293            {
3294                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3295                    next[i] &= (data[i] << 1) & (data[i] >>> 1) & data[i - ySections] & data[i + ySections];
3296                }
3297            }
3298        }
3299
3300        if(yEndMask != -1) {
3301            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3302                next[a] &= yEndMask;
3303            }
3304        }
3305        data = next;
3306        tallied = false;
3307        return this;
3308    }

3312     * this iteeratively amount times, making each "on" cell that was within amount orthogonal distance to an "off" cell
3313     * into an "off" cell.
3314     * <br>
3315     * This method is very efficient due to how the class is implemented, and the various spatial increase/decrease
3316     * methods (including {@link #expand()}, {@link #retract()}, {@link #fringe()}, and {@link #surface()}) all perform
3317     * very well by operating in bulk on up to 64 cells at a time.
3318     * @return this for chaining
3319     */
3320    public GreasedRegion retract(int amount)
3321    {
3322        for (int i = 0; i < amount; i++) {
3323            retract();
3324        }
3325        return this;
