3366        for (int i = 1; i < amount; i++) {
3367            regions[i] = new GreasedRegion(temp.retract());
3368        }

3376    public ArrayList<GreasedRegion> surfaceSeriesToLimit()
3377    {
3378        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> regions = retractSeriesToLimit();
3379        if(regions.isEmpty())
3380            return regions;
3381        regions.add(0, regions.get(0).copy().xor(this));
3382        for (int i = 1; i < regions.size() - 1; i++) {
3383            regions.get(i).xor(regions.get(i+1));
3384        }
3385        return regions;

3387    public GreasedRegion expand8way()
3388    {
3389        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0)
3390            return this;
3391
3392        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3393        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
3394        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
3395            next[a] |= (data[a] << 1) | (data[a] >>> 1)
3396                    | data[a+ySections] | (data[a+ySections] << 1) | (data[a+ySections] >>> 1);
3397            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1)
3398                    | data[(width-2) *ySections+a] | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] >>> 1);
3399
3400            for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3401                next[i] |= (data[i] << 1) | (data[i] >>> 1)
3402                        | data[i - ySections] | (data[i - ySections] << 1) | (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)
3403                        | data[i + ySections] | (data[i + ySections] << 1) | (data[i + ySections] >>> 1);
3404            }
3405
3406            if(a > 0) {
3407                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3408                    next[i] |= ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63) |
3409                            ((data[i - ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63) |
3410                            ((data[i + ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63);
3411                }
3412            }
3413
3414            if(a < ySections - 1) {
3415                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3416                    next[i] |= ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63) |
3417                            ((data[i - ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63) |
3418                            ((data[i + ySections+ 1] & 1L) << 63);
3419                }
3420            }
3421        }
3422
3423        if(ySections > 0 && yEndMask != -1) {
3424            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3425                next[a] &= yEndMask;
3426            }
3427        }
3428        data = next;
3429        tallied = false;
3430        return this;
3431    }

3500    public GreasedRegion retract8way()
3501    {
3502        if(width <= 2 || ySections <= 0)
3503            return this;
3504
3505        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3506        System.arraycopy(data, ySections, next, ySections, (width - 2) * ySections);
3507        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
3508            if(a > 0 && a < ySections - 1) {
3509                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3510                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3511                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63))
3512                            & data[i - ySections]
3513                            & data[i + ySections]
3514                            & ((data[i - ySections] << 1) | ((data[i - 1 - ySections] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3515                            & ((data[i + ySections] << 1) | ((data[i - 1 + ySections] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3516                            & ((data[i - ySections] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1 - ySections] & 1L) << 63))
3517                            & ((data[i + ySections] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1 + ySections] & 1L) << 63));
3518                }
3519            }
3520            else if(a > 0) {
3521                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3522                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3523                            & (data[i] >>> 1)
3524                            & data[i - ySections]
3525                            & data[i + ySections]
3526                            & ((data[i - ySections] << 1) | ((data[i - 1 - ySections] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3527                            & ((data[i + ySections] << 1) | ((data[i - 1 + ySections] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3528                            & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)
3529                            & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1);
3530                }
3531            }
3532            else if(a < ySections - 1) {
3533                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3534                    next[i] &= (data[i] << 1)
3535                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63))
3536                            & data[i - ySections]
3537                            & data[i + ySections]
3538                            & (data[i - ySections] << 1)
3539                            & (data[i + ySections] << 1)
3540                            & ((data[i - ySections] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1 - ySections] & 1L) << 63))
3541                            & ((data[i + ySections] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1 + ySections] & 1L) << 63));
3542                }
3543            }
3544            else // only the case when ySections == 1
3545            {
3546                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3547                    next[i] &= (data[i] << 1)
3548                            & (data[i] >>> 1)
3549                            & data[i - ySections]
3550                            & data[i + ySections]
3551                            & (data[i - ySections] << 1)
3552                            & (data[i + ySections] << 1)
3553                            & (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)
3554                            & (data[i + ySections] >>> 1);
3555                }
3556            }
3557        }
3558
3559        if(yEndMask != -1) {
3560            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3561                next[a] &= yEndMask;
3562            }
3563        }
3564        data = next;
3565        tallied = false;
3566        return this;
3567    }

3610    public GreasedRegion[] surfaceSeries8way(int amount)
3611    {
3612        if(amount <= 0) return new GreasedRegion[0];
3613        GreasedRegion[] regions = new GreasedRegion[amount];
3614        GreasedRegion temp = new GreasedRegion(this);
3615        regions[0] = new GreasedRegion(temp);
3616        for (int i = 1; i < amount; i++) {
3617            regions[i] = new GreasedRegion(temp.retract8way());
3618        }
3619        for (int i = 0; i < amount - 1; i++) {
3620            regions[i].xor(regions[i + 1]);
3621        }
3622        regions[amount - 1].surface8way();
3623        return regions;
3624    }
3625    public ArrayList<GreasedRegion> surfaceSeriesToLimit8way()
3626    {
3627        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> regions = retractSeriesToLimit8way();
3628        if(regions.isEmpty())
3629            return regions;
3630        regions.add(0, regions.get(0).copy().xor(this));
3631        for (int i = 1; i < regions.size() - 1; i++) {
3632            regions.get(i).xor(regions.get(i+1));
3633        }
3634        return regions;
3635    }
3636    public GreasedRegion flood(GreasedRegion bounds)
3637    {
3638        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0 || bounds == null || bounds.width < 2 || bounds.ySections <= 0)
3639            return this;
3640
3641        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3642        for (int a = 0; a < ySections && a < bounds.ySections; a++) {
3643            next[a] |= (data[a] |(data[a] << 1) | (data[a] >>> 1) | data[a+ySections]) & bounds.data[a];
3644            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1)
3645                    | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1) | data[(width-2) *ySections+a]) & bounds.data[(width-1)*bounds.ySections+a];
3646
3647            for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections &&
3648                    j < (bounds.width - 1) * bounds.ySections; i+= ySections, j+= bounds.ySections) {
3649                next[i] |= (data[i] | (data[i] << 1) | (data[i] >>> 1) | data[i - ySections] | data[i + ySections]) & bounds.data[j];
3650            }
3651
3652            if(a > 0) {
3653                for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections && j < (bounds.width-1) * bounds.ySections;
3654                     i+= ySections, j += bounds.ySections) {
3655                    next[i] |= (data[i] | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63)) & bounds.data[j];
3656                }
3657            }
3658
3659            if(a < ySections - 1 && a < bounds.ySections - 1) {
3660                for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a;
3661                     i < (width-1) * ySections && j < (bounds.width-1) * bounds.ySections; i+= ySections, j += bounds.ySections) {
3662                    next[i] |= (data[i] | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63)) & bounds.data[j];
3663                }
3664            }
3665        }
3666
3667        if(yEndMask != -1 && bounds.yEndMask != -1) {
3668            if(ySections == bounds.ySections) {
3669                long mask = ((yEndMask >>> 1) <= (bounds.yEndMask >>> 1))
3670                        ? yEndMask : bounds.yEndMask;
3671                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3672                    next[a] &= mask;
3673                }
3674            }
3675            else if(ySections < bounds.ySections) {
3676                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3677                    next[a] &= yEndMask;
3678                }
3679            }
3680            else {
3681                for (int a = bounds.ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3682                    next[a] &= bounds.yEndMask;
3683                }
3684            }
3685        }
3686        data = next;
3687        tallied = false;
3688        return this;
3689    }
3690

3692    {
3693        int ct = size(), ct2;
3694        for (int i = 0; i < amount; i++) {
3695            flood(bounds);
3696            if(ct == (ct2 = size()))
3697                break;
3698            else
3699                ct = ct2;
3700
3701        }
3702        return this;
3703    }

3719                if (ct == (ct2 = temp.size()))

3721                else

3723            }
3724        }

3743    public GreasedRegion flood8way(GreasedRegion bounds)
3744    {
3745        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0 || bounds == null || bounds.width < 2 || bounds.ySections <= 0)
3746            return this;
3747
3748        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3749        for (int a = 0; a < ySections && a < bounds.ySections; a++) {
3750            next[a] |= (data[a] | (data[a] << 1) | (data[a] >>> 1)
3751                    | data[a+ySections] | (data[a+ySections] << 1) | (data[a+ySections] >>> 1)) & bounds.data[a];
3752            next[(width-1)*ySections+a] |= (data[(width-1)*ySections+a]
3753                    | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-1)*ySections+a] >>> 1)
3754                    | data[(width-2) *ySections+a] | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] << 1) | (data[(width-2)*ySections+a] >>> 1))
3755                    & bounds.data[(width-1)*bounds.ySections+a];
3756
3757            for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections &&
3758                    j < (bounds.width - 1) * bounds.ySections; i+= ySections, j+= bounds.ySections) {
3759                next[i] |= (data[i] | (data[i] << 1) | (data[i] >>> 1)
3760                        | data[i - ySections] | (data[i - ySections] << 1) | (data[i - ySections] >>> 1)
3761                        | data[i + ySections] | (data[i + ySections] << 1) | (data[i + ySections] >>> 1))
3762                        & bounds.data[j];
3763            }
3764
3765            if(a > 0) {
3766                for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a; i < (width-1) * ySections && j < (bounds.width-1) * bounds.ySections;
3767                     i+= ySections, j += bounds.ySections) {
3768                    next[i] |= (data[i] | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63) |
3769                            ((data[i - ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63) |
3770                            ((data[i + ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63)) & bounds.data[j];
3771                }
3772            }
3773
3774            if(a < ySections - 1 && a < bounds.ySections - 1) {
3775                for (int i = ySections+a, j = bounds.ySections+a;
3776                     i < (width-1) * ySections && j < (bounds.width-1) * bounds.ySections; i+= ySections, j += bounds.ySections) {
3777                    next[i] |= (data[i] | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63) |
3778                            ((data[i - ySections + 1] & 1L) << 63) |
3779                            ((data[i + ySections+ 1] & 1L) << 63)) & bounds.data[j];
3780                }
3781            }
3782        }
3783
3784        if(yEndMask != -1 && bounds.yEndMask != -1) {
3785            if(ySections == bounds.ySections) {
3786                long mask = ((yEndMask >>> 1) <= (bounds.yEndMask >>> 1))
3787                        ? yEndMask : bounds.yEndMask;
3788                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3789                    next[a] &= mask;
3790                }
3791            }
3792            else if(ySections < bounds.ySections) {
3793                for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3794                    next[a] &= yEndMask;
3795                }
3796            }
3797            else {
3798                for (int a = bounds.ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3799                    next[a] &= bounds.yEndMask;
3800                }
3801            }
3802        }
3803        data = next;
3804        tallied = false;
3805        return this;
3806    }

3856    public GreasedRegion spill(GreasedRegion bounds, int volume, IRNG rng)
3857    {
3858        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0 || bounds == null || bounds.width < 2 || bounds.ySections <= 0)
3859            return this;
3860        int current = size();
3861        if(current >= volume)
3862            return this;
3863        GreasedRegion t = new GreasedRegion(this).notAnd(bounds);
3864        long[] b2 = new long[t.data.length];
3865        System.arraycopy(t.data, 0, b2, 0, b2.length);
3866        t.remake(this).fringe().and(bounds).tally();
3867        if(t.ct <= 0)
3868            return this;
3869        Coord c;
3870        int x, y, p;
3871        for (int i = current; i < volume; i++) {
3872            c = t.singleRandom(rng);
3873            x = c.x;
3874            y = c.y;
3875            if(data[p = x * ySections + (y >> 6)] != (data[p] |= 1L << (y & 63)))
3876            {
3877                counts[p]++;
3878                for (int j = p+1; j < data.length; j++) {
3879                    if(counts[j] > 0) ++counts[j];
3880                }
3881                ct++;
3882                t.data[p] &= ~(1L << (y & 63));
3883//                b2[p] &= ~(1L << (y & 63));
3884                if(x < width - 1 && (b2[p = (x+1) * ySections + (y >> 6)] & 1L << (y & 63)) != 0)
3885                {
3886                    t.data[p] |= 1L << (y & 63);
3887                }
3888                if(y < height - 1 && (b2[p = x * ySections + (y+1 >> 6)] & 1L << (y+1 & 63)) != 0)
3889                {
3890                    t.data[p] |= 1L << (y+1 & 63);
3891                }
3892                if(y > 0 && (b2[p = x * ySections + (y-1 >> 6)] & 1L << (y-1 & 63)) != 0)
3893                {
3894                    t.data[p] |= 1L << (y-1 & 63);
3895                }
3896                if(x > 0 && (b2[p = (x-1) * ySections + (y >> 6)] & 1L << (y & 63)) != 0)
3897                {
3898
3899                    t.data[p] |= 1L << (y & 63);
3900                }
3901                t.tally();
3902                if(t.ct <= 0) break;
3903            }
3904            else
3905                break;
3906        }
3907        tallied = false;
3908        return this;
3909    }
3910
3911    public GreasedRegion removeCorners()
3912    {
3913        if(width <= 2 || ySections <= 0)
3914            return this;
3915
3916        final long[] next = new long[width * ySections];
3917        System.arraycopy(data, 0, next, 0, width * ySections);
3918        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
3919            if(a > 0 && a < ySections - 1) {
3920                next[a] &= (((data[a] << 1) | ((data[a - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3921                        & ((data[a] >>> 1) | ((data[a + 1] & 1L) << 63)));
3922                next[(width - 1) * ySections + a] &= (((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] << 1)
3923                        | ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3924                        & ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] >>> 1)
3925                        | ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a + 1] & 1L) << 63)));
3926                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3927                    next[i] &= (((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3928                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63)))
3929                            | (data[i - ySections]
3930                            & data[i + ySections]);
3931                }
3932            }
3933            else if(a > 0) {
3934                next[a] &= (((data[a] << 1) | ((data[a - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3935                        & (data[a] >>> 1));
3936                next[(width - 1) * ySections + a] &= (((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] << 1)
3937                        | ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3938                        & (data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] >>> 1));
3939                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3940                    next[i] &= (((data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63))
3941                            & (data[i] >>> 1))
3942                            | (data[i - ySections]
3943                            & data[i + ySections]);
3944                }
3945            }
3946            else if(a < ySections - 1) {
3947                next[a] &= ((data[a] << 1)
3948                        & ((data[a] >>> 1)
3949                        | ((data[a + 1] & 1L) << 63)));
3950                next[(width - 1) * ySections + a] &= ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] << 1)
3951                        & ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a] >>> 1)
3952                        | ((data[(width - 1) * ySections + a + 1] & 1L) << 63)));
3953                for (int i = ySections+a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
3954                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1)
3955                            & ((data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63)))
3956                            | (data[i - ySections]
3957                            & data[i + ySections]);
3958                }
3959            }
3960            else // only the case when ySections == 1
3961            {
3962                next[0] &= (data[0] << 1) & (data[0] >>> 1);
3963                next[width-1] &= (data[width-1] << 1) & (data[width-1] >>> 1);
3964                for (int i = 1+a; i < (width - 1); i++) {
3965                    next[i] &= ((data[i] << 1) & (data[i] >>> 1)) | (data[i - ySections] & data[i + ySections]);
3966                }
3967            }
3968        }
3969
3970        if(yEndMask != -1) {
3971            for (int a = ySections - 1; a < next.length; a += ySections) {
3972                next[a] &= yEndMask;
3973            }
3974        }
3975        data = next;
3976        tallied = false;
3977        return this;
3978    }
3979
3980    /**
3981     * If this GreasedRegion stores multiple unconnected "on" areas, this finds each isolated area (areas that
3982     * are only adjacent diagonally are considered separate from each other) and returns it as an element in an
3983     * ArrayList of GreasedRegion, with one GreasedRegion per isolated area. Not to be confused with
3984     * {@link #split8way()}, which considers diagonally-adjacent cells as part of one region, while this method requires
3985     * cells to be orthogonally adjacent.
3986     * <br>
3987     * Useful when you have, for example, all the rooms in a dungeon with their connecting corridors removed, but want
3988     * to separate the rooms. You can get the aforementioned data assuming a bare dungeon called map using:
3989     * <br>
3990     * {@code GreasedRegion floors = new GreasedRegion(map, '.'),
3991     * rooms = floors.copy().retract8way().flood(floors, 2),
3992     * corridors = floors.copy().andNot(rooms),
3993     * doors = rooms.copy().and(corridors.copy().fringe());}
3994     * <br>
3995     * You can then get all rooms as separate regions with {@code List<GreasedRegion> apart = split(rooms);}, or
3996     * substitute {@code split(corridors)} to get the corridors. The room-finding technique works by shrinking floors
3997     * by a radius of 1 (8-way), which causes thin areas like corridors of 2 or less width to be removed, then
3998     * flood-filling the floors out from the area that produces by 2 cells (4-way this time) to restore the original
3999     * size of non-corridor areas (plus some extra to ensure odd shapes are kept). Corridors are obtained by removing
4000     * the rooms from floors. The example code also gets the doors (which overlap with rooms, not corridors) by finding
4001     * where the a room and a corridor are adjacent. This technique is used with some enhancements in the RoomFinder
4002     * class.
4003     * @see squidpony.squidgrid.mapping.RoomFinder for a class that uses this technique without exposing GreasedRegion
4004     * @return an ArrayList containing each unconnected area from packed as a GreasedRegion element
4005     */
4006    public ArrayList<GreasedRegion> split()
4007    {
4008        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> scattered = new ArrayList<>(32);
4009        int fst = firstTight();
4010        GreasedRegion remaining = new GreasedRegion(this);
4011        while (fst >= 0) {
4012            GreasedRegion filled = new GreasedRegion(width, height).insert(fst).flood(remaining, width * height);
4013            scattered.add(filled);
4014            remaining.andNot(filled);
4015            fst = remaining.firstTight();
4016        }
4017        return scattered;
4018    }
4019    /**
4020     * If this GreasedRegion stores multiple unconnected "on" areas, this finds each isolated area (areas that
4021     * are only adjacent diagonally are considered <b>one area</b> with this) and returns it as an element in an
4022     * ArrayList of GreasedRegion, with one GreasedRegion per isolated area. This should not be confused with
4023     * {@link #split()}, which is almost identical except that split() considers only orthogonal connections, while this
4024     * method considers both orthogonal and diagonal connections between cells as joining an area.
4025     * <br>
4026     * Useful when you have, for example, all the rooms in a dungeon with their connecting corridors removed, but want
4027     * to separate the rooms. You can get the aforementioned data assuming a bare dungeon called map using:
4028     * <br>
4029     * {@code GreasedRegion floors = new GreasedRegion(map, '.'),
4030     * rooms = floors.copy().retract8way().flood(floors, 2),
4031     * corridors = floors.copy().andNot(rooms),
4032     * doors = rooms.copy().and(corridors.copy().fringe());}
4033     * <br>
4034     * You can then get all rooms as separate regions with {@code List<GreasedRegion> apart = split(rooms);}, or
4035     * substitute {@code split(corridors)} to get the corridors. The room-finding technique works by shrinking floors
4036     * by a radius of 1 (8-way), which causes thin areas like corridors of 2 or less width to be removed, then
4037     * flood-filling the floors out from the area that produces by 2 cells (4-way this time) to restore the original
4038     * size of non-corridor areas (plus some extra to ensure odd shapes are kept). Corridors are obtained by removing
4039     * the rooms from floors. The example code also gets the doors (which overlap with rooms, not corridors) by finding
4040     * where the a room and a corridor are adjacent. This technique is used with some enhancements in the RoomFinder
4041     * class.
4042     * @see squidpony.squidgrid.mapping.RoomFinder for a class that uses this technique without exposing GreasedRegion
4043     * @return an ArrayList containing each unconnected area from packed as a GreasedRegion element
4044     */
4045    public ArrayList<GreasedRegion> split8way()
4046    {
4047        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> scattered = new ArrayList<>(32);
4048        int fst = firstTight();
4049        GreasedRegion remaining = new GreasedRegion(this);
4050        while (fst >= 0) {
4051            GreasedRegion filled = new GreasedRegion(width, height).insert(fst).flood8way(remaining, width * height);
4052            scattered.add(filled);
4053            remaining.andNot(filled);
4054            fst = remaining.firstTight();
4055        }
4056        return scattered;
4057    }
4058
4059    /**
4060     * Finds the largest contiguous area of "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and returns it; does not modify this
4061     * GreasedRegion. If there are multiple areas that are all equally large with no larger area, this returns the
4062     * region it checks first and still is largest (first determined by the same ordering {@link #nth(int)} takes).
4063     * This may return an empty GreasedRegion if there are no "on" cells, but it will never return null.
4064     * Here, contiguous means adjacent on an orthogonal direction, and this doesn't consider diagonally-connected cells
4065     * as contiguous unless they also have an orthogonal connection.
4066     * @return a new GreasedRegion that corresponds to the largest contiguous sub-region of "on" cells in this.
4067     */
4068    public GreasedRegion largestPart()
4069    {
4070        int fst = firstTight(), bestSize = 0, currentSize;
4071        GreasedRegion remaining = new GreasedRegion(this), filled = new GreasedRegion(width, height),
4072                choice = new GreasedRegion(width, height);
4073        while (fst >= 0) {
4074            filled.empty().insert(fst).flood(remaining, width * height);
4075            if((currentSize = filled.size()) > bestSize)
4076            {
4077                bestSize = currentSize;
4078                choice.remake(filled);
4079            }
4080            remaining.andNot(filled);
4081            fst = remaining.firstTight();
4082        }
4083        return choice;
4084    }
4085
4086    /**
4087     * Finds the largest contiguous area of "on" cells in this GreasedRegion and returns it; does not modify this
4088     * GreasedRegion. If there are multiple areas that are all equally large with no larger area, this returns the
4089     * region it checks first and still is largest (first determined by the same ordering {@link #nth(int)} takes).
4090     * This may return an empty GreasedRegion if there are no "on" cells, but it will never return null.
4091     * Here, contiguous means adjacent on any 8-way direction, and considers cells as part of a contiguous area even if
4092     * all connections but one, which can be orthogonal or diagonal, are blocked by "off" cells.
4093     * @return a new GreasedRegion that corresponds to the largest contiguous sub-region of "on" cells in this.
4094     */
4095    public GreasedRegion largestPart8way()
4096    {
4097        int fst = firstTight(), bestSize = 0, currentSize;
4098        GreasedRegion remaining = new GreasedRegion(this), filled = new GreasedRegion(width, height),
4099                choice = new GreasedRegion(width, height);
4100        while (fst >= 0) {
4101            filled.empty().insert(fst).flood8way(remaining, width * height);
4102            if((currentSize = filled.size()) > bestSize)
4103            {
4104                bestSize = currentSize;
4105                choice.remake(filled);
4106            }
4107            remaining.andNot(filled);
4108            fst = remaining.firstTight();
4109        }
4110        return choice;
4111    }
4112
4113    /**
4114     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so the only cells that will be "on" have a neighbor upwards when this is called.
4115     * Up is defined as negative y. Neighbors are "on" cells exactly one cell away. A cell can have a neighbor
4116     * without itself being on; this is useful when finding the "shadow" cast away from "on" cells in one direction.
4117     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
4118     */
4119    public GreasedRegion neighborUp()
4120    {
4121        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0)
4122            return this;
4123        for (int a = ySections - 1; a >= 0; a--) {
4124            if(a > 0) {
4125                for (int i = a; i < width * ySections; i+= ySections) {
4126                    data[i] = (data[i] << 1) | ((data[i - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63);
4127                }
4128            }
4129            else {
4130                for (int i = a; i < width * ySections; i+= ySections) {
4131                    data[i] = (data[i] << 1);
4132                }
4133            }
4134        }
4135        tallied = false;
4136        return this;
4137    }
4138
4139    /**
4140     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so the only cells that will be "on" have a neighbor downwards when this is called.
4141     * Down is defined as positive y. Neighbors are "on" cells exactly one cell away. A cell can have a neighbor
4142     * without itself being on; this is useful when finding the "shadow" cast away from "on" cells in one direction.
4143     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
4144     */
4145    public GreasedRegion neighborDown()
4146    {
4147        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0)
4148            return this;
4149        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
4150            if(a < ySections - 1) {
4151                for (int i = a; i < width * ySections; i+= ySections) {
4152                    data[i] = (data[i] >>> 1) | ((data[i + 1] & 1L) << 63);
4153                }
4154            }
4155            else {
4156                for (int i = a; i < width * ySections; i+= ySections) {
4157                    data[i] = (data[i] >>> 1);
4158                }
4159            }
4160        }
4161        tallied = false;
4162        return this;
4163    }

4165    /**
4166     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so the only cells that will be "on" have a neighbor to the left when this is called.
4167     * Left is defined as negative x. Neighbors are "on" cells exactly one cell away. A cell can have a neighbor
4168     * without itself being on; this is useful when finding the "shadow" cast away from "on" cells in one direction.
4169     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
4170     */
4171    public GreasedRegion neighborLeft()
4172    {
4173        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0)
4174            return this;
4175        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
4176            for (int i = ySections * (width - 1) + a; i >= ySections; i-= ySections) {
4177                data[i] = data[i - ySections];
4178            }
4179            data[a] = 0L;
4180        }
4181        tallied = false;
4182        return this;
4183    }

4186     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so the only cells that will be "on" have a neighbor to the right when this is called.
4187     * Right is defined as positive x. Neighbors are "on" cells exactly one cell away. A cell can have a neighbor
4188     * without itself being on; this is useful when finding the "shadow" cast away from "on" cells in one direction.
4189     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
4190     */
4191    public GreasedRegion neighborRight()
4192    {
4193        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0)
4194            return this;
4195        for (int a = 0; a < ySections; a++) {
4196            for (int i = a; i < (width - 1) * ySections; i+= ySections) {
4197                data[i] = data[i + ySections];
4198            }
4199            data[(width-1)*ySections+a] = 0L;
4200        }
4201        tallied = false;
4202        return this;
4203    }

4205    /**
4206     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so the only cells that will be "on" have a neighbor upwards and to the left when this
4207     * is called. Up is defined as negative y, left as negative x. Neighbors are "on" cells exactly one cell away. A
4208     * cell can have a neighbor without itself being on; this is useful when finding the "shadow" cast away from "on"
4209     * cells in one direction.
4210     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
4211     */
4212    public GreasedRegion neighborUpLeft()
4213    {
4214        if(width < 2 || ySections <= 0)
4215            return this;
4216        for (int a = ySections - 1; a >= 0; a--) {
4217            if(a > 0) {
4218                for (int i = ySections * (width - 1) + a; i >= ySections; i-= ySections) {
4219                    data[i] = (data[i - ySections] << 1) | ((data[i - ySections - 1] & 0x8000000000000000L) >>> 63);
4220                }
4221                data[a] = 0L;
4222            }
4223            else {
4224                for (int i = ySections * (width - 1) + a; i >= ySections; i-= ySections) {
4225                    data[i] = (data[i - ySections] << 1);
4226                }
4227                data[a] = 0L;
4228            }
4229        }
4230        return this;
4231    }

4320    public GreasedRegion removeIsolated()
4321    {
4322        int fst = firstTight();
4323        GreasedRegion remaining = new GreasedRegion(this), filled = new GreasedRegion(this);
4324        while (fst >= 0) {
4325            filled.empty().insert(fst).flood(remaining, 8);
4326            if(filled.size() <= 4)
4327                andNot(filled);
4328            remaining.andNot(filled);
4329            fst = remaining.firstTight();
4330        }
4331        return this;
4332    }
4333
4334    /**
4335     * Returns true if any cell is "on" in both this GreasedRegion and in other; returns false otherwise. For example,
4336     * if (1,1) is "on" in this and (1,1) is "on" in other, this would return true, regardless of other cells.
4337     * @param other another GreasedRegion; its size does not have to match this GreasedRegion's size
4338     * @return true if this shares any "on" cells with other
4339     */
4340    public boolean intersects(GreasedRegion other)
4341    {
4342        if(other == null)
4343            return false;
4344        for (int x = 0; x < width && x < other.width; x++) {
4345            for (int y = 0; y < ySections && y < other.ySections; y++) {
4346                if((data[x * ySections + y] & other.data[x * ySections + y]) != 0)
4347                    return true;
4348            }
4349        }
4350        return false;
4351    }
4352
4353    public static OrderedSet<GreasedRegion> whichContain(int x, int y, GreasedRegion ... packed)
4354    {
4355        OrderedSet<GreasedRegion> found = new OrderedSet<>(packed.length);
4356        GreasedRegion tmp;
4357        for (int i = 0; i < packed.length; i++) {
4358            if((tmp = packed[i]) != null && tmp.contains(x, y))
4359                found.add(tmp);
4360        }
4361        return found;
4362    }
4363
4364    public static OrderedSet<GreasedRegion> whichContain(int x, int y, Collection<GreasedRegion> packed)
4365    {
4366        OrderedSet<GreasedRegion> found = new OrderedSet<>(packed.size());
4367        for (GreasedRegion tmp : packed) {
4368            if(tmp != null && tmp.contains(x, y))
4369                found.add(tmp);
4370        }
4371        return found;
4372    }

4375    public int size()
4376    {
4377        if(!tallied)
4378            tally();
4379        return ct;
4380    }
4381
4382    public Coord fit(double xFraction, double yFraction)
4383    {
4384        int tmp, xTotal = 0, yTotal = 0, xTarget, yTarget, bestX = -1;
4385        long t;
4386        int[] xCounts = new int[width];
4387        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4388            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4389                t = data[x * ySections + s];
4390                if (t != 0) {
4391                    tmp = Long.bitCount(t);
4392                    xCounts[x] += tmp;
4393                    xTotal += tmp;
4394                }
4395            }
4396        }
4397        xTarget = (int)(xTotal * xFraction);
4398        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4399            if((xTarget -= xCounts[x]) < 0)
4400            {
4401                bestX = x;
4402                yTotal = xCounts[x];
4403                break;
4404            }
4405        }
4406        if(bestX < 0)
4407        {
4408            return Coord.get(-1, -1);
4409        }
4410        yTarget = (int)(yTotal * yFraction);
4411
4412        for (int s = 0, y = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4413            t = data[bestX * ySections + s];
4414            for (long cy = 1; cy != 0 && y < height; y++, cy <<= 1) {
4415                if((t & cy) != 0 && --yTarget < 0)
4416                {
4417                    return Coord.get(bestX, y);
4418                }
4419            }
4420        }
4421
4422        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
4423    }
4424
4425    public int[][] fit(int[][] basis, int defaultValue)
4426    {
4427        int[][] next = ArrayTools.fill(defaultValue, width, height);
4428        if(basis == null || basis.length <= 0 || basis[0] == null || basis[0].length <= 0)
4429            return next;
4430        int tmp, xTotal = 0, yTotal = 0, xTarget, yTarget, bestX = -1, oX = basis.length, oY = basis[0].length, ao;
4431        long t;
4432        int[] xCounts = new int[width];
4433        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4434            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4435                t = data[x * ySections + s];
4436                if (t != 0) {
4437                    tmp = Long.bitCount(t);
4438                    xCounts[x] += tmp;
4439                    xTotal += tmp;
4440                }
4441            }
4442        }
4443        if(xTotal <= 0)
4444            return next;
4445        for (int aX = 0; aX < oX; aX++) {
4446            CELL_WISE:
4447            for (int aY = 0; aY < oY; aY++) {
4448                if((ao = basis[aX][aY]) == defaultValue)
4449                    continue;
4450                xTarget = xTotal * aX / oX;
4451                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4452                    if((xTarget -= xCounts[x]) < 0)
4453                    {
4454                        bestX = x;
4455                        yTotal = xCounts[x];
4456                        yTarget = yTotal * aY / oY;
4457                        for (int s = 0, y = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4458                            t = data[bestX * ySections + s];
4459                            for (long cy = 1; cy != 0 && y < height; y++, cy <<= 1) {
4460                                if((t & cy) != 0 && --yTarget < 0)
4461                                {
4462                                    next[bestX][y] = ao;
4463                                    continue CELL_WISE;
4464                                }
4465                            }
4466                        }
4467                        continue CELL_WISE;
4468                    }
4469                }
4470
4471            }
4472        }
4473
4474        return next;
4475    }
4476    
4477    /**
4478     * Don't use this in new code; prefer {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double)}, {@link #quasiRandomSeparated(double)},
4479     * or {@link #separatedZCurve(double)}. This method has issues with being unable to fill the requested fraction, but
4480     * the others mentioned don't. See their documentation for what all these group of methods do.
4481     * @param fraction between 0.0 and 1.0
4482     * @return a Coord array that may not have the full fraction used; you have been advised
4483     */
4484    public Coord[] separatedPortion(double fraction)
4485    {
4486        if(fraction < 0)
4487            return new Coord[0];
4488        if(fraction > 1)
4489            fraction = 1;
4490        int ct, tmp, xTotal = 0, yTotal = 0, xTarget, yTarget, bestX = -1;
4491        long t;
4492        int[] xCounts = new int[width];
4493        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4494            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4495                t = data[x * ySections + s];
4496                if (t != 0) {
4497                    tmp = Long.bitCount(t);
4498                    xCounts[x] += tmp;
4499                    xTotal += tmp;
4500                }
4501            }
4502        }
4503        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct = (int)(fraction * xTotal)];
4504        double[] vec = new double[2];
4505        sobol.skipTo(1337);
4506        EACH_SOBOL:
4507        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
4508        {
4509            sobol.fillVector(vec);
4510            xTarget = (int) (xTotal * vec[0]);
4511            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4512                if ((xTarget -= xCounts[x]) < 0) {
4513                    bestX = x;
4514                    yTotal = xCounts[x];
4515                    break;
4516                }
4517            }
4518            yTarget = (int) (yTotal * vec[1]);
4519
4520            for (int s = 0, y = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4521                t = data[bestX * ySections + s];
4522                for (long cy = 1; cy != 0 && y < height; y++, cy <<= 1) {
4523                    if ((t & cy) != 0 && --yTarget < 0) {
4524                        vl[i] = Coord.get(bestX, y);
4525                        continue EACH_SOBOL;
4526                    }
4527                }
4528            }
4529        }
4530        return vl;
4531
4532    }
4533    /**
4534     * Don't use this in new code; prefer {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int, long)} with a random long as the
4535     * last parameter. This method has issues with being unable to fill the requested fraction, but mixedRandomSeparated
4536     * does not. See its documentation for what this method is supposed to do.
4537     * @param fraction between 0.0 and 1.0
4538     * @param rng an IRNG that will be used to get a random starting point in the Sobol sequence this uses internally
4539     * @return a Coord array that may not have the full fraction used; you have been advised
4540     */
4541    public Coord[] randomSeparated(double fraction, IRNG rng)
4542    {
4543        return randomSeparated(fraction, rng, -1);
4544    }
4545    /**
4546     * Don't use this in new code; prefer {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int, long)} with a random long as the
4547     * last parameter. This method has issues with being unable to fill the requested fraction, but mixedRandomSeparated
4548     * does not. See its documentation for what this method is supposed to do.
4549     * @param fraction between 0.0 and 1.0
4550     * @param rng an IRNG that will be used to get a random starting point in the Sobol sequence this uses internally
4551     * @param limit how many Coord values this should return, at most; typically this will return less
4552     * @return a Coord array that may not have the full fraction used; you have been advised
4553     */
4554    public Coord[] randomSeparated(double fraction, IRNG rng, int limit)
4555    {
4556        if(fraction < 0)
4557            return new Coord[0];
4558        if(fraction > 1)
4559            fraction = 1;
4560        int ct, tmp, xTotal = 0, yTotal = 0, xTarget, yTarget, bestX = -1;
4561        long t;
4562        int[] xCounts = new int[width];
4563        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4564            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4565                t = data[x * ySections + s];
4566                if (t != 0) {
4567                    tmp = Long.bitCount(t);
4568                    xCounts[x] += tmp;
4569                    xTotal += tmp;
4570                }
4571            }
4572        }
4573        ct = (int)(fraction * xTotal);
4574        if(limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
4575            ct = limit;
4576        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct];
4577        double[] vec = new double[2];
4578        sobol.skipTo(rng.between(1000, 65000));
4579        EACH_SOBOL:
4580        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
4581        {
4582            sobol.fillVector(vec);
4583            xTarget = (int) (xTotal * vec[0]);
4584            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4585                if ((xTarget -= xCounts[x]) < 0) {
4586                    bestX = x;
4587                    yTotal = xCounts[x];
4588                    break;
4589                }
4590            }
4591            yTarget = (int) (yTotal * vec[1]);
4592
4593            for (int s = 0, y = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4594                t = data[bestX * ySections + s];
4595                for (long cy = 1; cy != 0 && y < height; y++, cy <<= 1) {
4596                    if ((t & cy) != 0 && --yTarget < 0) {
4597                        vl[i] = Coord.get(bestX, y);
4598                        continue EACH_SOBOL;
4599                    }
4600                }
4601            }
4602        }
4603        return vl;
4604
4605    }
4606
4607    /**
4608     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a deterministic but random-seeming
4609     * scattering of chosen cells with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
4610     * in this. This is pseudo-random with a fixed seed, but is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as
4611     * {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double, int)}, and probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a
4612     * value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in
4613     * testing. Does not restrict the size of the returned array other than only using up to
4614     * {@code fraction * size()} cells.
4615     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4616     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the quasi-random cells
4617     */
4618    public Coord[] mixedRandomSeparated(double fraction)
4619    {
4620        return mixedRandomSeparated(fraction, -1, 1L);
4621    }
4622
4623    /**
4624     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a deterministic but random-seeming
4625     * scattering of chosen cells with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
4626     * in this. This is pseudo-random with a fixed seed, but is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as
4627     * {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double, int)}, and probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a
4628     * value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in
4629     * testing. Restricts the total size of the returned array to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells
4630     * are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the size.
4631     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4632     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return
4633     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the pseudo-random cells
4634     */
4635    public Coord[] mixedRandomSeparated(double fraction, int limit)
4636    {
4637        return mixedRandomSeparated(fraction, limit, 1L);
4638    }

4640    /**
4641     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a deterministic but random-seeming
4642     * scattering of chosen cells with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
4643     * in this. This is pseudo-random with the given seed (which will be made into an odd number if it is not one
4644     * already), and is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as {@link #separatedZCurve(double, int)}, and
4645     * probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but
4646     * a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in testing. Restricts the total size of the returned array to
4647     * a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the
4648     * size.
4649     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4650     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return
4651     * @param seed a long seed to change the points; the most significant 21 bits (except the sign bit) and least significant bit are ignored
4652     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the pseudo-random cells
4653     */
4654    public Coord[] mixedRandomSeparated(double fraction, int limit, long seed) {
4655        if (fraction < 0)
4656            return new Coord[0];
4657        if (fraction > 1)
4658            fraction = 1;
4659        int tmp, ic;
4660        long t, w;
4661        seed |= 1L;
4662        final int total = size();
4663        int ct = (int) (total * fraction);
4664        if (limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
4665            ct = limit;
4666        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct];
4667        EACH_QUASI:
4668        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++) {
4669            tmp = (int) (VanDerCorputQRNG.altDetermine(seed, i + 1) * total);
4670
4671            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4672                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4673                    if ((ic = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
4674                        t = data[x * ySections + s];
4675                        for (--ic; t != 0; ic--) {
4676                            w = t & -t;
4677                            if (ic == tmp) {
4678                                vl[i] = Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.bitCount(w - 1));
4679                                continue EACH_QUASI;
4680                            }
4681                            t ^= w;
4682                        }
4683                    }
4684                }
4685            }
4686        }
4687        return vl;
4688    }

4693     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a deterministic but random-seeming subset of its previous contents,
4694     * choosing cells so that the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
4695     * in this. This is pseudo-random with a fixed seed, and is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as
4696     * {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double, int)}, and probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a
4697     * value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in
4698     * testing. Does not restrict the count of "on" cells after this returns other than by only using up to
4699     * {@code fraction * size()} cells.
4700     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4701     * @return this for chaining
4702     */
4703    public GreasedRegion mixedRandomRegion(double fraction) {

4706    /**
4707     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a deterministic but random-seeming subset of its previous contents,
4708     * choosing cells so that the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
4709     * in this. This is pseudo-random with a fixed seed, and is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as
4710     * {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double, int)}, and probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a
4711     * value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in
4712     * testing. Restricts the total count of "on" cells after this returns to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0
4713     * if no cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the count.
4714     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4715     * @param limit the maximum count of "on" cells to keep
4716     * @return this for chaining
4717     */
4718    public GreasedRegion mixedRandomRegion(double fraction, int limit) {

4721    /**
4722     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a deterministic but random-seeming subset of its previous contents,
4723     * choosing cells so that the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
4724     * in this. This is pseudo-random with the given seed (which will be made into an odd number if it is not one
4725     * already), and is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as {@link #separatedZCurve(double, int)}, and
4726     * probably faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but
4727     * a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in testing. Restricts the total count of "on" cells after
4728     * this returns to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will
4729     * not restrict the count.
4730     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4731     * @param limit the maximum count of "on" cells to keep
4732     * @return this for chaining
4733     */
4734    public GreasedRegion mixedRandomRegion(double fraction, int limit, long seed) {
4735        int idx, run = 0;
4736        final int total = size();
4737        if (total <= limit)
4738            return this;
4739        if (total <= 0)
4740            return empty();
4741        if (limit < 0)
4742            limit = (int) (fraction * ct);
4743        if(limit <= 0)
4744            return empty();
4745        seed |= 1L;
4746        int[] order = new int[limit];
4747        for (int i = 0, m = 1; i < limit; i++, m++) {
4748            idx = (int)(VanDerCorputQRNG.altDetermine(seed, m) * total);
4749            BIG:
4750            while (true) {
4751                for (int j = 0; j < i; j++) {
4752                    if (order[j] == idx) {
4753                        idx = (int)(VanDerCorputQRNG.altDetermine(seed, ++m) * total);
4754                        continue BIG;
4755                    }
4756                }
4757                break;
4758            }
4759            order[i] = idx;
4760        }
4761        idx = 0;
4762        Arrays.sort(order);
4763        long t, w;
4764        ALL:
4765        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4766            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4767                if ((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0) {
4768                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4769                    while (w != 0) {
4770                        if (run++ == order[idx]) {
4771                            if (++idx >= limit) {
4772                                data[x * ySections + s] &= (w<<1)-1;
4773                                for (int rx = x+1; rx < width; rx++) {
4774                                    data[rx * ySections + s] = 0;
4775                                }
4776                                for (int rs = s+1; rs < ySections; rs++) {
4777                                    for (int rx = 0; rx < width; rx++) {
4778                                        data[rx * ySections + rs] = 0;
4779                                    }
4780                                }
4781                                break ALL;
4782                            }
4783                        } else {
4784                            data[x * ySections + s] ^= w;
4785                        }
4786                        t ^= w;
4787                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4788                    }
4789                }
4790            }
4791        }
4792        tallied = false;
4793        return this;
4794    }

4796    /**
4797     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a quasi-random scattering of chosen cells
4798     * with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
4799     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
4800     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however.
4801     * Does not restrict the size of the returned array other than only using up to {@code fraction * size()} cells.
4802     * <br>
4803     * You can choose between {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double)}, {@link #separatedZCurve(double)}, and this method,
4804     * where all are quasi-random, mixedRandom is probably fastest, ZCurve may have better 2-dimensional gaps between
4805     * cells, and this method is somewhere in the middle.
4806     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4807     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the quasi-random cells
4808     */
4809    public Coord[] quasiRandomSeparated(double fraction)
4810    {
4811        return quasiRandomSeparated(fraction, -1);
4812    }

4814    /**
4815     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a quasi-random scattering of chosen cells
4816     * with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
4817     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
4818     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however.
4819     * Restricts the total size of the returned array to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on").
4820     * If limit is negative, this will not restrict the size.
4821     * <br>
4822     * You can choose between {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int)}, {@link #separatedZCurve(double, int)}, and
4823     * this method, where all are quasi-random, mixedRandom is probably fastest, ZCurve may have better 2-dimensional
4824     * gaps between cells, and this method is somewhere in the middle.
4825     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4826     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return
4827     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the quasi-random cells
4828     */
4829    public Coord[] quasiRandomSeparated(double fraction, int limit)
4830    {
4831        if(fraction < 0)
4832            return new Coord[0];
4833        if(fraction > 1)
4834            fraction = 1;
4835        int ct = 0, tmp, total, ic;
4836        long t, w;
4837        int[] counts = new int[width * ySections];
4838        for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
4839            tmp = Long.bitCount(data[i]);
4840            counts[i] = tmp == 0 ? -1 : (ct += tmp);
4841        }
4842        total = ct;
4843        ct *= fraction;// (int)(fraction * ct);
4844        if(limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
4845            ct = limit;
4846        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct];
4847        EACH_QUASI:
4848        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
4849        {
4850            tmp = (int)(VanDerCorputQRNG.determine2(i ^ i >>> 1) * total);
4851            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4852                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4853                    if ((ic = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
4854                        t = data[x * ySections + s];
4855                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4856                        for (--ic; w != 0; ic--) {
4857                            if (ic == tmp) {
4858                                vl[i] = Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
4859                                continue EACH_QUASI;
4860                            }
4861                            t ^= w;
4862                            w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4863                        }
4864                    }
4865                }
4866            }
4867            vl[i] = atFraction(tmp);
4868        }
4869        return vl;
4870    }

4877     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
4878     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however.
4879     * Does not restrict the count of "on" cells after this returns other than by only using up to
4880     * {@code fraction * size()} cells.
4881     * <br>
4882     * You can choose between {@link #mixedRandomRegion(double)}, {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double)}, and this
4883     * method, where all are quasi-random, mixedRandom is probably fastest, ZCurve may have better 2-dimensional gaps
4884     * between cells, and this method is somewhere in the middle.

4891    /**
4892     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a quasi-random subset of its previous contents, choosing cells so that
4893     * the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
4894     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
4895     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however.
4896     * Restricts the total count of "on" cells after this returns to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no
4897     * cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the count.
4898     * <br>
4899     * You can choose between {@link #mixedRandomRegion(double, int)}, {@link #separatedRegionZCurve(double, int)}, and
4900     * this method, where all are quasi-random, mixedRandom is probably fastest, ZCurve may have better 2-dimensional
4901     * gaps between cells, and this method is somewhere in the middle.
4902     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
4903     * @param limit the maximum count of "on" cells to keep
4904     * @return this for chaining
4905     */
4906    public GreasedRegion quasiRandomRegion(double fraction, int limit) {
4907        int ct = size(), idx, run = 0;
4908        if (ct <= limit)
4909            return this;
4910        if (ct <= 0)
4911            return empty();
4912        if (limit < 0)
4913            limit = (int) (fraction * ct);
4914        if(limit <= 0)
4915            return empty();
4916        int[] order = new int[limit];
4917        for (int i = 0, m = 1; i < limit; i++, m++) {
4918            idx = (int) (VanDerCorputQRNG.determine2(m) * ct);
4919            BIG:
4920            while (true) {
4921                for (int j = 0; j < i; j++) {
4922                    if (order[j] == idx) {
4923                        idx = (int) (VanDerCorputQRNG.determine2(++m) * ct);
4924                        continue BIG;
4925                    }
4926                }
4927                break;
4928            }
4929            order[i] = idx;
4930        }
4931        idx = 0;
4932        Arrays.sort(order);
4933        long t, w;
4934        ALL:
4935        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
4936            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
4937                if ((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0) {
4938                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4939                    while (w != 0) {
4940                        if (run++ == order[idx]) {
4941                            if (++idx >= limit) {
4942                                data[x * ySections + s] &= (w<<1)-1;
4943                                for (int rx = x+1; rx < width; rx++) {
4944                                    data[rx * ySections + s] = 0;
4945                                }
4946                                for (int rs = s+1; rs < ySections; rs++) {
4947                                    for (int rx = 0; rx < width; rx++) {
4948                                        data[rx * ySections + rs] = 0;
4949                                    }
4950                                }
4951                                break ALL;
4952                            }
4953                        } else {
4954                            data[x * ySections + s] ^= w;
4955                        }
4956                        t ^= w;
4957                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
4958                    }
4959                }
4960            }
4961        }
4962        tallied = false;
4963        return this;
4964    }

4966    /**
4967     * Like {@link #retract()}, this removes the "on" cells that are 4-way-adjacent to any "off" cell, but unlike that
4968     * method it keeps a fraction of those surface cells, quasi-randomly selecting them. This can be thought of as
4969     * running {@link #surface()} on a copy of this GreasedRegion, running {@link #quasiRandomRegion(double)} on that
4970     * surface with the given fractionKept, taking the original GreasedRegion and removing its whole surface with
4971     * {@link #retract()}, then inserting the quasi-randomly-removed surface into this GreasedRegion to replace its
4972     * surface with a randomly "damaged" one.
4973     * @param fractionKept the fraction between 0.0 and 1.0 of how many cells on the outer surface of this to keep "on"
4974     * @return this for chaining
4975     */
4976    public GreasedRegion fray(double fractionKept)
4977    {
4978        GreasedRegion cpy = new GreasedRegion(this).retract();
4979        return xor(cpy).quasiRandomRegion(1.0 - fractionKept).or(cpy);
4980    }

4982    /**
4983     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a random subset of its previous contents, choosing cells so that the
4984     * distance between any two "on" cells is at least {@code minimumDistance}, with at least one cell as "on" if any
4985     * were "on" in this originally. Does not limit the count of "on" cells in the result.
4986     * @param rng used to generate random positions
4987     * @param minimumDistance the minimum distance between "on" cells in the result
4988     * @return this for chaining
4989     */
4990    public GreasedRegion randomScatter(IRNG rng, int minimumDistance) {
4991        return randomScatter(rng, minimumDistance, -1);
4992    }
4993    /**
4994     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a random subset of its previous contents, choosing cells so that the
4995     * distance between any two "on" cells is at least {@code minimumDistance}, with at least one cell as "on" if any
4996     * were "on" in this originally.
4997     * Restricts the total count of "on" cells after this returns to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no
4998     * cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the count.
4999     * @param rng used to generate random positions
5000     * @param minimumDistance the minimum distance between "on" cells in the result
5001     * @param limit the maximum count of "on" cells to keep
5002     * @return this for chaining
5003     */
5004    public GreasedRegion randomScatter(IRNG rng, int minimumDistance, int limit) {
5005        int ic = 0;
5006        for (; ic < width * ySections; ic++) {
5007            if(data[ic] != 0)
5008                break;
5009        }
5010        if(ic == width * ySections)
5011            return this;
5012        if(limit == 0)
5013            return empty();
5014        else if(limit < 0)
5015            limit = 0x7fffffff;
5016        long[] data2 = new long[data.length];
5017        long t, w;
5018        int tmp, total = 0;
5019        MAIN_LOOP:
5020        while (total < limit) { 
5021            if(!tallied) 
5022                tally();
5023            tmp = rng.nextInt(ct);
5024
5025            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5026                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5027                    if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
5028                        t = data[x * ySections + s];
5029                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5030                        for (--ct; w != 0; ct--) {
5031                            if (ct == tmp) {
5032                                data2[x * ySections + s] |= w;
5033                                ++total;
5034                                removeRectangle(x - minimumDistance,
5035                                        ((s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)) - minimumDistance,
5036                                        minimumDistance << 1 | 1, minimumDistance << 1 | 1);
5037                                continue MAIN_LOOP;
5038                            }
5039                            t ^= w;
5040                            w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5041                        }
5042                    }
5043                }
5044            }
5045            break;
5046        }
5047        data = data2;
5048        tallied = false;
5049        return this;
5050    }

5052    public double rateDensity()
5053    {
5054        double sz = height * width;
5055        if(sz == 0)
5056            return 0;
5057        double onAmount = sz - size(), retractedOn = sz - copy().retract().size();
5058        return (onAmount + retractedOn) / (sz * 2.0);
5059    }
5060    public double rateRegularity()
5061    {
5062        GreasedRegion me2 = copy().surface8way();
5063        double irregularCount = me2.size();
5064        if(irregularCount == 0)
5065            return 0;
5066        return me2.remake(this).surface().size() / irregularCount;
5067    }
