5069    private static int median(int[] working, int start, int amount)
5070    {
5071        Arrays.sort(working, start, start + amount);
5072        if ((amount & 1) == 0) {
5073            return working[start + (amount >> 1) - 1] + working[start + (amount >> 1)] >>> 1;
5074        } else {
5075            return working[start + (amount >> 1)];
5076        }
5077    }
5078
5079    /**
5080     * Calculates a perceptual hash for this GreasedRegion using a method that is only precise for some sizes of
5081     * GreasedRegion; it writes a result to into, and uses working as a temporary buffer. The lengths of into and
5082     * working should be related; if into is length 1, then working should be length 64, and though the hash won't be
5083     * very detailed, it will work well for images with width and height that are multiples of 8; if into is length 4,
5084     * then working should be length 256, and this will work with more detail on images that have width and height that
5085     * are multiples of 16. If working is null or is too small, then this won't reuse it and will allocate an
5086     * appropriately-sized array for internal use.
5087     * <br>
5088     * Ported from https://github.com/commonsmachinery/blockhash/blob/master/blockhash.c , which is MIT-licensed.
5089     * @param into should be a long array of length 1 or 4; the contents don't matter and this will be where output is written to
5090     * @param working should be an int array of length 64 (if into has length 1) or 256 (if into has length 4); may be null if you like garbage collection
5091     */
5092    public void perceptualHashQuick(long[] into, int[] working)
5093    {
5094        final int bits = 8 << (Integer.numberOfTrailingZeros(Integer.highestOneBit(into.length)) >> 1);
5095        if(working == null || working.length < bits * bits)
5096            working = new int[bits * bits];
5097        final int blockWidth = width / bits, blockHeight = height / bits, blockWidthSections = blockWidth * ySections;
5098        if(blockHeight == 1)
5099        {
5100            for (int y = 0; y < bits; y++) {
5101                for (int x = 0; x < bits; x++) {
5102                    int value = 0;
5103                    for (int ix = 0; ix < blockWidthSections; ix += ySections) {
5104                        value += (data[x * blockWidthSections + ix + (y >> 6)] >>> (y & 63) & 1L);
5105                    }
5106                    working[x * bits + y] = value;
5107                }
5108            }
5109        }
5110        else if(blockHeight < 64 && Integer.bitCount(blockHeight) == 1) {
5111            final long yBlockMask = ~(-1L << blockHeight);
5112            final int divisorMask = (64 / blockHeight) - 1;
5113            long currentMask;
5114            int blockY = 0;
5115            for (int y = 0; y < bits; y++, blockY += blockHeight) {
5116                currentMask = yBlockMask << ((y & divisorMask) << blockHeight);
5117                for (int x = 0; x < bits; x++) {
5118                    int value = 0;
5119                    for (int ix = 0; ix < blockWidthSections; ix += ySections) {
5120                        value += Long.bitCount(data[x * blockWidthSections + ix + (blockY >> 6)] & currentMask);
5121                    }
5122                    working[x * bits + y] = value;
5123                }
5124            }
5125        }
5126        final int cellsPerBlock = blockWidth * blockHeight, numBlocks = bits * bits,
5127                halfCellCount = cellsPerBlock >>> 1;
5128        int bandSize = numBlocks >>> 2;
5129        int m, v;
5130        int currentInto = 0;
5131        long currentIntoPos = 1L;
5132        for (int i = 0; i < 4; i++) {
5133            m = median(working, i * bandSize, bandSize);
5134            for (int j = i * bandSize; j < (i + 1) * bandSize; j++) {
5135                v = working[j];
5136                if(v > m || (v - m == 0 && m > halfCellCount)) into[currentInto] |= currentIntoPos;
5137                if((currentIntoPos <<= 1) == 0)
5138                {
5139                    ++currentInto;
5140                    currentIntoPos = 1L;
5141                }
5142            }
5143        }
5144    }
5145
5146    /*
5147    // This showed a strong x-y correlation because it didn't have a way to use a non-base-2 van der Corput sequence.
5148    // It also produced very close-together points, unfortunately.
5149    public static double quasiRandomX(int idx)
5150    {
5151        return atVDCSequence(26 + idx * 5);
5152    }
5153    public static double quasiRandomY(int idx)
5154    {
5155        return atVDCSequence(19 + idx * 3);
5156    }
5157
5158    private static double atVDCSequence(int idx)
5159    {
5160        int leading = Integer.numberOfLeadingZeros(idx);
5161        return (Integer.reverse(idx) >>> leading) / (1.0 * (1 << (32 - leading)));
5162    }
5163    */
5164    public Coord[] asCoords()
5165    {
5166        return asCoords(new Coord[size()]);
5167
5168    }
5169    public Coord[] asCoords(Coord[] points)
5170    {
5171        if(points == null)
5172            points = new Coord[size()];
5173        int idx = 0, len = points.length;
5174        long t, w;
5175        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5176            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5177                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5178                {
5179                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5180                    while (w != 0) {
5181                        if(idx >= len) return points;
5182                        points[idx++] = Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5183                        t ^= w;
5184                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5185                    }
5186                }
5187            }
5188        }
5189        return points;
5190    }
5191    public int[] asEncoded()
5192    {
5193        int ct = size(), idx = 0;
5194        int[] points = new int[ct];
5195        long t, w;
5196        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5197            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5198                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5199                {
5200                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5201                    while (w != 0) {
5202                        points[idx++] = Coord.pureEncode(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5203                        t ^= w;
5204                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5205                    }
5206                }
5207            }
5208        }
5209        return points;
5210    }
5211    public int[] asTightEncoded()
5212    {
5213        int ct = size(), idx = 0;
5214        int[] points = new int[ct];
5215        long t, w;
5216        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5217            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5218                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5219                {
5220                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5221                    while (w != 0) {
5222                        points[idx++] =  ((s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)) * width + x;
5223                        t ^= w;
5224                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5225                    }
5226                }
5227            }
5228        }
5229        return points;
5230    }
5231
5232    /**
5233     * @return All cells in this zone.
5234     */
5235    @Override
5236    public List<Coord> getAll() {
5237        ArrayList<Coord> points = new ArrayList<>();
5238        long t, w;
5239        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5240            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5241                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5242                {
5243                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5244                    while (w != 0) {
5245                        points.add(Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)));
5246                        t ^= w;
5247                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5248                    }
5249                }
5250            }
5251        }
5252        return points;
5253
5254    }
5255
5256    public Coord first()
5257    {
5258        long w;
5259        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5260            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5261                if ((w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(data[x * ySections + s])) != 0) {
5262                    return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5263                }
5264            }
5265        }
5266        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5267    }
5268
5269    public int firstTight()
5270    {
5271        long w;
5272        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5273            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5274                if ((w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(data[x * ySections + s])) != 0) {
5275                    return ((s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)) * width + x;
5276                }
5277            }
5278        }
5279        return -1;
5280    }
5281    public Coord nth(final int index)
5282    {
5283        if(index < 0)
5284            return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5285        int ct = size(), tmp;
5286        if(index >= ct)
5287            return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5288        long t, w;
5289        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5290            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5291                if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > index) {
5292                    t = data[x * ySections + s];
5293                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5294                    for (--ct; w != 0; ct--) {
5295                        if (ct == index)
5296                            return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5297                        t ^= w;
5298                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5299                    }
5300                }
5301            }
5302        }
5303        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5304    }
5305
5306    public Coord atFraction(final double fraction)
5307    {
5308        int ct = size(), tmp;
5309        if(ct <= 0) return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5310        tmp = Math.abs((int)(fraction * ct) % ct);
5311        long t, w;
5312        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5313            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5314                if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
5315                    t = data[x * ySections + s];
5316                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5317                    for (--ct; w != 0; ct--) {
5318                        if (ct == tmp)
5319                            return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5320                        t ^= w;
5321                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5322                    }
5323                }
5324            }
5325        }
5326        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5327    }
5328
5329    public int atFractionTight(final double fraction)
5330    {
5331        int ct = size(), tmp;
5332        if(ct <= 0) return -1;
5333        tmp = Math.abs((int)(fraction * ct) % ct);
5334        long t, w;
5335
5336        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5337            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5338                if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
5339                    t = data[x * ySections + s];
5340                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5341                    for (--ct; w != 0; ct--) {
5342                        if (ct == tmp)
5343                            return ((s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)) * width + x;
5344                        t ^= w;
5345                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5346                    }
5347                }
5348            }
5349        }
5350        return -1;
5351    }
5352
5353    /**
5354     * Gets a single random Coord from the "on" positions in this GreasedRegion, or the Coord (-1,-1) if this is empty.
5355     * Uses the given IRNG to generate one random int, which is used as an index. The technique this uses to iterate
5356     * over bits can be credited to Erling Ellingsen and Daniel Lemire, found
5357     * <a href="https://lemire.me/blog/2013/12/23/even-faster-bitmap-decoding/">here</a>, and seems to be a little
5358     * faster than the previous method. The fastest way to get a random Coord from a GreasedRegion is to avoid iterating
5359     * over the bits at all, so if your region data doesn't change you should get it as a Coord array with
5360     * {@link #asCoords()} and call {@link IRNG#getRandomElement(Object[])} with that array as the parameter. If you
5361     * take the asCoords() call out of consideration, getting random elements out of an array (especially a large one)
5362     * can be hundreds of times faster.
5363     * @param rng an IRNG such as an {@link RNG} or {@link GWTRNG}
5364     * @return a single randomly-chosen Coord from the "on" positions in this GreasedRegion, or (-1,-1) if empty
5365     */
5366    public Coord singleRandom(IRNG rng)
5367    {
5368        int ct = size(), tmp = rng.nextInt(ct);
5369        long t, w;
5370        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5371            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5372                if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
5373                    t = data[x * ySections + s];
5374                    for (--ct; t != 0; ct--) {
5375                        w = t & -t;
5376                        if (ct == tmp)
5377                            return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.bitCount(w-1));
5378                        t ^= w;
5379                    }
5380                }
5381            }
5382        }
5383        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5384    }
5385
5386    public int singleRandomTight(IRNG rng)
5387    {
5388        int ct = size(), tmp = rng.nextInt(ct);
5389        long t, w;
5390        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5391            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5392                if ((ct = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
5393                    t = data[x * ySections + s];
5394                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5395                    for (--ct; w != 0; ct--) {
5396                        if (ct == tmp)
5397                            return ((s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)) * width + x;
5398                        t ^= w;
5399                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5400                    }
5401                }
5402            }
5403        }
5404
5405        return -1;
5406    }
5407
5408    /**
5409     * Narrow-purpose; takes an x and a y value, each between 0 and 65535 inclusive, and interleaves their bits so the
5410     * least significant bit and every other bit after it are filled with the bits of x, while the
5411     * second-least-significant bit and every other bit after that are filled with the bits of y. Essentially, this
5412     * takes two numbers with bits labeled like {@code a b c} for x and {@code R S T} for y and makes a number with
5413     * those bits arranged like {@code R a S b T c}.
5414     * @param x an int between 0 and 65535, inclusive
5415     * @param y an int between 0 and 65535, inclusive
5416     * @return an int that interleaves x and y, with x in the least significant bit position
5417     */
5418    public static int interleaveBits(int x, int y)
5419    {
5420        x |= y << 16;
5421        x =    ((x & 0x0000ff00) << 8) | ((x >>> 8) & 0x0000ff00) | (x & 0xff0000ff);
5422        x =    ((x & 0x00f000f0) << 4) | ((x >>> 4) & 0x00f000f0) | (x & 0xf00ff00f);
5423        x =    ((x & 0x0c0c0c0c) << 2) | ((x >>> 2) & 0x0c0c0c0c) | (x & 0xc3c3c3c3);
5424        return ((x & 0x22222222) << 1) | ((x >>> 1) & 0x22222222) | (x & 0x99999999);
5425    }
5426
5427    /**
5428     * Narrow-purpose; takes an int that represents a distance down the Z-order curve and moves its bits around so that
5429     * its x component is stored in the bottom 16 bits (use {@code (n & 0xffff)} to obtain) and its y component is
5430     * stored in the upper 16 bits (use {@code (n >>> 16)} to obtain). This may be useful for ordering traversals of all
5431     * points in a GreasedRegion less predictably.
5432     * @param n an int that has already been interleaved, though this can really be any int
5433     * @return an int with x in its lower bits ({@code x = n & 0xffff;}) and y in its upper bits ({@code y = n >>> 16;})
5434     */
5435    public static int disperseBits(int n)
5436    {
5437        n =    ((n & 0x22222222) << 1) | ((n >>> 1) & 0x22222222) | (n & 0x99999999);
5438        n =    ((n & 0x0c0c0c0c) << 2) | ((n >>> 2) & 0x0c0c0c0c) | (n & 0xc3c3c3c3);
5439        n =    ((n & 0x00f000f0) << 4) | ((n >>> 4) & 0x00f000f0) | (n & 0xf00ff00f);
5440        return ((n & 0x0000ff00) << 8) | ((n >>> 8) & 0x0000ff00) | (n & 0xff0000ff);
5441    }
5442    private static int nextPowerOfTwo(int n)
5443    {
5444        final int highest = Integer.highestOneBit(n);
5445        return  (highest == NumberTools.lowestOneBit(n)) ? highest : highest << 1;
5446    }
5447
5448    /**
5449     * Like {@link #nth(int)}, this gets the Coord at a given index along a path through the GreasedRegion, but unlike
5450     * nth(), this traverses the path in a zig-zag pattern called the Z-Order Curve. This method is often not very fast
5451     * compared to nth(), but this different path can help if iteration needs to seem less regular while still covering
5452     * all "on" cells in the GresedRegion eventually.
5453     * @param index the distance along the Z-order curve to travel, only counting "on" cells in this GreasedRegion.
5454     * @return the Coord at the given distance, or the Coord with x and y both -1 if index is too high or low
5455     */
5456    public Coord nthZCurve(final int index)
5457    {
5458        int ct = -1, x, y, s, d, max = nextPowerOfTwo(width) * nextPowerOfTwo(height);
5459        long t, w;
5460        for (int o = 0; o < max; o++) {
5461            d = disperseBits(o);
5462            x = d & 0xffff;
5463            y = d >>> 16;
5464            if(x >= width && y >= height)
5465                break;
5466            if(x >= width)
5467                continue;
5468            if(y >= height)
5469                continue;
5470            s = d >>> 22;
5471            t = data[x * ySections + s];
5472            if((ct += (t >>> (y & 63) & 1L)) == index)
5473                return Coord.get(x, y);
5474        }
5475        return Coord.get(-1, -1);
5476    }
5477    /**
5478     * Like {@link #nth(int)}, this finds a given index along a path through the GreasedRegion, but unlike nth(), this
5479     * traverses the path in a zig-zag pattern called the Z-Order Curve, and unlike {@link #nthZCurve(int)}, this does
5480     * not return a Coord and instead produces a "tight"-encoded int. This method is often not very fast compared to
5481     * nth(), but this different path can help if iteration needs to seem less regular while still covering all "on"
5482     * cells in the GreasedRegion eventually, and the tight encoding may be handy if you need to use ints.
5483     * @param index the distance along the Z-order curve to travel, only counting "on" cells in this GreasedRegion.
5484     * @return the "tight" encoded point at the given distance, or -1 if index is too high or low
5485     */
5486
5487    public int nthZCurveTight(final int index)
5488    {
5489        int ct = -1, x, y, s, d, max = nextPowerOfTwo(width) * nextPowerOfTwo(height);
5490        long t;
5491        for (int o = 0; o < max; o++) {
5492            d = disperseBits(o);
5493            x = d & 0xffff;
5494            y = d >>> 16;
5495            if(x >= width && y >= height)
5496                break;
5497            if(x >= width)
5498                continue;
5499            if(y >= height)
5500                continue;
5501            s = d >>> 22;
5502            t = data[x * ySections + s];
5503            if((ct += (t >>> (y & 63) & 1L)) == index)
5504                return y * width + x;
5505        }
5506        return -1;
5507    }
5508
5509    /**
5510     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a quasi-random scattering of chosen cells
5511     * with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
5512     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
5513     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however. Contrast with
5514     * {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int)}, which tends to overlap more frequently. This method seems to work
5515     * well because it chooses quasi-random points by their index in the Z-Order Curve as opposed to the simpler
5516     * approach mixedRandomSeparated uses to traverse points (which just runs through the "on" cells a column at a time,
5517     * not caring if two points are in adjacent cells as long as they are in different columns). Testing with a dungeon
5518     * layout of mostly-on cells, this method has no overlap with a fraction of 0.4, while mixedRandomSeparated has
5519     * overlap as early as 0.15 for fraction, and it only gets worse at higher values. A change to the algorithm used by
5520     * {@link #quasiRandomSeparated(double)} has it overlapping at the same rate as this method, though it should be
5521     * much faster. This method can be especially slow, since each Z-Order traversal may need to try many cells that are
5522     * outside the GreasedRegion but are on the Z-Order Curve.
5523     * Does not restrict the size of the returned array other than only using up to {@code fraction * size()} cells.
5524     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
5525     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the quasi-random cells
5526     */
5527    public Coord[] separatedZCurve(double fraction)
5528    {
5529        return separatedZCurve(fraction, -1);
5530    }
5531
5532    /**
5533     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a quasi-random scattering of chosen cells
5534     * with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
5535     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
5536     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however. Contrast with
5537     * {@link #mixedRandomSeparated(double, int)}, which tends to overlap more frequently. This method seems to work
5538     * well because it chooses quasi-random points by their index in the Z-Order Curve as opposed to the simpler
5539     * approach mixedRandomSeparated uses to traverse points (which just runs through the "on" cells a column at a time,
5540     * not caring if two points are in adjacent cells as long as they are in different columns). Testing with a dungeon
5541     * layout of mostly-on cells, this method has no overlap with a fraction of 0.4, while mixedRandomSeparated has
5542     * overlap as early as 0.15 for fraction, and it only gets worse at higher values. A change to the algorithm used by
5543     * {@link #quasiRandomSeparated(double, int)} has it overlapping at the same rate as this method, though it should
5544     * be much faster. This method can be especially slow, since each Z-Order traversal may need to try many cells that
5545     * are outside the GreasedRegion but are on the Z-Order Curve.
5546     * Restricts the total size of the returned array to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on").
5547     * If limit is negative, this will not restrict the size.
5548     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
5549     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return
5550     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the quasi-random cells
5551     */
5552    public Coord[] separatedZCurve(double fraction, int limit)
5553    {
5554        if(fraction < 0)
5555            return new Coord[0];
5556        if(fraction > 1)
5557            fraction = 1;
5558        int ct = size(), total;
5559        total = ct;
5560        ct *= fraction;
5561        if(limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
5562            ct = limit;
5563        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct];
5564        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
5565        {
5566            vl[i] = nthZCurve((int) (VanDerCorputQRNG.determine2(i ^ i >>> 1) * total));
5567        }
5568        return vl;
5569    }
5570    /**
5571     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a quasi-random subset of its previous contents, choosing cells so that
5572     * the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
5573     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
5574     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however. Contrast with
5575     * {@link #mixedRandomRegion(double)}, which tends to overlap more frequently. This method seems to work
5576     * well because it chooses quasi-random points by their index in the Z-Order Curve as opposed to the simpler
5577     * approach mixedRandomRegion uses to traverse points (which just runs through the "on" cells a column at a time,
5578     * not caring if two points are in adjacent cells as long as they are in different columns). Testing with a dungeon
5579     * layout of mostly-on cells, this method has no overlap with a fraction of 0.4, while mixedRandomRegion has
5580     * overlap as early as 0.15 for fraction, and it only gets worse at higher values. A change to the algorithm used by
5581     * {@link #quasiRandomRegion(double)} has it overlapping at the same rate as this method, though it should be much
5582     * faster. This method can be especially slow, since each Z-Order traversal may need to try many cells that are
5583     * outside the GreasedRegion but are on the Z-Order Curve.
5584     * Does not restrict the size of the returned array other than only using up to {@code fraction * size()} cells.
5585     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
5586     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
5587     */
5588    public GreasedRegion separatedRegionZCurve(double fraction)
5589    {
5590        return separatedRegionZCurve(fraction, -1);
5591    }

5593    /**
5594     * Modifies this GreasedRegion so it contains a quasi-random subset of its previous contents, choosing cells so that
5595     * the {@link #size()} matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells in this. This is quasi-
5596     * random instead of pseudo-random because it is somewhat less likely to produce nearby cells in the result. If you
5597     * request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, however. Contrast with
5598     * {@link #mixedRandomRegion(double, int)}, which tends to overlap more frequently. This method seems to work
5599     * well because it chooses quasi-random points by their index in the Z-Order Curve as opposed to the simpler
5600     * approach mixedRandomRegion uses to traverse points (which just runs through the "on" cells a column at a time,
5601     * not caring if two points are in adjacent cells as long as they are in different columns). Testing with a dungeon
5602     * layout of mostly-on cells, this method has no overlap with a fraction of 0.4, while mixedRandomRegion has
5603     * overlap as early as 0.15 for fraction, and it only gets worse at higher values. A change to the algorithm used by
5604     * {@link #quasiRandomRegion(double, int)} has it overlapping at the same rate as this method, though it should be
5605     * much faster. This method can be especially slow, since each Z-Order traversal may need to try many cells that
5606     * are outside the GreasedRegion but are on the Z-Order Curve.
5607     * Restricts the total size of the returned array to a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on").
5608     * If limit is negative, this will not restrict the size.
5609     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
5610     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return
5611     * @return this, after modifications, for chaining
5612     */
5613    public GreasedRegion separatedRegionZCurve(double fraction, int limit)
5614    {
5615        if(fraction <= 0)
5616            return empty();
5617        if(fraction >= 1)
5618            return this;
5619        int ct = size(), total;
5620        if(limit >= ct)
5621            return this;
5622        total = ct;
5623        ct *= fraction;
5624        if(limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
5625            ct = limit;
5626        int[] vl = new int[ct];
5627        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
5628        {
5629            vl[i] = nthZCurveTight((int) (VanDerCorputQRNG.determine2(i ^ i >>> 1) * total));
5630        }
5631        return empty().insertSeveral(vl);
5632    }
5633
5634
5635    public Coord[] randomPortion(IRNG rng, int size)
5636    {
5637        int ct = size(), idx = 0, run = 0;
5638        if(ct <= 0 || size <= 0)
5639            return new Coord[0];
5640        if(ct <= size)
5641            return asCoords();
5642        Coord[] points = new Coord[size];
5643        int[] order = rng.randomOrdering(ct);
5644        Arrays.sort(order, 0, size);
5645        long t, w;
5646        ALL:
5647        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5648            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5649                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5650                {
5651                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5652                    while (w != 0) {
5653                        if (run++ == order[idx]) {
5654                            points[idx++] = Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5655                            if (idx >= size) break ALL;
5656                        }
5657                        t ^= w;
5658                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5659                    }
5660                }
5661            }
5662        }
5663        return points;
5664    }
5665
5666    public GreasedRegion randomRegion(IRNG rng, int size)
5667    {
5668        int ct = size(), idx = 0, run = 0;
5669        if(ct <= 0 || size <= 0)
5670            return empty();
5671        if(ct <= size)
5672            return this;
5673        int[] order = rng.randomOrdering(ct);
5674        Arrays.sort(order, 0, size);
5675        long t, w;
5676        ALL:
5677        for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
5678            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
5679                if((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0)
5680                {
5681                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5682                    while (w != 0) {
5683                        if (run++ == order[idx]) {
5684                            if(++idx >= size) break ALL;
5685                        }
5686                        else
5687                        {
5688                            data[x * ySections + s] &= ~(1L << Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
5689                        }
5690                        t ^= w;
5691                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
5692                    }
5693                }
5694            }
5695        }
5696        return this;
5697    }
5698
5699    @Override
5700    public boolean contains(int x, int y)
5701    {
5702        return x >= 0 && y >= 0 && x < width && y < height && ySections > 0 &&
5703                ((data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0);
5704    }

5707    /**
5708     * @return Whether this zone is empty.
5709     */
5710    @Override
5711    public boolean isEmpty() {
5712        if(tallied) return ct > 0;
5713        for (int i = 0; i < data.length; i++) {
5714            if(data[i] != 0L) return false;
5715        }
5716        return true;
5717    }

5719    /**
5720     * Generates a 2D int array from an array or vararg of GreasedRegions, starting at all 0 and adding 1 to the int at
5721     * a position once for every GreasedRegion that has that cell as "on." This means if you give 8 GreasedRegions to
5722     * this method, it can produce any number between 0 and 8 in a cell; if you give 16 GreasedRegions, then it can
5723     * produce any number between 0 and 16 in a cell.
5724     * @param regions an array or vararg of GreasedRegions; must all have the same width and height
5725     * @return a 2D int array with the same width and height as the regions, where an int cell equals the number of given GreasedRegions that had an "on" cell at that position
5726     */
5727    public static int[][] sum(GreasedRegion... regions)
5728    {
5729        if(regions == null || regions.length <= 0)
5730            return new int[0][0];
5731        int w = regions[0].width, h = regions[0].height, l = regions.length, ys = regions[0].ySections;
5732        int[][] numbers = new int[w][h];
5733        for (int x = 0; x < w; x++) {
5734            for (int y = 0; y < h; y++) {
5735                for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5736                    numbers[x][y] += (regions[i].data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1 : 0;
5737                }
5738            }
5739        }
5740        return numbers;
5741    }

5746     * this method, it can produce any number between 0 and 8 in a cell; if you give 16 GreasedRegions, then it can

5750     */
5751    public static int[][] sum(List<GreasedRegion> regions)

5754            return new int[0][0];

5756        int w = t.width, h = t.height, l = regions.size(), ys = t.ySections;
5757        int[][] numbers = new int[w][h];
5758        for (int x = 0; x < w; x++) {
5759            for (int y = 0; y < h; y++) {
5760                for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5761                    numbers[x][y] += (regions.get(i).data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1 : 0;
5762                }
5763            }
5764        }
5765        return numbers;
5766    }

5817    /**
5818     * Generates a 2D int array from an array of GreasedRegions and an array of weights, starting the 2D result at all 0
5819     * and, for every GreasedRegion that has that cell as "on," adding the int in the corresponding weights array at
5820     * the position of that cell. This means if you give an array of 4 GreasedRegions to this method along with the
5821     * weights {@code 1, 2, 3, 4}, it can produce a number between 0 and 10 in a cell (where 10 is used when all 4
5822     * GreasedRegions have a cell "on," since {@code 1 + 2 + 3 + 4 == 10}); if the weights are instead
5823     * {@code 1, 10, 100, 1000}, then the results can vary between 0 and 1111, where 1111 is only if all GreasedRegions
5824     * have a cell as "on." The weights array must have a length at least equal to the length of the regions array.
5825     * @param regions an array of GreasedRegions; must all have the same width and height
5826     * @param weights an array of ints; must have length at least equal to regions' length
5827     * @return a 2D int array with the same width and height as the regions, where an int cell equals the sum of the weights corresponding to GreasedRegions that had an "on" cell at that position
5828     */
5829    public static int[][] sumWeighted(GreasedRegion[] regions, int[] weights)
5830    {
5831        if(regions == null || regions.length <= 0 || weights == null || weights.length < regions.length)
5832            return new int[0][0];
5833        int w = regions[0].width, h = regions[0].height, l = regions.length, ys = regions[0].ySections;
5834        int[][] numbers = new int[w][h];
5835        for (int x = 0; x < w; x++) {
5836            for (int y = 0; y < h; y++) {
5837                for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5838                    numbers[x][y] += (regions[i].data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? weights[i] : 0;
5839                }
5840            }
5841        }
5842        return numbers;
5843    }

5846     * Generates a 2D double array from an array of GreasedRegions and an array of weights, starting the 2D result at
5847     * all 0 and, for every GreasedRegion that has that cell as "on," adding the double in the corresponding weights
5848     * array at the position of that cell. This means if you give an array of 4 GreasedRegions to this method along with
5849     * the weights {@code 1, 2, 3, 4}, it can produce a number between 0 and 10 in a cell (where 10 is used when all 4
5850     * GreasedRegions have a cell "on," since {@code 1 + 2 + 3 + 4 == 10}); if the weights are instead
5851     * {@code 1, 10, 100, 1000}, then the results can vary between 0 and 1111, where 1111 is only if all GreasedRegions
5852     * have a cell as "on." The weights array must have a length at least equal to the length of the regions array.
5853     * @param regions an array of GreasedRegions; must all have the same width and height
5854     * @param weights an array of doubles; must have length at least equal to regions' length
5855     * @return a 2D double array with the same width and height as the regions, where an double cell equals the sum of the weights corresponding to GreasedRegions that had an "on" cell at that position
5856     */
5857    public static double[][] sumWeightedDouble(GreasedRegion[] regions, double[] weights)
5858    {
5859        if(regions == null || regions.length <= 0 || weights == null || weights.length < regions.length)
5860            return new double[0][0];
5861        int w = regions[0].width, h = regions[0].height, l = regions.length, ys = regions[0].ySections;
5862        double[][] numbers = new double[w][h];
5863        for (int x = 0; x < w; x++) {
5864            for (int y = 0; y < h; y++) {
5865                for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5866                    numbers[x][y] += (regions[i].data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? weights[i] : 0.0;
5867                }
5868            }
5869        }
5870        return numbers;
5871    }

5873    /**
5874     * Adds to an existing 2D int array with an array or vararg of GreasedRegions, adding 1 to the int in existing at
5875     * a position once for every GreasedRegion that has that cell as "on." This means if you give 8 GreasedRegions to
5876     * this method, it can increment by any number between 0 and 8 in a cell; if you give 16 GreasedRegions, then it can
5877     * increase the value in existing by any number between 0 and 16 in a cell.
5878     * @param existing a non-null 2D int array that will have each cell incremented by the sum of the GreasedRegions
5879     * @param regions an array or vararg of GreasedRegions; must all have the same width and height
5880     * @return existing, after modification, where an int cell will be changed by the number of given GreasedRegions that had an "on" cell at that position
5881     */
5882    public static int[][] sumInto(int[][] existing, GreasedRegion... regions)
5883    {
5884        if(regions == null || regions.length <= 0 || existing == null || existing.length == 0 || existing[0].length == 0)
5885            return existing;
5886        int w = existing.length, h = existing[0].length, l = regions.length, ys;
5887        for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5888            GreasedRegion region = regions[i];
5889            ys = region.ySections;
5890            for (int x = 0; x < w && x < region.width; x++) {
5891                for (int y = 0; y < h && y < region.height; y++) {
5892                    existing[x][y] += (region.data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1 : 0;
5893                }
5894            }
5895        }
5896        return existing;
5897    }

5901     * Adds to an existing 2D double array with an array or vararg of GreasedRegions, adding 1 to the double in existing
5902     * at a position once for every GreasedRegion that has that cell as "on." This means if you give 8 GreasedRegions to
5903     * this method, it can increment by any number between 0 and 8 in a cell; if you give 16 GreasedRegions, then it can
5904     * increase the value in existing by any number between 0 and 16 in a cell.
5905     * @param existing a non-null 2D double array that will have each cell incremented by the sum of the GreasedRegions
5906     * @param regions an array or vararg of GreasedRegions; must all have the same width and height
5907     * @return existing, after modification, where a double cell will be changed by the number of given GreasedRegions that had an "on" cell at that position
5908     */
5909    public static double[][] sumIntoDouble(double[][] existing, GreasedRegion... regions)
5910    {
5911        if(regions == null || regions.length <= 0 || existing == null || existing.length == 0 || existing[0].length == 0)
5912            return existing;
5913        int w = existing.length, h = existing[0].length, l = regions.length, ys = regions[0].ySections;
5914        for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5915            for (int x = 0; x < w && x < regions[i].width; x++) {
5916                for (int y = 0; y < h && y < regions[i].height; y++) {
5917                    existing[x][y] += (regions[i].data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1.0 : 0.0;
5918                }
5919            }
5920        }
5921        return existing;
5922    }

5924    /**
5925     * Discouraged from active use; slower than {@link squidpony.squidai.DijkstraMap} and has less features.
5926     * @param map a 2D char array where '#' is a wall
5927     * @param goals an array or vararg of Coord to get the distances toward
5928     * @return a 2D double array of distances from a cell to the nearest goal
5929     */
5930    public static double[][] dijkstraScan(char[][] map, Coord... goals)
5931    {
5932        if(map == null || map.length <= 0 || map[0].length <= 0 || goals == null || goals.length <= 0)
5933            return new double[0][0];
5934        int w = map.length, h = map[0].length, ys = (h + 63) >>> 6;
5935        double[][] numbers = new double[w][h];
5936        GreasedRegion walls = new GreasedRegion(map, '#'), floors = new GreasedRegion(walls).not(),
5937                middle = new GreasedRegion(w, h, goals).and(floors);
5938        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> regions = middle.floodSeriesToLimit(floors);
5939        int l = regions.size();
5940        for (int x = 0; x < w; x++) {
5941            for (int y = 0; y < h; y++) {
5942                for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5943                    numbers[x][y] += (regions.get(i).data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1 : 0;
5944                }
5945            }
5946        }
5947        return numbers;
5948    }

5962                middle = new GreasedRegion(w, h, goals).and(floors);
5963        ArrayList<GreasedRegion> regions = middle.floodSeriesToLimit8way(floors);

5975    /**
5976     * Generates a 2D int array from an array or vararg of GreasedRegions, treating each cell in the nth region as the
5977     * nth bit of the int at the corresponding x,y cell in the int array. This means if you give 8 GreasedRegions to
5978     * this method, it can produce any 8-bit number in a cell (0-255); if you give 16 GreasedRegions, then it can
5979     * produce any 16-bit number (0-65535).
5980     * @param regions an array or vararg of GreasedRegions; must all have the same width and height
5981     * @return a 2D int array with the same width and height as the regions, with bits per int taken from the regions
5982     */
5983    public static int[][] bitSum(GreasedRegion... regions)
5984    {
5985        if(regions == null || regions.length <= 0)
5986            return new int[0][0];
5987        int w = regions[0].width, h = regions[0].height, l = Math.min(32, regions.length), ys = regions[0].ySections;
5988        int[][] numbers = new int[w][h];
5989        for (int x = 0; x < w; x++) {
5990            for (int y = 0; y < h; y++) {
5991                for (int i = 0; i < l; i++) {
5992                    numbers[x][y] |= (regions[i].data[x * ys + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) != 0 ? 1 << i : 0;
5993                }
5994            }
5995        }
5996        return numbers;
5997    }

6014    @Override
6015    public boolean equals(Object o) {
6016        if (this == o) return true;
6017        if (o == null || getClass() != o.getClass()) return false;
6018
6019        GreasedRegion that = (GreasedRegion) o;
6020
6021        if (height != that.height) return false;
6022        if (width != that.width) return false;
6023        if (ySections != that.ySections) return false;
6024        if (yEndMask != that.yEndMask) return false;
6025        return Arrays.equals(data, that.data);
6026    }

6056    public long hash64() {
6057        long result = 0x9E3779B97F4A7C94L, a = 0x632BE59BD9B4E019L;
6058        final int len = data.length;
6059        for (int i = 0; i < len; i++) {
6060            result += (a ^= 0x8329C6EB9E6AD3E3L * data[i]);
6061        }
6062        result += (a ^= 0x8329C6EB9E6AD3E3L * height);
6063        result += (a ^= 0x8329C6EB9E6AD3E3L * width);
6064        return (result * (a | 1L) ^ (result >>> 27 | result << 37));
6065    }
6066
6067    public String serializeToString()
6068    {
6069        return width +
6070                "," + height +
6071                "," + StringKit.joinAlt(",",data);
6072    }
6073    public static GreasedRegion deserializeFromString(String s)
6074    {
6075        if(s == null || s.isEmpty())
6076            return null;
6077        int gap = s.indexOf(','), w = Integer.parseInt(s.substring(0, gap)),
6078                gap2 = s.indexOf(',', gap+1), h = Integer.parseInt(s.substring(gap+1, gap2));
6079        String[] splits = StringKit.split(s.substring(gap2+1), ",");
6080        long[] data = new long[splits.length];
6081        for (int i = 0; i < splits.length; i++) {
6082            data[i] = StringKit.longFromDec(splits[i]);
6083        }
6084        return new GreasedRegion(data, w, h);
6085    }

6087    /**
6088     * Constructs a GreasedRegion using a vararg for data. Primarily meant for generated code, since
6089     * {@link #serializeToString()} produces a String that happens to be a valid parameter list for this method.
6090     * @param width width of the GreasedRegion to produce
6091     * @param height height of the GreasedRegion to produce
6092     * @param data array or vararg of long containing the exact data, probably from an existing GreasedRegion
6093     * @return a new GreasedRegion with the given width, height, and data
6094     */
6095    public static GreasedRegion of(final int width, final int height, final long... data)
6096    {
6097        return new GreasedRegion(data, width, height);
6098    }
6099
6100    public String toCompressedString()
6101    {
6102        if(height > 0x4000)
6103            throw new UnsupportedOperationException("Height is too large to compress, aborting.");
6104        StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(width * height >> 2);
6105        boolean on = false;
6106        int span = 0;
6107        char adjust = (char) nextPowerOfTwo(Math.max(height, 32));
6108        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6109            for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
6110                if(((data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] & (1L << (y & 63))) == 0) == on)
6111                    span++;
6112                else
6113                {
6114                    on = !on;
6115                    sb.append((char)(adjust | span));
6116                    span = 1;
6117                }
6118            }
6119            if(on)
6120            {
6121                sb.append((char)(adjust | span));
6122            }
6123            sb.append('\n');
6124            on = false;
6125            span = 0;
6126        }
6127        return sb.toString();
6128    }

6212    @Override
6213    public boolean retainAll(Collection<?> c) {
6214        GreasedRegion g2 = new GreasedRegion(width, height);
6215        for(Object o : c)
6216        {
6217            if(contains(o) && o instanceof Coord)
6218            {
6219                g2.add((Coord)o);
6220            }
6221        }
6222        boolean changed = equals(g2);
6223        remake(g2);
6224        return changed;
6225    }
6226
6227    /**
6228     * Randomly removes points from a GreasedRegion, with larger values for preservation keeping more of the existing
6229     * shape intact. If preservation is 1, roughly 1/2 of all points will be removed; if 2, roughly 1/4, if 3, roughly
6230     * 1/8, and so on, so that preservation can be thought of as a negative exponent of 2.
6231     * @param rng used to determine random factors
6232     * @param preservation roughly what degree of points to remove (higher keeps more); removes about {@code 1/(2^preservation)} points
6233     * @return a randomly modified change to this GreasedRegion
6234     */
6235    public GreasedRegion deteriorate(RandomnessSource rng, int preservation) {
6236        if(rng == null || width <= 2 || ySections <= 0 || preservation <= 0)
6237            return this;
6238        long mash;
6239        for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
6240            mash = rng.nextLong();
6241            for (int j = i; j < preservation; j++) {
6242                mash |= rng.nextLong();
6243            }
6244            data[i] &= mash;
6245        }
6246        tallied = false;
6247        return this;
6248    }
6249
6250    /**
6251     * Randomly removes points from a GreasedRegion, with preservation as a fraction between 1.0 (keep all) and 0.0
6252     * (remove all). If preservation is 0.5, roughly 1/2 of all points will be removed; if 0.25, roughly 3/4 will be
6253     * removed (roughly 0.25 will be _kept_), if 0.8, roughly 1/5 will be removed (and about 0.8 will be kept), and so
6254     * on. Preservation must be between 0.0 and 1.0 for this to have the intended behavior; 1.0 or higher will keep all
6255     * points without change (returning this GreasedRegion), while anything less than 0.015625 (1.0/64) will empty this
6256     * GreasedRegion (using {@link #empty()}) and then return it. The parameter {@code random} can be an object like a
6257     * {@link LinnormRNG}, an {@link RNG} backed by a well-distributed RandomnessSource like its default, LinnormRNG, a
6258     * {@link GWTRNG} (especially if you target GWT, where it will perform much better than most alternatives), or any
6259     * of various other RandomnessSource implementations that distribute bits well for
6260     * {@link RandomnessSource#nextLong()}, but should not be intentionally-biased RNGs like {@link DharmaRNG} or 
6261     * {@link EditRNG}, nor double-based QRNGs like {@link VanDerCorputQRNG} or {@link SobolQRNG}.
6262     * @param random used to determine random factors; likely to be an {@link RNG}, {@link LinnormRNG}, or {@link GWTRNG}
6263     * @param preservation the rough fraction of points to keep, between 0.0 and 1.0
6264     * @return a randomly modified change to this GreasedRegion
6265     */
6266    public GreasedRegion deteriorate(final RandomnessSource random, final double preservation) {
6267        if(random == null || width <= 2 || ySections <= 0 || preservation >= 1)
6268            return this;
6269        if(preservation <= 0)
6270            return empty();
6271        int bitCount = (int) (preservation * 64);
6272        for (int i = 0; i < width * ySections; i++) {
6273            data[i] &= approximateBits(random, bitCount);
6274        }
6275        tallied = false;
6276        return this;
6277    }
6278
6279    /**
6280     * Inverts the on/off state of the cell with the given x and y.
6281     * @param x the x position of the cell to flip
6282     * @param y the y position of the cell to flip
6283     * @return this for chaining, modified
6284     */
6285    public GreasedRegion flip(int x, int y) {
6286        if(x >= 0 && y >= 0 && x < width && y < height && ySections > 0)
6287        {
6288            data[x * ySections + (y >> 6)] ^= (1L << (y & 63));
6289            tallied = false;
6290        }
6291        return this;
6292
6293    }
6294
6295    /**
6296     * Returns a new GreasedRegion that has been mirrored along the rightmost edge, parallel to the y-axis. The new
6297     * GreasedRegion will have exactly twice the width, the additional width will have the contents of the original
6298     * GreasesRegion in reversed order. The positions shared by both GreasedRegions will be the same, that is, any area
6299     * not added to the original will be equal to the original.
6300     * @return a new GreasedRegion with twice the width of {@code this}, that is mirrored along the rightmost edge
6301     */
6302    public GreasedRegion mirrorY()
6303    {
6304        GreasedRegion next = new GreasedRegion(data, width, height, width * 2, height);
6305        for (int i = 0, o = width * 2 - 1; i < width; i++, o--) {
6306            System.arraycopy(data, ySections * i, next.data, ySections * o, ySections);
6307        }
6308        return next;
6309    }
6310
6311    @Override
6312    public boolean intersectsWith(Zone other) {
6313        if (other instanceof GreasedRegion)
6314            return intersects((GreasedRegion) other);
6315        long t, w;
6316        for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6317            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6318                if ((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0) {
6319                    w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6320                    while (w != 0) {
6321                        if (other.contains(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w)))
6322                            return true;
6323                        t ^= w;
6324                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6325                    }
6326                }
6327            }
6328        }
6329        return false;
6330    }
6331    /**
6332     * Translates a copy of {@code this} by the x,y values in {@code c}.
6333     * Implemented with {@code return copy().translate(c.x, c.y);}
6334     * @return {@code this} copied and shifted by {@code (c.x,c.y)}
6335     */
6336    @Override
6337    public GreasedRegion translate(Coord c) {
6338        return copy().translate(c.x, c.y);
6339    }
6340    /**
6341     * Gets a Collection of Coord values that are not in this GreasedRegion, but are
6342     * adjacent to it, either orthogonally or diagonally. Related to the fringe()
6343     * methods in CoordPacker and GreasedRegion, but guaranteed to use 8-way
6344     * adjacency and to return a new Collection of Coord. This implementation returns
6345     * a GreasedRegion produced simply by {@code return copy().fringe8way();} .
6346     * @return Cells adjacent to {@code this} (orthogonally or diagonally) that
6347     * aren't in {@code this}
6348     */
6349    @Override
6350    public GreasedRegion getExternalBorder() {
6351        return copy().fringe8way();
6352    }

6354    /**
6355     * Gets a new Zone that contains all the Coords in {@code this} plus all
6356     * neighboring Coords, which can be orthogonally or diagonally adjacent
6357     * to any Coord this has in it. Related to the expand() methods in
6358     * CoordPacker and GreasedRegion, but guaranteed to use 8-way adjacency
6359     * and to return a new Zone. This implementation returns a GreasedRegion
6360     * produced simply by {@code return copy().expand8way();} .
6361     * @return A new GreasedRegion where "off" cells adjacent to {@code this}
6362     *         (orthogonally or diagonally) have been added to the "on" cells
6363     *         in {@code this}
6364     */
6365    @Override
6366    public GreasedRegion extend() {
6367        return copy().expand8way();
6368    }

6370    /**
6371     * Checks if {@code c} is present in this GreasedRegion. Returns true if and only if c is present in this
6372     * GreasedRegion as an "on" cell. This will never be true if c is null, has negative x or y, has a value for x that
6373     * is equal to or greater than {@link #width}, or has a value for y that is equal to or greater than
6374     * {@link #height}, but none of those conditions will cause Exceptions to be thrown.
6375     * @param c a Coord to try to find in this GreasedRegion; if null this will always return false
6376     * @return true if {@code c} is an "on" cell in this GreasedRegion, or false otherwise, including if c is null
6377     */
6378    @Override
6379    public boolean contains(Coord c) {
6380        return c != null && contains(c.x, c.y);
6381    }
6382
6383    /**
6384     * Checks whether all Coords in {@code other} are also present in {@code this}.
6385     * Requires that {@code other} won't give a null Coord while this method iterates over it.
6386     * @param other another Zone, such as a GreasedRegion or a {@link squidpony.squidgrid.zone.CoordPackerZone}
6387     * @return true if all Coords in other are "on" in this GreasedRegion, or false otherwise
6388     */
6389    @Override
6390    public boolean contains(Zone other) {
6391        if(other instanceof Collection)
6392            return containsAll((Collection) other);
6393        for(Coord c : other)
6394        {
6395            if(!contains(c.x, c.y))
6396                return false;
6397        }
6398        return true;
6399    }
6400
6401    /**
6402     * @param smallestOrBiggest if true, finds the smallest x-coordinate value;
6403     *                          if false, finds the biggest.
6404     * @return The x-coordinate of the Coord within {@code this} that has the
6405     * smallest (or biggest) x-coordinate. Or -1 if the zone is empty.
6406     */
6407    @Override
6408    public int x(boolean smallestOrBiggest) {
6409        if(smallestOrBiggest)
6410            return first().x;
6411        else
6412            return nth(size()-1).x;
6413    }
6414
6415    /**
6416     * @param smallestOrBiggest if true, finds the smallest y-coordinate value;
6417     *                          if false, finds the biggest.
6418     * @return The y-coordinate of the Coord within {@code this} that has the
6419     * smallest (or biggest) y-coordinate. Or -1 if the zone is empty.
6420     */
6421    @Override
6422    public int y(boolean smallestOrBiggest) {
6423        long t, w;
6424        if(smallestOrBiggest) {
6425            int best = Integer.MAX_VALUE;
6426            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6427                for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6428                    if ((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0) {
6429                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6430                        while (w != 0) {
6431                            best = Math.min(s << 6 | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w), best);
6432                            if(best == 0)
6433                                return 0;
6434                            t ^= w;
6435                            w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6436                        }
6437                    }
6438                }
6439            }
6440            return best == Integer.MAX_VALUE ? -1 : best;
6441        }
6442        else
6443        {
6444            int best = -1;
6445            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6446                for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6447                    if ((t = data[x * ySections + s]) != 0) {
6448                        w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6449                        while (w != 0) {
6450                            best = Math.max(s << 6 | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w), best);
6451                            if(best == height - 1)
6452                                return best;
6453                            t ^= w;
6454                            w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(t);
6455                        }
6456                    }
6457                }
6458            }
6459            return best;
6460        }
6461    }
6462
6463    /**
6464     * Gets the distance between the minimum x-value contained in this GreasedRegion and the maximum x-value in it.
6465     * Not the same as accessing the field {@link #width} on a GreasedRegion! The field will get the span of the space
6466     * that the GreasedRegion can use, including "on" and "off" cells. This method will only get the distance between
6467     * the furthest-separated "on" cells on the x-axis, and won't consider "off" cells. This method can return -1 if the
6468     * GreasedRegion is empty, 0 if the "on" cells are all in a vertical line (that is, when the minimum x is equal to
6469     * the maximum x), or a positive int in other cases with multiple x-values.
6470     * @return the distance on the x-axis between the "on" cell with the lowest x-value and the one with the highest
6471     */
6472    @Override
6473    public int getWidth() {
6474        if (super.width == -2)
6475            super.width = isEmpty() ? -1 : x(false) - x(true);
6476        return super.width;
6477    }
6478    /**
6479     * Gets the distance between the minimum y-value contained in this GreasedRegion and the maximum y-value in it.
6480     * Not the same as accessing the field {@link #height} on a GreasedRegion! The field will get the span of the space
6481     * that the GreasedRegion can use, including "on" and "off" cells. This method will only get the distance between
6482     * the furthest-separated "on" cells on the y-axis, and won't consider "off" cells. This method can return -1 if the
6483     * GreasedRegion is empty, 0 if the "on" cells are all in a horizontal line (that is, when the minimum y is equal to
6484     * the maximum y), or a positive int in other cases with multiple y-values.
6485     * @return the distance on the y-axis between the "on" cell with the lowest y-value and the one with the highest
6486     */
6487    @Override
6488    public int getHeight() {
6489        if (super.height == -2)
6490            super.height = isEmpty() ? -1 : y(false) - y(true);
6491        return super.height;
6492    }
6493
6494    /**
6495     * Gets the diagonal distance from the point combining the lowest x-value present in this GreasedRegion with the
6496     * lowest y-value in this, to the point combining the highest x-value and the highest y-value. These minimum and
6497     * maximum values don't necessarily match a single "on" cell for each min and max corner, and can take their x and y
6498     * values from two different points. The diagonal distance uses Euclidean measurement (basic Pythagorean Theorem
6499     * math here), and will be a double.
6500     * @return the diagonal distance from (min x, min y) to (max x, max y), as a double
6501     */
6502    @Override
6503    public double getDiagonal() {
6504        final int w = getWidth();
6505        final int h = getHeight();
6506        return Math.sqrt((w * w) + (h * h));
6507    }

6514    @Override
6515    public GreasedRegion getInternalBorder() {
6516        return copy().surface8way();
6517    }
6518
6519    /**
6520     * Gets a Coord array from the "on" contents of this GreasedRegion, using a deterministic but random-seeming
6521     * scattering of chosen cells with a count that matches the given {@code fraction} of the total amount of "on" cells
6522     * in this. This is pseudo-random with the given seed (which will be made into an odd number if it is not one
6523     * already), and is very good at avoiding overlap (just as good as {@link #separatedZCurve(double, int)}, and
6524     * much faster). If you request too many cells (too high of a value for fraction), it will start to overlap, but
6525     * a fraction value of 0.4 reliably has had no overlap in testing. Restricts the total size of the returned array to
6526     * a maximum of {@code limit} (minimum is 0 if no cells are "on"). If limit is negative, this will not restrict the
6527     * size.
6528     * @param fraction the fraction of "on" cells to randomly select, between 0.0 and 1.0
6529     * @param limit the maximum size of the array to return
6530     * @param seed a long seed to change the points; the most significant 21 bits (except the sign bit) and least significant bit are ignored
6531     * @return a freshly-allocated Coord array containing the pseudo-random cells
6532     */
6533    public Coord[] mixedRandomSeparatedAlt(double fraction, int limit, long seed)
6534    {
6535        if(fraction < 0)
6536            return new Coord[0];
6537        if(fraction > 1)
6538            fraction = 1;
6539        int tmp, ic;
6540        long t, w;
6541        seed |= 1L;
6542        final int total = size();
6543        int ct = (int)(total * fraction);
6544        if(limit >= 0 && limit < ct)
6545            ct = limit;
6546        Coord[] vl = new Coord[ct];
6547        EACH_QUASI:
6548        for (int i = 0; i < ct; i++)
6549        {
6550            tmp = (int)(VanDerCorputQRNG.altDetermine(seed, i+1) * total);
6551
6552            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6553                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6554                    if ((ic = counts[x * ySections + s]) > tmp) {
6555                        t = data[x * ySections + s];
6556                        for (--ic; t != 0; ic--) {
6557                            w = t & -t;
6558                            if (ic == tmp)
6559                            {
6560                                vl[i] = Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.bitCount(w-1));
6561                                continue EACH_QUASI;
6562                            }
6563                            t ^= w;
6564                        }
6565                    }
6566                }
6567            }
6568        }
6569        return vl;
6570    }
6571
6572
6573    public class GRIterator implements Iterator<Coord>
6574    {
6575        public int index = 0;
6576        private long t, w;
6577        public GRIterator()
6578        {
6579            if(!tallied)
6580                tally();
6581        }
6582        @Override
6583        public boolean hasNext() {
6584            return index < ct;
6585        }
6586
6587        @Override
6588        public Coord next() {
6589            int c;
6590            if(index >= ct)
6591                return null;
6592            for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6593                for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6594                    if ((c = counts[x * ySections + s]) > index) {
6595                        t = data[x * ySections + s];
6596                        for (--c; t != 0; c--) {
6597                            w = t & -t;
6598                            if (c == index)
6599                            {
6600                                index++;
6601                                return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.bitCount(w-1));
6602                            }
6603                            t ^= w;
6604                        }
6605                    }
6606                }
6607            }
6608            return null;
6609
6610            /*
6611            for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
6612                for (int s = 0; s < ySections; s++) {
6613                    if ((w = NumberTools.lowestOneBit(data[x * ySections + s])) != 0 && i++ >= index) {
6614                        if(index++ < limit)
6615                            return Coord.get(x, (s << 6) | Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(w));
6616                        else
6617                            return null;
6618                    }
6619                }
6620            }
6621            */
6622        }
6623
6624        @Override
6625        public void remove() {
6626            throw new UnsupportedOperationException("remove() is not supported on this Iterator.");
6627        }
6628    }
6629}
